Tathwib in Fajr Adhan: Timing and Proofs
Ruling on wording for Fajr adhan and comparison with iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct timing of saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the Fajr adhan (after 'حي على الفلاح'), cite the hadith evidence, and explain why the phrase is exclusive to Fajr.

Core Idea
Tathwib is only for Fajr, said inside the adhan after 'حي على الفلاح'.

The phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is a distinctive part of the Fajr adhan. Some scholars thought it should be said after the adhan ends, but the authentic Hanafi position places it within the adhan itself. This lesson walks through the evidence from the Prophet's command to Bilal and the hadith restricting tathwib to Fajr, and clarifies the difference between adhan and iqamah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the Fajr adhan. The ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah). Note that it is part of the adhan, not a separate statement after it.
This is a sunnah act within the adhan; omitting it does not invalidate the adhan but reduces its completeness.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'لا تثويب في شيء من الصلاة إلا في الفجر' narrated by al-Tirmidhi. The Prophet said this to Bilal, explaining that tathwib (this phrase) is only for Fajr.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'لا تثويب في شيء من الصلاة إلا في الفجر' uses a negative (لا) followed by an exception (إلا). This indicates exclusivity: tathwib is prohibited in all prayers except Fajr. Therefore, the phrase is only for Fajr.
The word 'تثويب' is interpreted here as saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم'.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Some, including Imam Muhammad in his Muwatta', considered the phrase to be said after the adhan. The author of Umdat al-Ri'ayah refutes this. There is also a cross-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, who holds different views on both the phrase and the similarity with iqamah.
The mufta bihi (operative) position is that it is said inside the adhan after 'حي على الفلاح'.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author prefers the view that the phrase is inside the adhan, based on the action of Bilal and the explicit command of the Prophet. This is supported by the hadith and is the majority Hanafi position.
The tarjih authority is the author's own work 'al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad' where he refutes the alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[4] قوله : بعد فلاح الفجر؛ ذهب بعض المشايخ إلى أن محل الصلاة خير من النوم بعد تمام الأذان، وإليه يميل كلام الإمام محمد في «الموطأ»، وقد رددته عليه في «التعليق الممجد»، وبينت أن الصحيح هو كونه في الأذان بعد حي على الفلاح من أذان الفجر، وهو الثابت من فعل بلال، وبه أمره رسول الله كما أخرجه ابن ماجة والطبراني وغيرهما. الفجر الصلاة خير من النوم مرتين، والإقامة مثله خلافاً للشافعي [1] قوله : الفجر؛ دون غيره من الصلوات؛ لحديث: «لا تثويب في شيء من الصلاة إلا في الفجر» قاله النبي للبلال المؤذن، أخرجه الترمذي، وفسر التثويب بأن يقول بعد الفلاح : الصلاة خير من النوم. [2] قوله : خير من النوم؛ قال في «منح الغفار» تبعاً لصاحب «البحر»: «إنما كان النوم مشاركاً للصلاة في أصل الخيرية؛ لأنه قد يكون عبادة كما إذا كان وسيلة إلى طاعة أو ترك معصية، أو لأن النوم راحة في الدنيا، والصلاة راحة في الآخرة، فتكون الراحة في الآخرة أفضل». [3] قوله : والإقامة مثله، هو في الأصل مصدر، ثم سميت بها الكلمات التي تقال عند إرادة ابتداء الصلاة لإعلام الحاضرين، وليس المراد المثلية في جميع الأحوال، فإن بينهما فرقاً من وجوه ولا في الأحوال التي مر ذكرها في المتن، فإن منها :
[4] His saying: after the success of Fajr; some scholars held that the place of 'prayer is better than sleep' is after the completion of the adhan, and the statement of Imam Muhammad in al-Muwatta' leans towards it, and I replied to it in al-Ta'liq al-Mumajjad, and I showed that the correct view is that it is in the adhan after 'come to success' from the Fajr adhan, and it is established from the action of Bilal, and the Messenger of Allah commanded him with it as narrated by Ibn Majah, al-Tabarani and others. Fajr: 'prayer is better than sleep' twice, and the iqamah is like it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [1] His saying: Fajr; not other prayers, because of the hadith: 'There is no tathwib in any prayer except in Fajr', the Prophet said it to the mu'adhdhin Bilal, narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and he interpreted tathwib as saying after success: prayer is better than sleep. [2] His saying: better than sleep; he said in Manh al-Ghaffar following the author of al-Bahr: 'Sleep shares with prayer in the essence of goodness because it can be an act of worship when it is a means to obedience or abandoning sin, or because sleep is rest in this world and prayer is rest in the hereafter, so rest in the hereafter is better.' [3] His saying: and the iqamah is like it; it is originally a verbal noun, then it came to name the words that are said when intending to begin the prayer to inform those present, and what is meant is not similarity in all conditions, for there are differences between them in many aspects, nor in the conditions that have been mentioned in the text, among which are:
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the specific wording for Fajr adhan. It first addresses the correct timing of the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' (prayer is better than sleep). Some scholars (including the author's earlier opinion) held it should be said after the adhan is complete, but the correct view (as narrated from Bilal and the Prophet) is that it is part of the adhan itself, said immediately after 'حي على الفلاح'. This is supported by a hadith in al-Tirmidhi that 'tathwib' (the act of saying this phrase) is only for Fajr. The commentary then explains that the phrase is exclusive to Fajr, not other prayers, due to a hadith explicitly limiting tathwib to Fajr. A philosophical explanation is given for why sleep is mentioned: sleep can be a form of worship if used for obedience or avoiding sin, or because sleep is rest in this world while prayer is rest in the hereafter, making the latter superior. Finally, the text clarifies that the matn's statement 'والإقامة مثله' (and the iqamah is like it) does not mean identical in all respects; both have differences in wording and conditions, though the base similarity is that both inform of the prayer.

Key Terms
تثويب (tathwib): The act of saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the adhan, specifically for Fajr according to this hadith.
الصلاة خير من النوم (al-salatu khayrun min al-nawm): The phrase 'prayer is better than sleep' added to the Fajr adhan.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The words said immediately before the prayer starts to inform those present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when exactly should 'الصلاة خير من النوم' be said in the Fajr adhan?
A) At the very beginning before the takbir.
B) After 'حي على الفلاح' within the adhan.
C) After completing the entire adhan.
D) During the iqamah instead of the adhan.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is a confirmed sunnah exclusively for Fajr adhan, recited after 'حي على الفلاح' as part of the adhan.

Tathwib in Fajr Adhan and Differences Between Adhan and Iqamah
Inter-madhhab dispute on tathwib and adhan/iqamah differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tathwib in the Fajr adhan, explain the Hadith evidence, and distinguish adhan from iqamah in terms of wording and actions.

Core Idea
Tathwib is a sunnah for Fajr adhan only; iqamah is said singly except for 'قد قامت الصلاة'.

The adhan and iqamah are distinct calls to prayer with specific wording and sunan. In the Hanafi school, the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' (tathwib) is a sunnah in the Fajr adhan only. The iqamah shares some structure with the adhan but differs in repetition, actions, and content. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position, the evidence, and the practical differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
Recognize that the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is the subject of ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is. Note that Hanafis consider it a sunnah of Fajr adhan.
This phrase is called tathwib.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that tathwib is said twice after 'حي على الفلاح' in Fajr adhan. The evidence includes the practice of Bilal and a hadith from al-Tirmidhi.
The prophetic command and practice establish sunnah.
3
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees. While the passage does not detail his proof, the practical difference is clear: in Shafi'i practice, tathwib is not part of the adhan.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the similarities and differences between adhan and iqamah
Compare the two calls: adhan is double (except takbir first four), iqamah is single (except 'قد قامت الصلاة' twice). Also note actions like placing fingers in ears and turning which are not done in iqamah.
The hadith of Anas and Abu Mahdhurah provide the word counts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in Hanafi mosques, tathwib is recited in Fajr adhan; in Shafi'i mosques it is omitted. The iqamah differences affect how the mu'adhdhin pronounces each phrase.
Understanding this helps avoid confusion in mixed communities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفجر الصلاة خير من النوم مرتين، والإقامة مثله خلافاً للشافعي. وبينت أن الصحيح هو كونه في الأذان بعد حي على الفلاح من أذان الفجر، وهو الثابت من فعل بلال، وبه أمره رسول الله كما أخرجه ابن ماجة والطبراني وغيرهما. قوله: الفجر؛ دون غيره من الصلوات؛ لحديث: «لا تثويب في شيء من الصلاة إلا في الفجر» قاله النبي لبلال المؤذن، أخرجه الترمذي، وفسّر التثويب بأن يقول بعد الفلاح: الصلاة خير من النوم. لكن يحدر فيها ويقول بعد فلاحها: قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. فإن عنده الإقامة فرادى إلا قد قامت الصلاة. لكن يحدر فيها، ويقول بعد فلاحها: قد قامت الصلاة مرتين. ١. وضع الأصبعين في الأذنين وليس ذلك في الإقامة على القول المعتمد. ٢. وكذا لا تحويل فيها. ٣. وكذا لا يزاد فيها الصلاة خير من النوم. بل المراد المثلية في الكلمات، وكيفيتها من الترتيب، وكونها مثنى مثنى غير التكبير الأول فإنه أربع مرات. قوله فرادى؛ أي تفرد كل كلمة وتثنى: قد قامت الصلاة؛ لحديث: أنس: أمر بلال أن يشفع الأذان، ويوتر الإقامة، أخرجه الشيخان وغيرهم. ولنا: حديث أبي محذورة: أن النبي علمه الأذان تسع عشرة كلمة، والإقامة سبع عشرة، أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وغيرهما.
The Fajr (prayer): 'Prayer is better than sleep' twice, and the iqamah is like it, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And it is explained that the correct (view) is that it is in the adhan after 'hayya 'ala al-falah' of the Fajr adhan, and it is established from the action of Bilal, and the Messenger of Allah commanded him with it, as narrated by Ibn Majah, al-Tabarani, and others. His statement: 'Fajr'; to the exclusion of other prayers; due to the hadith: 'There is no tathwib in any prayer except in Fajr' said by the Prophet to Bilal the mu'adhdhin, narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and he interpreted tathwib as saying after al-falah: 'Prayer is better than sleep.' But he lowers (his voice) in it and says after its falah: 'The prayer has begun' twice. For indeed, according to him, the iqamah is single except for 'The prayer has begun.' But he lowers in it and says after its falah: 'The prayer has begun' twice. 1. Placing the fingers in the ears, and that is not in the iqamah according to the relied-upon view. 2. Likewise, there is no turning in it. 3. Likewise, 'Prayer is better than sleep' is not added in it. Rather, the similarity is in the words and their manner of order, and that they are two by two except the first takbir, for it is four times. His statement: 'single'; meaning each word is singular and 'The prayer has begun' is repeated; due to the hadith of Anas: 'Bilal was commanded to make the adhan double and the iqamah single', narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim and others. And we have the hadith of Abu Mahdhurah: 'That the Prophet taught him the adhan as nineteen words and the iqamah as seventeen words', narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and others.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the tathwib (saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم') in the Fajr adhan. The Hanafi position, as stated, is that this phrase is said twice in the Fajr adhan after 'حي على الفلاح', based on the practice of Bilal and the Prophet's approval, as recorded in hadith. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed. The text then explains that the iqamah is similar to the adhan in words but differs in some respects: in the iqamah, the words are said singly (فرادى) except for 'قد قامت الصلاة' which is said twice; there is no placing of fingers in ears, no turning, and no addition of 'الصلاة خير من النوم'. The similarity is in the wording and order, with the takbir at the beginning being said four times in both. The evidence for the iqamah being single is the hadith of Anas commanding that the adhan be double and the iqamah single. Another hadith from Abu Mahdhurah counts the adhan as nineteen words and iqamah as seventeen, supporting the Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwīb): The phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' said in the Fajr adhan after 'حي على الفلاح'
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call to prayer, consisting of specified words, said when about to commence prayer
فرادى (furādā): Each word of the iqamah is said one time, not repeated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a difference between adhan and iqamah?
A) The iqamah includes 'الصلاة خير من النوم' twice.
B) In iqamah, the mu'adhdhin places his fingers in his ears.
C) In iqamah, 'قد قامت الصلاة' is said twice while other phrases are said once.
D) The takbir is said four times in adhan but two times in iqamah.

Key Takeaway
Tathwib is a sunnah of Fajr adhan in the Hanafi school; iqamah is single except for 'قد قامت الصلاة'.

Iqama is Odd: Proofs and Differences from Adhan
Explains iqama is odd except one phrase, with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on iqama repetitions, identify the key differences from adhan, and explain the primary evidence from the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
The iqama is recited with odd repetitions except for 'قد قامت الصلاة', explicitly commanded by the Prophet.

In the previous lesson, we learned the rulings of the adhan. Now we turn to the iqama, the second call to prayer. A common point of confusion is whether the iqama mirrors the adhan in repetition. The Hanafi school, drawing on specific prophetic commands, holds that the iqama is recited with odd repetitions (فرادى) with one notable exception. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its evidence, and the practical differences between adhan and iqama.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on iqama repetitions
Identify that the iqama is odd (فرادى) – each phrase is said once – except for 'قد قامت الصلاة', which is said twice. Contrast this with the adhan, where most phrases are repeated twice.
The phrase 'فرادى' comes from the Arabic for 'singular' or 'odd'.
2
Recall the three differences between adhan and iqama
List the three differences mentioned: (1) placing fingers in ears is not done in iqama, (2) there is no turning (to the right and left), and (3) the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is not added, even in Fajr.
These are based on the relied-upon opinion (قول معتمد).
3
Examine the primary proof: the hadith of Anas
The hadith commands: 'أمر بلال أن يشفع الأذان، ويوتر الإقامة' – the Prophet ordered Bilal to make the adhan even (in twos) and the iqama odd. This is the foundational evidence for the Hanafi position.
The word 'يوتِر' (make odd) is the key imperative.
4
Examine the supporting proof: the hadith of Abu Mahdhura
The Prophet taught Abu Mahdhura the adhan as 19 phrases and the iqama as 17 phrases. Counting the phrases shows that 'قد قامت الصلاة' is the only repeated phrase in the iqama, confirming the odd pattern.
Adhan: 4+4+4+4+8=24? Actually the text says 19 phrases for adhan and 17 for iqama. The exact count is a separate analysis.
5
Note the inter-madhhab dispute and Hanafi tarjih
The Shafi'i school holds that iqama is even (in twos) like adhan, based on hadiths of Abdullah ibn Zayd. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Anas is explicit and preferred, and the practice of the Companions supports the odd pattern.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the odd pattern.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لكن يحدر فيها ويقول بعد فلاحها: قد قامت الصلاة مرتين؛ فإن عنده الإقامة فرادى إلا قد قامت الصلاة. ١. وضع الأصبعين في الأذنين وليس ذلك في الإقامة على القول المعتمد. ٢. وكذا لا تحويل فيها. ٣. وكذا لا يزاد فيها الصلاة خير من النوم. بل المراد المثلية في الكلمات، وكيفيتها من الترتيب، وكونها مثنى مثنى غير التكبير الأول فإنه أربع مرات. [قوله فرادى]؛ أي تفرد كل كلمة وتثنى: قد قامت الصلاة؛ لحديث أنس: أمر بلال أن يشفع الأذان، ويوتر الإقامة، أخرجه الشيخان وغيرهم. ولنا: حديث أبي محذورة: أن النبي ﷺ علمه الأذان تسع عشرة كلمة، والإقامة سبع عشرة كلمة، أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي وغيرهما. (١) في صحيح البخاري (١): (٢١٩)، وصحيح مسلم (١): (٢٨٦)، وغيرهما، ومن الأحاديث الدالة على أن الأذان كالإقامة: ١. عن عبد الرحمن بن أبي ليلى قال: حدثنا أصحاب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم أن عبد الله بن زيد لما رأى الأذان أتى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فأخبره، فقال: علمه بلالاً، فقام بلال فأذن مثنى مثنى وأقام مثنى مثنى وقعد قعدة» في صحيح ابن خزيمة (١): (١٩٦)، والآحاد والمثاني (٣: ٤٧٦)، وشرح معاني الآثار (١: ١٣١)، وإسناده صحيح. كما في إعلاء السنن (٢: ٩٩). ٢. عن الشعبي عن عبد الله بن زيد الأنصاري سمعت أذان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فكان أذانه وإقامته مثنى مثنى» في مسند أبي عوانة (١): (٢٧٦)، وغيره، وهو مرسل قوي. كما في إعلاء السنن (٢: ١٠٠-١٠١). (٢) في سنن الترمذي (١: ٣٦٧)، وقال: حسن صحيح، وسنن أبي داود (١: ١٩١)، ولفظه: أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم علمه الأذان تسع عشرة كلمة والإقامة سبع عشرة كلمة. الأذان: الله أكبر الله أكبر الله أكبر الله أكبر، أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله، حي على الصلاة حي على الصلاة، حي على الفلاح حي على الفلاح، الله أكبر الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله. والإقامة: الله أكبر الله أكبر، أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله أشهد أن محمداً رسول الله، حي على الصلاة حي على الصلاة، حي على الفلاح حي على الفلاح، قد قامت الصلاة قد قامت الصلاة، الله أكبر الله أكبر، لا إله إلا الله.
But he lowers his voice in it and says after its completion: 'قد قامت الصلاة' twice, for according to him the iqama is odd (فرادى) except for 'قد قامت الصلاة'. 1. Placing the two fingers in the ears is not in the iqama according to the relied-upon opinion. 2. Likewise, there is no turning (to the right and left) in it. 3. Likewise, 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is not added in it. Rather, what is meant is similarity in the words, and their manner concerning order, and that they are repeated twice (مثنى مثنى) except for the first takbir, for it is four times. [His statement: 'فرادى'] means each word is singular and 'قد قامت الصلاة' is repeated twice; based on the hadith of Anas: 'He commanded Bilal to make the adhan even (in repetitions) and the iqama odd', narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim and others. And we have the hadith of Abu Mahdhura: 'The Prophet ﷺ taught him the adhan as nineteen phrases and the iqama as seventeen phrases', narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i and others. (1) In Sahih al-Bukhari (1): (219), and Sahih Muslim (1): (286), and others, and among the hadiths indicating that the adhan is like the iqama: 1. From Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Layla: 'The companions of Muhammad ﷺ told us that Abdullah ibn Zayd, when he saw the adhan, came to the Prophet ﷺ and informed him, so he said: Teach it to Bilal. Then Bilal stood and gave the adhan in twos and the iqama in twos and sat a sitting.' in Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah (1): (196), and al-Ahad wa al-Mathani (3:476), and Sharh Ma'ani al-Athar (1:131), and its chain is sahih, as in I'la al-Sunan (2:99). 2. From al-Sha'bi from Abdullah ibn Zayd al-Ansari: 'I heard the adhan of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and his adhan and iqama were both in twos.' in Musnad Abi 'Awanah (1): (276), and others, and it is a strong mursal, as in I'la al-Sunan (2:100-101). (2) In Sunan al-Tirmidhi (1:367), and he said: hasan sahih, and Sunan Abi Dawud (1:191), with its wording: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ taught him the adhan as nineteen phrases and the iqama as seventeen phrases. The adhan: Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah, Hayya 'ala al-salah Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah Hayya 'ala al-falah, Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah. And the iqama: Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar, Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah, Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah Ashhadu anna Muhammadan Rasul Allah, Hayya 'ala al-salah Hayya 'ala al-salah, Hayya 'ala al-falah Hayya 'ala al-falah, Qad qamati al-salah Qad qamati al-salah, Allahu Akbar Allahu Akbar, La ilaha illa Allah.'
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage from a Hanafi commentary on al-Wiqayah. The text explains that the iqama is recited in odd numbers (فرادى) except for the phrase 'قد قامت الصلاة', which is said twice, unlike the adhan where most phrases are repeated twice. The author then lists three additional differences: (1) placing fingers in ears is not done in iqama, (2) turning right and left (تحويل) is not done, and (3) the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' is not added in the iqama, even in the Fajr prayer. The similarity (مثلية) between adhan and iqama is in the words and order, and iqama is recited in twos (مثنى مثنى) except the opening takbir which is four times. The proof comes from two hadiths: first, the hadith of Anas that the Prophet commanded Bilal to make the adhan even (شفع) and iqama odd (وتر), narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. Second, the hadith of Abu Mahdhura that the Prophet taught him the adhan as 19 phrases and iqama as 17 phrases, narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. The author then cites additional supporting hadiths affirming that both adhan and iqama can be in twos. The Hanafi position is that iqama is odd except for 'قد قامت الصلاة', relying on the hadith of Anas, while the opposing view (Shafi'i) holds iqama should be in twos like adhan, based on other hadiths. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Anas is explicit and the practice of Bilal is authoritative.

Key Terms
فرادى (furaadaa): Odd, singular; each phrase of the iqama is said once (except 'قد قامت الصلاة' which is twice).
مثنى مثنى (muthanna muthanna): In twos; each phrase is repeated twice, as in the adhan except the first takbir.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, announcing that the prayer is about to commence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which phrase in the iqama is repeated twice?
A) الله أكبر
B) قد قامت الصلاة
C) حي على الفلاح
D) لا إله إلا الله

Key Takeaway
The iqama is odd (فرادى) except for 'قد قامت الصلاة', as per the explicit command of the Prophet to Bilal.

Speaking During Adhan/Iqama and the Dispute on Tathwib
Inter-madhhab dispute on tathwib and ruling on speaking in adhan/iqama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on speaking during adhan/iqama and distinguish the later Hanafi position on tathwib from the earlier Hanafi and other school positions.

Core Idea
Speaking invalidates adhan unless minimal; later Hanafis consider tathwib mustahsan in all prayers.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses two issues: the prohibition of speaking during adhan and iqama, and the practice of tathwib (saying 'الصلاة خير من النوم'). While the ruling on speech is clear—unnecessary talk invalidates the call unless negligible—the tathwib dispute reveals an intra-Hanafi shift from early dislike to later recommendation, as well as inter-madhhab differences. Understanding this helps you navigate both fixed rulings and areas of legitimate flexibility in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and prohibited speech
Recognise that the text forbids any speech during adhan and iqama that is not part of the prescribed phrases, including replies to salam, sneezes, etc.
The exception is very little speech (يسير).
2
Determine the consequence of speaking
If one speaks deliberately or even a few words, the adhan/iqama must be restarted (استأنف). This shows the act is invalidated by speech.
The threshold for 'يسير' is not precisely defined; refer to later Hanafi texts.
3
Define tathwib and its scope
Tathwib means 'notification after notification' and refers to the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم'. The passage states that later scholars considered it mustahsan in all prayers.
Earlier Hanafis (متقدمون) considered it makruh in non-Fajr prayers.
4
Analyse the intra-Hanafi difference
Contrast the early view (makruh in other than Fajr) with the later view (mustahsan in all prayers). Note that this is a shift in fatwa over time.
The later view is the mufta bihi, based on the need to awaken people for all prayers.
5
Map the inter-madhhab dispute
Identify the positions of Shafi'i (tathwib only in Fajr), Maliki (not used), Hanbali (Fajr only), and Hanafi later (all prayers). The text cites hadiths from both sides and concludes the difference is permissible.
The dispute is considered 'ikhtilaf fi mubah' – both practices are acceptable.

And one should not speak during them, and the later scholars considered tathwib (adding 'الصلاة خير من النوم') in all prayers as good. [His statement: 'and one should not speak during them'] means one should not speak during the adhan, nor during the iqama. And the later scholars considered tathwib in all prayers as good (1). In this chapter there are hadiths from both sides which we have detailed with responses from both parties in 'al-Sa'ayah'. The truth is that this difference and similar ones are differences in permissible matters, and all are established and permissible. Among them, some would repeat (tarji') the adhan and make the iqama even, while Bilal used to make the iqama odd and not repeat. So al-Shafi'i took the iqama of Bilal, and the people of Makkah took the adhan of Abu Mahdhura with tarji' and the iqama of Bilal, and Abu Hanifah and the people of Iraq took the adhan of Bilal and the iqama of Abu Mahdhura, and Ahmad and the people of Madinah took the adhan and iqama of Bilal, and Malik differed from them in two matters: the double takbir and the double wording of iqama.' [1] His statement: 'and one should not speak during them' – what is meant by speech here is anything other than the words of adhan and iqama, even if it be a reply to salam, or responding to a sneeze, or praising after a sneeze, or saying salam. If one speaks, he must start over unless it is insignificant. As stated in al-Bahr and al-Khulasah. [2] His statement: 'and the later scholars considered tathwib...' – know that tathwib is notification after notification. (1) Al-Timirtashi said in Manh al-Ghaffar: 'The author of al-Wiqayah indicated by its implication that it is not considered good by the earlier scholars, and it is so. For it is stated in al-Bahr and others that it is disliked (makruh) according to them in other than Fajr, and it is the view of the majority, as al-Nawawi reported in al-Majmu'. And his absolute wording indicates that it is not specific to any person, so the amir and others are equal, and it is the view of Muhammad.' (2) 'al-Sa'ayah' (2:21) and beyond. (3) 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' (1:272). (4) 'Khulasat al-Fatawa' (1:50).

Commentary
This passage contains two main rulings: First, it is prohibited to speak during the adhan and iqama. The commentary clarifies that 'speech' here means any words other than the prescribed phrases of adhan/iqama, including replying to greetings (salam), responding to a sneeze, or praising after sneezing. If one speaks even a few words, the adhan/iqama must be restarted unless the speech is very minimal (يسير). This ruling is sourced from 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' and 'Khulasat al-Fatawa'. Second, the text discusses tathwib, which is adding the phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' in the adhan. The later scholars (متأخرون) considered tathwib recommended (mustahsan) in all prayers, not just Fajr. This is a change from the earlier Hanafi position, which considered it disliked (makruh) in other than Fajr. The author notes that this difference among schools is acceptable and all practices are permissible. He cites 'al-Mawahib al-Ladunniyyah' listing the four mu'adhdhins of the Prophet and the different practices adopted by Imams: Abu Hanifah took Bilal's adhan (without tarji') and Abu Mahdhura's iqama (with tarji'?). The commentary also states that tathwib is 'notification after notification' meaning the repetition of the call. The footnote by al-Timirtashi clarifies that the earlier scholars disliked tathwib except in Fajr, but the later scholars considered it good generally. The authority weight is from later Fatawa (متأخرون).

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwib): The phrase 'الصلاة خير من النوم' (prayer is better than sleep) added to the adhan; literally 'notification after notification'.
المتأخرون (al-muta'akhkhirun): Later Hanafi scholars who issued fatwas in contrast to early scholars (متقدمون).
الكلام (al-kalam): Speech; any words other than the prescribed adhan/iqama phrases, including replies to salam, sneezes, etc.

Ruling of al-Tathwib in the Adhan: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explaining the ruling and opinions on tathwib in adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi opinions on tathwib and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Tathwib evolved from Fajr-specific to recommended in all prayers except Maghrib according to later Hanafi scholars.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of tathwib — the additional call after the adhan, such as 'Al-salah khayrun min al-nawm'. The commentator traces the debate from the early prohibition to the later endorsement, reflecting how fiqh rulings adapt to changing circumstances. By analyzing the three opinions, you will understand how later Hanafi jurists (mutakkhirin) weighed textual evidence against public need.

Guided Path
1
Define tathwib and its origin
Identify what tathwib means historically (the phrase 'Prayer is better than sleep' in Fajr) and how it later expanded to general calls between adhan and iqamah.
Distinguish between the original Prophetic practice and later developments.
2
State the three Hanafi opinions
List the three rulings: 1) makruh except in Fajr; 2) permissible for rulers/judges/muftis; 3) mustahsan for all except Maghrib. Note the proponents of each.
Opinion 1 is early, opinion 2 is Abu Yusuf & Qadi Khan, opinion 3 is the later scholars.
3
Examine the dalil for each opinion
For opinion 1: hadith of Abu Bakrah (special attention to Fajr). For opinion 2: narrations of Bilal calling after the adhan. For opinion 3: practical evidence of laziness; also respond to the condemnation by 'Umar and Ibn 'Umar.
The condemnation was for a specific practice (between adhan and iqamah) not tathwib in general.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
Explain why the later scholars' view (mustahsan for all except Maghrib) is the mufta bihi. Note the authority of Al-'Inayah, Al-Durar, and Al-Nihayah.
The later view adapts to the need to remind people due to prevalent laziness.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: a mu'adhdhin today can commendably add tathwib in all prayers except Maghrib, following the mufta bihi.
Maghrib is excepted due to short interval between adhan and iqamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بنحو: الصلاة خير من النوم، أو حي على الصلاة، أو الصلاة حاضرة أو نحو ذلت بأي لسان كان وقد كان يسمّى في العهد النبوي وعهد أصحابه زيادة : الصلاة خير من النوم في أذان الفجر تثويباً، وهو المراد بقول بلال : «أمرني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن لا أثوب إلا في الفجر»، أخرجه ابن ماجة. وأخرج الطحاوي في «شرح معاني الآثار»: عن ابن عمر وأنس : «كان التثويب في الغداة إذا قال المؤذّن حي على الفلاح قال : الصلاة خير من النوم». وأما التثويب بين الأذان والإقامة فلم يكن في ذلك العهد، بل قد أنكر عليه كما أخرجه ابن أبي شَيْبَةَ : «أنّ أبا محذورة له مؤذن مكة أتى عمره بعد الأذان ، وقال : الصلاة الصلاة، فقال عمر له : ويحك أمجنون أنت، أما كان في دعائك الذي دعوتنا ما نأتيك ، وكذا أنكر التثويب بين الأذان والإقامة ابن عمر ه كما في «سنن أبي داود». واختلف الفقهاء في حكم هذا التثويب على ثلاثة أقوال : الأول : إنّه يكره في جميع الصلوات إلا الفجر ؛ لكونه وقت نوم وغفلة، ويشهد له حديث أبي بكرة له : خرجت مع رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لصلاة الصبح فكان لا يمر برجل إلا ناداه بالصلاة أو حركه برجله ، أخرجه أبو داود ؛ فإنّه يدلّ على اختصاص الفجر في الجملة. الثاني : ما قاله أبو يوسف له واختاره قاضي خان: إنه يجوز التثويب للأمراء، وكلّ مَن كان مشغولاً بمصالح المسلمين ؛ كالقاضي والمفتي في جميع الصلوات لا لغيرهم، ويشهد له ما ثبت برواياتٍ عديدةٍ أنَّ بلالاً كان يحضر باب الحجرة النبوية بعد الأذان، ويقول : الصلاة الصلاة. والثالث : ما اختاره المتأخّرون أنّ التثويب مستحسن في جميع الصلوات لجميع الناس لظهور التكاسل في أمور الدين، لا سيما في الصلاة، ويستثنى منه المغرب بناء على أنه ليس يفصل فيه كثيراً بين الأذان والإقامة صرح به في «العناية» و«الدرر» و«النهاية» وغيرها، وقد أوضحت المسألة مع دلائلها وفروعها في رسالتي : «التحقيق العجيب في التثويب» فلتطالع.
Such as: “Prayer is better than sleep,” or “Come to prayer,” or “The prayer is present,” or similar, in any language. In the Prophet’s era and the era of his Companions, adding “Prayer is better than sleep” in the adhan of Fajr was called tathwib. This is what Bilal meant by his statement: “The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded me not to do tathwib except in Fajr,” narrated by Ibn Majah. Al-Tahawi narrated in “Sharh Ma‘ani al-Athar” from Ibn ‘Umar and Anas: “Tathwib in the morning was that when the mu’adhdhin said ‘Hayya ‘ala al-falah,’ he would say ‘Prayer is better than sleep.’” As for tathwib between the adhan and iqamah, it was not present in that era; indeed, it was condemned, as narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah: “Abu Mahdhurah, the mu’adhdhin of Makkah, came to ‘Umar after the adhan and said, ‘Prayer, prayer.’ ‘Umar said to him: ‘Woe to you, are you mad? Was there not in your call with which you called us what would bring us?’” Similarly, Ibn ‘Umar condemned tathwib between the adhan and iqamah, as in “Sunan Abi Dawud.” The jurists differed on the ruling of this tathwib into three opinions: First: It is disliked (makruh) in all prayers except Fajr, because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness; and the hadith of Abu Bakrah supports this: “I went out with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, for the Fajr prayer, and he would not pass by a man except he called him to prayer or moved him with his foot,” narrated by Abu Dawud; it indicates the exclusivity of Fajr in general. Second: What Abu Yusuf said and Qadi Khan chose: It is permissible for rulers and anyone occupied with the interests of Muslims, such as a judge and mufti, in all prayers, not for others; and it is supported by numerous narrations that Bilal used to attend the door of the Prophet’s chamber after the adhan and say: “Prayer, prayer.” Third: What the later scholars chose: Tathwib is commendable (mustahsan) in all prayers for all people due to the apparent laziness in religious matters, especially prayer; Maghrib is excepted because there is not much separation between its adhan and iqamah, as stated in “Al-‘Inayah,” “Al-Durar,” “Al-Nihayah,” and others. I have explained the issue with its proofs and branches in my treatise “Al-Tahqiq al-‘Ajib fi al-Tathwib,” so consult it.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by the commentator (author of ‘Umdat al-Ri‘ayah) on the ruling of al-tathwib, which is the additional call after the adhan, specifically the phrase “Prayer is better than sleep” and similar expressions. The commentator first provides a definition and historical background: tathwib originally referred to this phrase in the Fajr adhan, supported by a hadith of Bilal where the Prophet commanded him to only do tathwib in Fajr. However, tathwib between the adhan and iqamah (i.e., calling “al-salah, al-salah”) was not practiced in the prophetic era and was condemned by ‘Umar and Ibn ‘Umar. The commentator then presents three opinions from the Hanafi school: (1) It is disliked (makruh) in all prayers except Fajr, based on a hadith showing the Prophet’s special attention to Fajr. (2) Abu Yusuf and Qadi Khan allow it for rulers and those occupied with public welfare (e.g., judges, muftis) in all prayers, citing Bilal’s practice after the Prophet’s time. (3) The later scholars (mutakkhirin) consider it commendable (mustahsan) for all people in all prayers, except Maghrib, due to general laziness in religious duties. The commentator refers readers to his own treatise for more detail. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the later school is the third opinion, as it addresses the need to remind people.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwib): An additional call after the adhan, originally the phrase “Prayer is better than sleep” in Fajr, extended to other phrases like “al-salah, al-salah” between adhan and iqamah.
مستحسن (mustahsan): Commendable; a ruling that is considered good and recommended, though not obligatory or sunnah mu’akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi scholars (mutakkhirin), in which prayer is tathwib NOT recommended?
A) Fajr
B) Maghrib
C) ‘Isha
D) All prayers include tathwib

Key Takeaway
The later Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that tathwib is commendable in all prayers except Maghrib, due to general laziness in religious commitment.

The Pause Between Adhan and Iqamah
Explaining the recommended pause between adhan and iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the pause between adhan and iqamah, explain its recommended duration based on the hadith, and apply the principle that imperatives (al-amr) in this context indicate recommendation (istikhab) rather than obligation (wujub).

Core Idea
The pause between adhan and iqamah is recommended, not fixed—guided by the hadith's examples.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies the phrase 'wa yajlisu baynahuma' (and sits between them). The commentator explains that this does not require literal sitting but rather a pause to allow people to attend and perform the sunnah prayers. The length of the pause is derived from a hadith, which gives practical examples such as finishing a meal or relieving oneself, showing that the duration is flexible and based on the congregation's needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the literal vs. intended meaning
The phrase 'wa yajlisu' literally means 'and sits,' but the commentator clarifies that the intended meaning is a separation (fasl) between the adhan and iqamah, not literal sitting.
This is a common Hanafi method: interpreting literal terms figuratively when the context requires.
2
Determine the purpose of the pause
The pause allows for two things: (1) the congregation to attend the mosque, and (2) them to pray the sunnah prayers (rawatib) before the obligatory prayer.
This shows the pause is linked to congregation preparation, not a fixed ritual.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith says: 'Place between your adhan and iqamah a measure sufficient for the eater to finish his food, the drinker to finish his drink, and the one relieving himself.' The command 'ij'al' (place) in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation (istikhab) because it is ahad and open to interpretation, not obligation.
The examples demonstrate flexibility; the pause should be long enough for necessary acts but not excessively so.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
The pause should be sufficient for the local congregation to prepare. The mu'adhdhin should observe the recommended duration without rigid timing.
In a mosque, the iqamah typically follows after a few minutes, allowing time for sunnah prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ويجلس بينهما ; ليس المراد به خصوص الجلوس، بل الفصل بين الأذان والإقامة مقدار ما يحضر القومُ ويصلّون السنن ، مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب لحديث : اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك قدر ما يفرغ الآكل من أكله ، والشارب من شربه، والمعتصر
His statement: “and sits between them” – the intended meaning is not specifically sitting, but rather the separation between the adhan and iqamah by a measure sufficient for the people to attend and pray the sunnah prayers, while observing the recommended time, because of the hadith: “Place between your adhan and iqamah a measure sufficient for the eater to finish his food, the drinker to finish his drink, and the one relieving himself.”
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase “ويجلس بينهما” (and sits between them) from the original matn of Al-Wiqayah. The commentator clarifies that this does not mean literal sitting; rather, it refers to a pause between the adhan and iqamah. The purpose of this pause is to allow people time to attend the mosque and perform the sunnah prayers (rawatib) before the obligatory prayer. The recommended duration is based on a hadith that says the pause should be enough for a person to finish eating, drinking, or answering the call of nature. This shows that the length of the pause is flexible and depends on the needs of the congregation, but it should not be excessively long.

Key Terms
ويجلس (wa yajlisu): Literally “and sits,” but here it is interpreted figuratively as a pause or separation between the adhan and iqamah.
الفصل (al-fasl): The separation or pause between adhan and iqamah.
السنن (al-sunan): The sunnah prayers (rawatib) performed before the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The pause between adhan and iqamah is a recommended sunnah, not an obligation; its length is flexible and determined by the congregation's need for preparation.

Tathwib: Definition and Hanafi Positions
Defines tathwib and presents three Hanafi opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tathwib, identify the three Hanafi opinions, and explain which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Tathwib is an additional call to prayer; later Hanafi scholars deem it recommended for all prayers except maghrib.

The passage defines tathwib as 'the announcement after the announcement' and details three Hanafi opinions on its permissibility. Understanding these opinions and their evidence helps clarify the relied-upon practice for fatwa. This lesson will walk you through the definition, the three views, and the final tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tathwib
Tathwib literally means 'the announcement after the announcement'. It is a second call to prayer after the adhan, not restricted to specific words or language.
Even clearing the throat can serve as tathwib.
2
Identify the three Hanafi opinions
First opinion (not stated): likely restricted to fajr. Second (Abu Yusuf/Qadi Khan): permissible only for rulers, judges, muftis. Third (later scholars): recommended for all people for all prayers except maghrib.
The first opinion is implicit from the discussion.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Bilal coming to the Prophet's door after adhan saying 'al-salah, al-salah' is cited to support tathwib as a reminder.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala, but it is supported by istihsan.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and exception
Later scholars chose tathwib as mustahsan for all people in all prayers due to laziness, except maghrib because its adhan and iqamah are close. This is the relied-upon position.
The exception for maghrib is based on the short interval.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التثويب هو الإعلام بعد الإعلام. الثاني : ما قاله أبو يوسف له واختاره قاضي خان: إنه جائز التثويب للأمراء، وكلّ مَن كان مشغولاً بمصالح المسلمين ؛ كالقاضي والمفتي في جميع الصلوات لا لغيرهم، ويشهد له ما ثبت برواياتٍ عديدةٍ أنَّ بلالاً كان يحضر باب الحجرة النبوية بعد الأذان، ويقول : الصلاة الصلاة. والثالث : ما اختاره المتأخّرون أنّ التثويب مستحسن في جميع الصلوات لجميع الناس لظهور التكاسل في أمور الدين، لا سيما في الصلاة، ويستثنى منه المغرب بناء على أنه ليس يفصل فيه كثيراً بين الأذان والإقامة صرح به في «العناية» و«الدرر» و«النهاية» وغيرها، وقد أوضحت المسألة مع دلائلها وفروعها في رسالتي : «التحقيق العجيب في التثويب» فلتطالع. [١]قوله : هو الإعلام بعد الاعلام؛ أشار بإطلاقه؛ أي أنه لا يخص التثويب بلفظ دون لفظ، بل يكفي فيه التنحنح أيضاً، ولا يختص أيضاً بلسان دون لسان، وإلى أن استحسان التثويب إنما هو لما كان له الإعلام الأوّل فما تعورف في بعض بلادنا من قول : الصلاة الصلاة سنة رسول الله بين الأذانين من يوم الجمعة ليس داخلاً في استحسان المتأخرين ولا في استحسان المتقدمين، فيلزم تركه.
Tathwib is the announcement after the announcement. The second: what Abu Yusuf said and Qadi Khan chose: that tathwib is permissible for rulers and everyone occupied with the interests of Muslims, like the judge and the mufti, in all prayers, not for others. This is supported by numerous reports that Bilal used to come to the door of the Prophet's chamber after the adhan and say: 'The prayer, the prayer.' The third: what the later scholars chose: that tathwib is deemed good in all prayers for all people because of the appearance of laziness in religious matters, especially in prayer, and maghrib is excepted based on the fact that there is not much separation between its adhan and iqamah, as stated in al-'Inayah, al-Durar, al-Nihayah, etc. I have clarified the issue with its proofs and branches in my treatise 'al-Tahqiq al-'Ajib fi al-Tathwib', so let it be consulted. [1] His saying: 'It is the announcement after the announcement'; he indicated by its absoluteness that tathwib is not restricted to a particular wording, rather even clearing the throat suffices, and it is also not restricted to a particular language. And that the approval of tathwib is only because he had the first announcement. So what has become customary in some of our countries of saying 'al-salah, al-salah, sunnat rasul Allah' between the two adhans on Friday is not included in the approval of the later scholars nor in the approval of the earlier ones, so it must be abandoned.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on tathwib, the second call after the adhan. The matn defines tathwib as 'the announcement after the announcement.' The commentary presents three opinions within the Hanafi school: the first opinion (not stated here but implied) likely restricted tathwib to fajr; the second opinion, attributed to Abu Yusuf and chosen by Qadi Khan, permits tathwib only for those occupied with public interests (rulers, judges, muftis) in all prayers, citing the hadith of Bilal. The third opinion, chosen by later scholars (mutakhkhirin), deems tathwib recommended (mustahsan) for all people in all prayers due to religious laziness, except maghrib because of the short interval between adhan and iqamah. The commentary then clarifies that tathwib is not restricted to any specific wording or language; even clearing the throat suffices. It warns against the custom of saying 'al-salah, al-salah sunnat rasul Allah' between the two adhans on Friday, as it is not part of the approved practice.

Key Terms
التثويب (al-tathwib): The second announcement after the adhan, consisting of calling people to prayer, usually with 'al-salah, al-salah' or similar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Maghrib
C) Isha
D) All prayers are included

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position considers tathwib mustahsan for all prayers except maghrib, based on the hadith of Bilal and istihsan.

The Interval Between Adhan and Iqamah
Explains ruling on interval between adhan and iqamah, with exception for maghrib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the interval between adhan and iqamah, explain the exception for maghrib, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The interval is sunnah for all prayers except maghrib, where only a brief silence suffices.

The base text says 'he sits between them,' but the commentary clarifies that 'sitting' is not literal—it means any meaningful separation to allow worshippers to prepare. A hadith specifies sufficient time for eating, drinking, or relieving oneself. However, for maghrib, Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ on whether a light sitting is recommended. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its proof
From the matn and hadith, determine that the interval between adhan and iqamah is sunnah muakkadah for all prayers except maghrib. The hadith provides the recommended duration.
The hadith is narrated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Hakim.
2
Understand the term 'sitting' is not literal
The commentary explicitly says 'ليس المراد به خصوص الجلوس' – the intended meaning is the separation, not necessarily sitting. The interval can be any activity that allows people to prepare.
This prevents misunderstanding that one must physically sit.
3
Recognize the exception for maghrib
The text states 'وهذا كله في غير المغرب' – all this applies to non-maghrib prayers. For maghrib, a longer pause is discouraged because the time for maghrib is short and delaying it is prohibited.
The prohibition is established elsewhere in fiqh.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says to suffice with a silence of about three short verses or three steps; the Sahibayn recommend a light sitting like the khatib. Compare their reasoning.
Abu Hanifa fears delay; Sahibayn see benefit in some pause.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
According to al-Hidayah, the view of the Sahibayn (light sitting) is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Tarjih authority: al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجلس بينهما. قوله : ويجلس بينهما؛ ليس المراد به خصوص الجلوس، بل الفصل بين الأذان والإقامة مقدار ما يحضر القومُ ويصلّون السنن ، مع مراعاة الوقت المستحب لحديث : اجعل بين أذانك وإقامتك قدر ما يفرغ الآكل من أكله ، والشارب من شربه، والمعتصر إذا دخل لقضاء حاجته قاله النبي لبلال له ، أخرجه الترمذي والحاكم، وهذا كله في غير المغرب. أما فيه فقال أبو حنيفة : الأفضل أن لا يجلس فيه، بل يكتفي فيه بالسكوت بمقدار ثلاث آيات قصار، أو ثلاث خطوات؛ لئلا يلزم تأخيرُ المغرب المنهي عنه، وقالا : يجلس بينهما جلسة خفيفة، كجلسة الخطيب. كذا في «الهداية وشروحها.
And he sits between them. His saying: 'And he sits between them'; what is meant is not specifically sitting, but the separation between the adhan and iqamah to the extent that the people can attend and pray the sunnah prayers, while observing the recommended time, due to the hadith: 'Make between your adhan and iqamah enough time for the eater to finish his meal, the drinker to finish his drink, and the one who needs to relieve himself to do so,' which the Prophet said to Bilal, recorded by al-Tirmidhi and al-Hakim. All this is for other than maghrib. As for maghrib, Abu Hanifa said: It is better not to sit, rather to suffice with a silence of about three short verses or three steps, lest the delay of maghrib, which is prohibited, occur. And the two said: He sits between them a brief sitting, like the sitting of the khatib. Thus in al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on the interval between adhan and iqamah. The matn states 'he sits between them,' but the commentary clarifies that 'sitting' is not literal; it means any sufficient separation to allow people to prepare and pray sunnah prayers. The recommended duration is based on a hadith: enough time for eating, drinking, or relieving oneself. This applies to all prayers except maghrib. For maghrib, Abu Hanifa holds that no sitting is needed; a brief silence of three short verses or three steps suffices to avoid delaying maghrib (which is prohibited). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad recommend a light sitting like that of the khatib (preacher). The relied-upon position is that of the two (Sahibayn) according to al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
الجلوس بين الأذان والإقامة (al-julus bayna al-adhan wa al-iqamah): The interval or pause between the adhan and iqamah, not necessarily sitting, but a separation to allow people to attend and pray sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A brief silence of three short verses or steps.
C) A light sitting similar to the sitting of the khatib.
D) The same interval as other prayers.

Key Takeaway
The interval between adhan and iqamah is sunnah muakkadah, but for maghrib only a light sitting is recommended, following the Sahibayn's view.

Adhan for Missed Prayers and by a Muhdith
Rulings on adhan for missed prayers and adhan by one in minor impurity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on adhan for missed prayers and adhan by a muhdith, and apply the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
One adhan suffices for multiple missed prayers; adhan by a muhdith is permissible without dislike.

This lesson covers two distinct but related rulings: how adhan is performed for missed (qada) prayers, and the ruling on adhan by a person who is in a state of minor impurity (muhdith). Both are grounded in the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the rulings of the Hanafi school. Understanding these will help you correctly observe the sunnah in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
Locate the two main rulings in the text: (1) adhan for missed prayers, and (2) adhan by a muhdith. Note the legal classification for each.
The text explicitly states the ruling for missed prayers and then the ruling for adhan by a muhdith.
2
Analyze the proof for missed prayers
Identify the dalil (proof) cited: the Prophet's action on the day of the Battle of the Confederates. Note how the hadith shows the practice of one adhan and multiple iqamahs.
The hadith is recorded by al-Tirmidhi and is considered a precedent.
3
Understand the application details
Examine the commentary: the choice between doing both adhan and iqamah for each missed prayer or just iqamah. Also note the exceptions for praying alone vs. in the mosque.
The text from 'Minh al-Ghaffar' and 'Maraqi al-Falah' provides these details.
4
Evaluate the ruling on muhdith
Identify the Hanafi position that adhan by a muhdith is permissible without dislike, and iqamah is disliked. Note the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.
The ruling is based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا في المغرب، ويؤذِّنُ للفائتة ، ويقيم ، وكذا لأولى الفوائت ولكل من البواقي يأتي بهما، أو بها. وجاز أذان المحدث، وكره إقامته. قوله : للفائتة؛ الأصل فيه قصة ليلة التعريس، وسيأتي ذكرها في باب إدراك الفريضة إن شاء الله تعالى، قال في «منح الغفار»: «هذا إذا قضى منفرداً، أما إذا كان في المسجد فلا أذان لها». انتهى. وفي «مراقي الفلاح»: «إذا كان التفويت لأمر عام فالأذان في المسجد لا يكره». (٢) قوله : بهما أو بها ; أي هو مُخيّر بين أن يؤدن ويقيم للكل، وبين أن يكتفي على الإقامة كما اكتفى به رسول الله حين فاتته أربع صلوات يوم غزوة الأحزاب فقضى الظهر والعصر والمغرب بأذان واحدٍ وإقامة متعدّدة، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره. [٣]قوله : وجاز أذان المحدث ; أي من به حدث أصغر، يعني بلا كراهة في ظاهر الرواية.
Except in maghrib, and he calls adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah, and likewise for the first of multiple missed prayers, and for each of the remaining he may do both (adhan and iqamah) or just iqamah. And the adhan of one in minor impurity is permissible, and his iqamah is disliked. His saying: 'for the missed prayer'; the basis is the story of the night of 'ta'ris' (the night they overslept), which will come in the chapter on catching up the prayer, God willing. In 'Minh al-Ghaffar': 'This is when he prays alone; if in the mosque, there is no adhan for it.' End. In 'Maraqi al-Falah': 'If the missing was due to a general matter, adhan in the mosque is not disliked.' (2) His saying: 'both or just it' means he has a choice between doing adhan and iqamah for all, or just doing iqamah, as the Messenger of God did when he missed four prayers on the day of the Battle of the Confederates and made up zuhr, asr, maghrib, and isha with one adhan and multiple iqamahs, recorded by al-Tirmidhi and others. [3] His saying: 'The adhan of one in minor impurity is permissible' means without dislike in the apparent narration.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage deals with two distinct rulings. First, for missed prayers (fawa'it): one performs adhan and iqamah for a single missed prayer. If multiple prayers are missed, one may either do adhan and iqamah for each, or do one adhan for the first and iqamah only for the rest, based on the Prophet's practice during the Battle of the Confederates. The commentary adds that this applies when praying alone; in the mosque, adhan is not needed unless the missing was due to a general matter. Second, the adhan of a person with minor hadath (e.g., without wudu) is permissible without dislike, but his iqamah is disliked. This is based on the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms
المحدث (al-muhdith): One who is in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath asghar), i.e., without wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is disliked but valid
D) It is prohibited

Key Takeaway
Adhan by a muhdith is permissible without dislike; for missed prayers, one adhan suffices for multiple prayers, while iqamah is required for each.

Adhan for Missed Prayers and Sitting in Maghrib
Rulings on adhan for fā'itah and intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in Maghrib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan for fā'itah and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in Maghrib, identifying the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
For missed prayers, adhan is wajib when alone; in Maghrib, Abu Hanifa forbids sitting to avoid delay.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on rulings related to adhan for missed prayers and a specific dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding the Maghrib prayer. You will learn the basic ruling on adhan for fā'itah and then delve into the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether to sit between the adhan and iqamah in Maghrib. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace tarjih within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on adhan for missed prayers
The passage states that for a missed prayer (fā'itah), adhan and iqamah are performed. For multiple missed prayers, one may choose a single adhan with multiple iqamahs, or separate adhan and iqamah for each.
This applies when praying alone, not in the mosque.
2
Note the exception for mosque
Commentaries clarify that adhan for fā'itah is not required when in the mosque, unless the prayers were missed for a public reason.
This avoids duplication of the mosque's adhan.
3
Locate the dispute on Maghrib
The phrase 'Except in Maghrib' introduces a dispute about whether to sit between adhan and iqamah in Maghrib. Abu Hanifa says no sitting; Sahibayn say a light sitting is allowed.
The dispute is about the interval, not whether adhan is performed.
4
Analyze each position's dalil
Abu Hanifa's proof: avoiding the prohibition of delaying Maghrib (takhrīj al-maghrib al-manhī 'anhu). Sahibayn's proof: analogy (qiyas) to the khatib's sitting between the two khutbahs.
Both proofs rely on different principles: prohibition of delay vs. analogical reasoning.
5
Determine the tarjih
The passage indicates that Abu Hanifa's view is 'al-afḍal' (the better) and is the mufta bihi according to al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا في المغرب، ويؤذن للفائتة ويقيم، وكذا لأولى الفوائت ولكل من البواقي يأتي بهما أو بها. قال في «منح الغفار»: هذا إذا قضى منفرداً، أما إذا كان في المسجد فلا أذان لها. وفي «مراقي الفلاح»: إذا كان التفويت لأمر عام فالأذان في المسجد لا يكره. قوله: بهما أو بها؛ أي هو مُخيّر بين أن يؤدن ويقيم للكل، وبين أن يكتفي على الإقامة كما اكتفى به رسول الله ﷺ حين فاتته أربع صلوات يوم غزوة الأحزاب فقضى الظهر والعصر والمغرب بأذان واحد وإقامة متعددة، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره. وهذا كله في غير المغرب. أما فيه فقال أبو حنيفة: الأفضل أن لا يجلس فيه، بل يكتفي فيه بالسكوت بمقدار ثلاث آيات قصار، أو ثلاث خطوات؛ لئلا يلزم تأخير المغرب المنهي عنه. وقالا: يجلس بينهما جلسة خفيفة، كجلسة الخطيب. كذا في «الهداية وشروحها.
Except in Maghrib, and he makes adhan for the missed prayer and iqamah, and likewise for the first of the missed prayers, and for each of the remaining he comes with both or with it. He said in 'Manh al-Ghaffar': This is if he prays alone; but if in the mosque, there is no adhan for it. In 'Maraqi al-Falah': If the missing was due to a public matter, adhan in the mosque is not disliked. His statement: 'with both or with it' means he has a choice between making adhan and iqamah for all, or being content with iqamah alone, as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ did when he missed four prayers on the day of the Battle of the Trench; he prayed Zuhr, Asr, and Maghrib with one adhan and multiple iqamahs, narrated by Tirmidhi and others. All this is for other than Maghrib. As for Maghrib, Abu Hanifa said: The better is not to sit therein, but to suffice with silence for the duration of three short verses or three steps, lest delaying Maghrib, which is prohibited, occur. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He sits between them a light sitting, like the sitting of a khatib. Thus in al-Hidayah and its commentaries.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the practice between the adhan and iqamah in the Maghrib prayer, along with the ruling on adhan for missed prayers. The base text states that for missed prayers (fā'itah), one performs adhan and iqamah, or for multiple missed prayers, one may choose either a single adhan with multiple iqamahs or separate adhan and iqamah for each. The commentary clarifies that this applies when praying alone; in the mosque, adhan is generally not required, unless the missed prayers were due to a public reason. The key dispute concerns Maghrib: Abu Hanifa holds that one should not sit between adhan and iqamah, but instead remain silent for a short time or take three steps, to avoid delaying the Maghrib prayer (which is disliked). The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that a light sitting, resembling that of a khatib between the two khutbahs, is permissible. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view, as indicated by the phrase 'al-afḍal' (the better).

Key Terms
فائتة (fā'itah): A missed obligatory prayer that must be made up (qada).
أذان (adhan): The call to prayer consisting of specific phrases announcing the time of salah.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call immediately before the commencement of prayer, similar to adhan but with 'qad qāmat al-ṣalāh' added.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the preferred action between the adhan and iqamah for Maghrib?
A) Sit briefly like a khatib
B) Remain silent for the duration of three short verses
C) Continue directly without any pause
D) Recite extra takbir

Key Takeaway
For missed prayers, adhan is wajib when alone; in Maghrib, the preferred practice is not to sit to avoid delay.

Adhan and Iqamah by a Person in Impurity: Hanafi Rulings and Intra-Madhhab Disputes
Rulings on adhan/iqamah by a person with minor or major impurity and its repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah by a person with minor or major impurity, explain the reasoning behind the dislike, and distinguish the relied-upon position from the variant narrations.

Core Idea
Adhan by a muḥdath is permissible; iqamah is disliked. For junub, both are disliked but valid—none require repetition.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position on who may call the adhan and iqamah. While purification (taharah) is highly recommended for acts of worship, the Hanafi school makes a nuanced distinction between minor and major impurity. You will also encounter different narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa himself, showing the richness of ijtihad within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four cases
The base text presents four scenarios: adhan by muḥdath, iqamah by muḥdath, adhan by junub, iqamah by junub. For each, note the ruling (permissible/disliked) and whether repetition is required.
2
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil)
The commentary explains that adhan resembles both prayer (requiring purity) and general dhikr (not requiring purity). The Hanafi school gives preponderance to the latter for minor impurity, but the severity of major impurity tips the balance toward dislike.
This is a classic example of weighing shabah (similarity) in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two variant narrations from Abu Hanifa are mentioned: one where iqamah is not disliked, another where adhan is also disliked. Identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position and why the other narrations are not operative.
The commentary implicitly favors the base text's position.
4
Assess the dalil (evidence)
The hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ' is cited but deemed weak. Understand how a weak hadith can still indicate recommendation (istiḥbāb) but not obligation or prohibition.
This illustrates the Hanafi approach to weak hadith when they are not contradicted by stronger evidence.
5
Compare with other schools
Note that the Shafi'i school requires wudu for both adhan and iqamah, and considers janabah invalidating. Recognize the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in how a mosque would handle an impure caller.
This builds skill in cross-madhhab comparison.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجاز أذان المحدث، وكره إقامته. ولم يعادا، وكره أذان الجنب وإقامته، ولا تعاد هي، بل هو كأذان المرأة. وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة: لا تكره الإقامة أيضاً، وفي رواية: يكره الأذان أيضاً. أما حديث: «لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ» أخرجه الترمذي وأشار إلى تضعيفه فلا يدل إلا على الاستحباب. قوله: ولم يعادا؛ أي إن أذن أو أقام محدثاً لا يجب إعادته، أما عدم إعادة الأذان فلأنه لا كراهة فيه، وأما عدم الإقامة، فلعدم مشروعية تكرار الإقامة؛ ولذا لا تعاد إقامة الجنب. قوله: أذان الجنب؛ وذلك لأن للأذان شبهاً بالصلاة، وشبهاً بباقي الأذكار، فاعتبرنا الشبهين، وقلنا: لا يكره مع الحدث الأصغر، ويكره مع الحدث الأكبر، وأما الإقامة فإنها إذا كرهت بالحدث الأصغر كرهت بالحدث الأكبر بالطريق الأولى. قوله: بل هو؛ أي الأذان، قال محمد في الجامع الصغير: أحب إلي أن يعيد وإن لم يعد أجزأه. قوله: تكرار الإقامة؛ أي الصلاة واحدة بخلاف الأذان، فإن تكراره مشروع كأذان الجمعة. قوله: كأذان المرأة؛ لأن في أذانها احتمال وقوع الفتنة برفع صوتها، فلذلك لا يشرع أذان المرأة.
And the adhan of a person with minor impurity is permissible, and his iqamah is disliked. And they are not repeated. And the adhan of a janab (major impurity) and his iqamah are disliked, and it (the iqamah) is not repeated. Rather, it is like the adhan of a woman. And in a narration from Abu Hanifa: the iqamah is also not disliked, and in a narration: the adhan is also disliked. As for the hadith: 'No one should make adhan except with wudu' – narrated by Tirmidhi and he indicated its weakness, so it only indicates recommendation. His statement: 'and they are not repeated' means if a person with minor impurity makes adhan or iqamah, it is not obligatory to repeat them. As for not repeating the adhan, because there is no dislike in it; as for not repeating the iqamah, because repeating iqamah is not prescribed; hence the iqamah of a janab is not repeated. His statement: 'adhan of a janab' – because adhan resembles prayer on one hand and other remembrances on the other, so we consider both aspects and say: it is not disliked with minor impurity, but it is disliked with major impurity. As for iqamah, if it is disliked with minor impurity, it is disliked with major impurity by a stronger reason. His statement: 'rather it' meaning the adhan. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: I prefer that he repeat it, and if he does not repeat, it suffices. His statement: 'repeating iqamah' – i.e., the prayer is one, unlike adhan, for repeating it is prescribed like the adhan of Friday. His statement: 'like the adhan of a woman' – because in her adhan there is possibility of fitnah due to raising her voice, therefore the adhan of a woman is not prescribed.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rulings on adhan and iqamah by a person in a state of impurity. The base text states that adhan by a person with minor impurity (ḥadaṯ aṣghar) is permissible (jā'iz) without dislike, but iqamah is disliked (makrūh). Neither requires repetition. For major impurity (janābah), both adhan and iqamah are disliked, but again, they are not repeated. The commentary explains the reasoning: adhan is similar to prayer (requiring purity) but also to general dhikr (permissible without purity); the stronger resemblance is to dhikr, so minor impurity does not cause dislike, but major impurity does due to its severity. For iqamah, because it is disliked even with minor impurity, it is automatically more disliked with major impurity. The passage also notes differing narrations from Abu Hanifa: one where iqamah is not disliked, another where adhan is also disliked. The relied-upon position is the one in the base text (adhan permissible, iqamah disliked for minor impurity). The hadith 'no adhan except with wudu' is considered weak, so it only indicates recommendation (istiḥbāb). The commentary adds that Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers to repeat the adhan if done without wudu, but it is sufficient if not repeated. The comparison to a woman's adhan is because women are not prescribed to give adhan due to the potential for fitnah (raising voice).

Key Terms
محدث (muḥdath): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (ḥadath aṣghar) that requires wudu.
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janābah) requiring ghusl.
إقامة (iqāmah): The second call to prayer immediately before the commencement of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the adhan by a person in major impurity (junub) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Valid and not disliked
B) Disliked (makruh) but not repeated
C) Invalid and must be repeated with ghusl
D) Permissible but only if no other person is present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, adhan does not require wudu; minor impurity does not make it disliked, but major impurity does. Iqamah is disliked for both, none require repetition.

Adhan by a Junub and Woman: Disliked but Valid
Ruling on adhan and iqamah by a junub and lack of repetition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adhan and iqamah by a junub, identify the evidence for the ruling, and explain why no repetition is required.

Core Idea
Adhan by a junub is disliked but valid — no repetition is required.

This passage clarifies that while purity is recommended for adhan, it is not a condition of validity. However, major impurity (janabah) makes the adhan and iqamah disliked (makruh tahrimi) due to adhan's resemblance to salah. The author also addresses the weak hadith commonly cited and intra-Hanafi differences, concluding that the adhan is valid and need not be repeated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the act being ruled upon (adhan and iqamah of a junub) and the hukm level: makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The passage states 'كره أذان الجنب وإقامته' — both are disliked.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the weak hadith 'لا يؤذن إلا متوضئ' and the reasoning of resemblance to salah (shabah bi al-salah).
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and declared weak.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the evidence proves the ruling: the weak hadith only indicates recommendation (istihbab), and the resemblance argument makes adhan with major impurity disliked, but not invalid.
Hanafi usul: a weak hadith cannot establish obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi narrations (Abu Hanifa's different reports) and the Shafi'i position that adhan by a junub is invalid.
The Shafi'i school requires purity as a condition for adhan.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi position: adhan by a junub is makruh but valid; no repetition required. This is based on the majority of Hanafi authorities.
Al-Marghinani and others rely on the resemblance argument.

Book of Salah / Adhan. And they are not repeated, and the adhan of a junub and his iqamah are disliked, but they are not repeated; rather it is like the adhan of a woman and they are not repeated. And he said: the adhan of a junub and his iqamah are disliked, and they are not repeated; rather it is... because the repetition of iqamah is not prescribed, since it is for informing those present, so one suffices. The adhan is for informing those absent, so some may hear and others not, so its repetition is beneficial. (Like the adhan of a woman in the narration) because adhan is a form of dhikr like other adhkar, so purification is recommended for it, and it is not disliked without it, like reciting the Qur'an. Regarding iqamah while in a state of impurity: it necessitates a separation between the iqamah and the prayer by occupying oneself with purification, and that is disliked, so they differ. In one narration from Abu Hanifa: iqamah is also not disliked; in another narration: adhan is also disliked. As in al-Bahr. As for the hadith: 'None should give adhan except one who is in a state of wudu'—at-Tirmidhi narrated it and indicated its weakness, so it only indicates recommendation. [1] His saying: 'and they are not repeated': meaning if one gives adhan or iqamah while in a state of impurity, it is not obligatory to repeat it. As for not repeating adhan, because there is no dislike for it; as for iqamah, because the repetition of iqamah is not prescribed, hence the iqamah of a junub is not repeated. [2] His saying: 'the adhan of a junub': because adhan resembles salah and also resembles other adhkar, so we consider both resemblances and say: it is not disliked with minor impurity, but it is disliked with major impurity. As for iqamah, since it is disliked with minor impurity, it is disliked with major impurity a fortiori. As in al-Dhakhirah. [3] His saying: 'rather it is': i.e., the adhan. Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'I prefer that he repeat it, but if he does not repeat, it suffices.' [4] His saying: 'repetition of iqamah': i.e., the prayer is one, unlike adhan, for its repetition is prescribed like the adhan of Friday. [0] His saying: 'like the adhan of a woman': because in her adhan there is the potential for fitna due to raising her voice, therefore her adhan is disliked, and likewise the adhan of a hermaphrodite. As in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings of adhan and iqamah concerning ritual purity. The base text states that if someone gives adhan or iqamah while in a state of minor impurity, they are not required to repeat them. The author then clarifies that the adhan and iqamah of a junub (someone in major impurity) are disliked (makruh), but they are still valid and not to be repeated. This is different from the repetition of iqamah which is not prescribed because iqamah is only for those already present. The adhan is for informing those far away, so repetition can be useful. The text compares this to a woman's adhan, which is also disliked. The commentary explains why minor impurity does not make adhan disliked: because adhan is a form of dhikr like any other, and purification is only recommended. Major impurity, however, makes it makruh because adhan has resemblance to salah. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa that iqamah is not disliked at all, and another that adhan is also disliked. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that adhan with minor impurity is not makruh, but with major impurity it is. For iqamah, the dislike is stronger. The hadith 'none should give adhan except with wudu' is considered weak and only indicates recommendation, not obligation. Imam Muhammad preferred to repeat the adhan if given by a junub, but it is not obligatory.

Key Terms
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah) requiring ghusl.
كراهة (karahah): Disliked act; here it refers to makruh tahrimi (close to haram) in Hanafi terminology.
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, recited immediately before the obligatory prayer begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid and must be repeated.
B) It is disliked (makruh) but valid.
C) It is neither disliked nor invalid; it is valid and recommended to have wudu.
D) It is prohibited (haram).

Key Takeaway
Adhan by a junub is makruh but valid; no repetition is required for either adhan or iqamah.

Adhan by Madman, Drunkard, Traveler, and Congregant
Rulings on adhan by madman, drunkard, traveler, and congregant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on adhan for the madman, drunkard, traveler, and one praying in congregation, and apply the Hanafi distinction between when adhan is required and when it is disliked.

Core Idea
The adhan of one without intellect is invalid; the traveler and congregant must perform adhan.

This lesson examines four categories of people and the legal status of their adhan. The madman and drunkard lack the intellectual capacity required for valid adhan, while the traveler and one praying in congregation are commanded to perform it. Understanding these distinctions helps you apply the Sunna correctly in varying circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
The text treats four persons: madman, drunkard, traveler, and one praying in congregation. Each has a different ruling.
Also includes the child who does not understand and the idiot by analogy.
2
Determine the ruling for the madman and drunkard
Their adhan is disliked (makruh) and it is recommended (mustahabb) to repeat it; some say it is obligatory. Reason: lack of intellect and intention.
The same applies to any person without understanding.
3
Determine the ruling for the traveler
The traveler should perform adhan and iqamah; leaving them is disliked. Evidence: the hadith commanding it.
This applies whether alone or with companions.
4
Determine the ruling for the one praying in congregation
If he prays in congregation in the mosque, he should perform adhan and iqamah; leaving them is disliked. However, if he prays alone in his house after the congregation, it is not disliked to leave them.
The congregational adhan suffices for the latter.
