Prayer Without Garment: Standing vs Sitting Gestures
Ruling for the garmentless

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that a person without any garment may pray standing or sitting with gestures, and determine which is recommended.

Core Idea
If you have no garment, prayer is valid but sitting with gestures is better than standing.

What if a person loses all clothing and must pray naked? The Hanafi school provides a choice: stand with bowing and prostration, or sit making gestures. This lesson explains the options and which is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person has no garment at all to cover his 'awrah. He must pray naked.
This is the extreme case.
2
State the basic choices
He may pray standing (with full ruku and sujud) or he may pray sitting with gestures (isharah). Both are permissible.
The text says 'praying standing is permissible, and sitting gesturing is recommended'.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Standing allows performance of the physical pillars (ruku, sujud), but he is naked. Sitting covers his body somewhat (by folding) but sacrifices the full pillars. Both have pros and cons.
The commentary says covering the 'awrah has no substitute, while pillars can be substituted with gestures.
4
Determine the recommended action
The text says sitting gesturing is recommended (mandub) because covering the 'awrah is more important than performing the pillars with full movements.
The principle: the substitute (gesture) can replace the pillars, but there is no substitute for covering 'awrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشعرٍ نزل من رأسها، وربع ذكره منفرداً، والأُنثَيين يمنع، وعادِمُ مزيل النَّجس صلى معه، ولم يعد، فإن صلى عارياً وربع ثوبه طاهر لم يجز، وفي أقل من ربع الأفضل صلاته فيه، ومن عَدمَ ثوباً فصلى قائماً جاز، وقاعداً مومئاً ندب.

قوله: نزل من رأسها؛ قيد به لأنه لا خلاف في الشعر الذي على الرأس في أنه عورة إنما الخلاف في المسترسل فقيل: ليس بعورة، والصحيح أنه عورة. قوله: ولم يعد؛ لأن تكليف التطهير سقط عنه للعجز. قوله: الأفضل؛ يعني هو مخير بين أن يصلي عُرياناً وبين أن يُصلي في ذلك النجس؛ لأن كلاً منهما مانع عن جواز الصلاة حالة الاختيار، ومستو في حق المقدار فتساويا، والأفضل هو التستّر، فإن لبس الثوب النجس أهون من كونه عُرياناً، حتى جاز الأول خارج الصلاة لا الثاني، ومن ابتلي ببليتين يختار أهونهما. قوله: نُدِبَ؛ إما مصدر بمعنى المفعول، أو ماض مجهول، يعني: إنه مخير بين أن يصلي قائماً بركوع وسجود، وبين أن يصلي قاعداً بالإيماء؛ لأن في القيام أداء الأركان، وفي القعود ستر في الجملة، فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، والأفضل هو الثاني؛ لأن الأركان لهما خلف وهو الإيماء، ولا خلف الستر العورة.

الأنثيان: الخصيتان. ينظر: «الصحاح»(١ : ٥١). أي الخبث عدماً حقيقياً أو حكمياً، كما إذا كان معه ماء، لكن يخاف العطش، فإن صلى مع النجس للضرورة لم يُعد، وإن كان الوقت باقياً؛ لأنه فعل ما في وسعه. كذا في «فتح باب العناية» (١ : ٢٢٠). وفي «المحيط»: الأصح أنه عورة وإلا جاز النظر إلى صدغ الأجنبية وطرف ناصيتها وهو يؤدي إلى الفتنة. وفي الغياثية: ولا بأس بالنظر إلى شعر الكافرة. ينظر: «التبيين» (٦ : ١٧)، «درر الحكام» (١ : ٥٩)، «الشرنبلالية» (١ : ٥٩)، وغيرها.
And hair that has fallen from her head, and a quarter of his organ alone, and the two testicles prevent. And one who lacks a means of removing impurity prays with it and does not repeat. For if he prays naked while a quarter of his garment is pure, it is not permissible. And in less than a quarter, it is better for him to pray in it. And one who lacks a garment, if he prays standing, it is permissible; and sitting gesturing is recommended.

His statement: 'hair that has fallen from her head' – he restricted it because there is no disagreement about the hair on the head being 'awrah; the disagreement is about the hanging hair, so it was said it is not 'awrah, and the correct view is that it is 'awrah. His statement: 'does not repeat' – because the obligation of purification has fallen from him due to inability. His statement: 'the best' – meaning he has a choice between praying naked and praying in that impurity, because each of them is a preventer of the permissibility of prayer in the state of ability, and they are equal in terms of quantity, so they are equal; but the best is to cover, because wearing the impure garment is lighter than being naked, so much so that the first is allowed outside the prayer while the second is not, and one who is afflicted with two afflictions chooses the lighter of them. His statement: 'recommended' – either a verbal noun in the sense of the passive, or a passive past verb; meaning he has a choice between praying standing with bowing and prostration, and praying sitting with gestures, because in standing there is performance of the pillars, and in sitting there is covering in general, so he may incline to whichever he wishes, but the better is the second, because the pillars have a substitute for them, which is gesture, and covering the 'awrah has no substitute.

The testicles: meaning the two testes. See: al-Sihah (1:51). That is, impurity, whether actual or legal, as when he has water but fears thirst; then if he prays with the impurity out of necessity, he does not repeat, even if the time remains, because he did what he could. Thus in Fath Bab al-Inayah (1:220). And in al-Muhit: the soundest view is that it is 'awrah, otherwise it would be permissible to look at the temple and the tip of the forelock of a foreign woman, which leads to fitna. And in al-Ghiyathiyyah: There is no harm in looking at the hair of a disbelieving woman. See: al-Tabyin (6:17), Durar al-Hukkam (1:59), al-Shurnubulaliyyah (1:59), etc.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage from the commentary provides detailed rulings on the conditions of covering the 'awrah (intimate parts) and removing impurity during prayer. The rulings are from the Hanafi school. The text begins by listing what constitutes a valid covering: hair that has fallen from a woman's head (i.e., not attached to the scalp) is considered a separate limb. For a man, a quarter of his organ alone (without the testicles) invalidates the prayer if uncovered, and the testicles themselves also prevent validity because they are 'awrah. 

Then the discussion turns to a person who has no means to remove impurity (e.g., no water, no clean cloth). Such a person prays with the impurity on his clothes or body and does not need to repeat the prayer later, because his obligation to remove it ceased due to inability. If a person prays completely naked while having a garment that is more than a quarter pure, it is not permissible; he must wear that garment even if impure. If the pure part is less than a quarter, it is better to wear it than to pray naked. If he has no garment at all, praying standing (with bowing and prostration) is permissible, but praying sitting with gestures is recommended. 

The commentary explains the reasoning behind each ruling. The hair that hangs down from the head is disputed: some say it is not 'awrah, but the correct Hanafi view is that it is. The one who cannot remove impurity is excused because he did his best. In choosing between praying naked or in an impure garment, both are equally prohibited under normal circumstances, but covering is better since it is less severe. For the one with no garment, standing is valid but recommended to sit and gesture because covering the 'awrah is more important than performing the pillars with full movement. 

Additional notes clarify that 'testicles' means the two testes, and that inability includes both actual lack of water and fear of harm from using it. Also, looking at the hair of a non-Muslim woman is not prohibited according to some views, though the general rule for Muslim women is strict.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā): Gestures made with head or body to substitute for bowing and prostration when unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is praying sitting with gestures considered better than praying standing for a person without a garment?
A) Because sitting is more comfortable
B) Because covering the 'awrah is more important than performing the pillars perfectly
C) Because standing without clothes is forbidden
D) Because gestures replace all pillars

Key Takeaway
Without a garment, both standing and sitting with gestures are valid, but sitting is better because covering the 'awrah takes priority over perfect pillars.

Salah — Prayer

The Qibla Concession for Fear and Inability
Ruling on facing the qibla for one in fear or unable, with conditions for taharrī and an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qibla for one who is unable or fearful, and identify when taharrī is permissible and when it is not.

Core Idea
If you cannot face the qibla, face what you can; if you don't know it, strive to find it.

Facing the qibla is a key condition for prayer, but what if you are unable due to fear, illness, or being on a moving animal? The Hanafi school provides a concession: you face the direction within your ability. This lesson unpacks that ruling, including when you must perform taharrī (striving to determine the direction) and when you may not, as well as an internal debate about the mode of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the underlying principle
Grasp the maxim 'obligation is according to capacity' (al-taklif bihasb al-taqa). This principle from the Quran (2:115) licenses the concession.
The verse 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' is cited.
2
Understand the primary ruling
The ruling: if a person fears an enemy or beast, is ill, or cannot dismount, he prays facing whatever direction he can manage. The condition of facing the exact Kaaba is lifted.
The text mentions various scenarios: fear, illness, inability to dismount.
3
Learn the role of taharrī
If one does not know the qibla and has no one to ask, he must strive (taharrī) to determine the direction. This is an obligation, not a mere option.
Taharrī is defined as seeking the more appropriate direction through reasoning.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to al-Hidayah, it is not permissible to pray standing with gestures (i.e., without bowing and prostration). Other sources grant a choice between standing with gestures or sitting with proper bowing and prostration.
The mufta bihi is the choice view, as it accommodates greater difficulty.
5
Apply the conditions for taharrī
Taharrī is invalid if one can ask a knowledgeable person from the locality, or can use astronomical signs (e.g., stars) to determine the qibla. One must not seek a stranger to ask if not obligatory.
If the available person is not knowledgeable, taharrī remains permissible.

Source Text

وقبلة خائف الاستقبال جهة قدرته، فإن جهلها وعُدِمَ مَن يسأله تَحرَّى.
وبهذا أفتى ابن عباس، أخرجه عبد الرزاق. وظاهر ما في «الهداية»: أنه لا يجوز الإيماء قائماً، وذكر في «ملتقى البحار» و«البرهان» وشروح «المنية»: إنه مخير بين أن يصلي قائماً مومئاً، أو راكعاً وساجداً، وأن يصلي قاعداً مومئاً أو بركوع وسجود.

قوله: وقبله؛ لما فرغ من تفصيل متعلق بالشرط الرابع شرع فيما يتعلق بالشرط الخامس، مشيراً إلى أنه ليس المراد بالقبلة في القول السابق الكعبة خاصة. فمن خاف من إنسان عدو أو سبع إن صلى إلى جهة الكعبة، أو مرض مرضاً لا يمكن به أن يتوجه إليها، ولم يجد من يوجهه، ومن عجز عن النزول عن الدابة السائرة لخوف أو مرض أو طين أو نحو ذلك، صلّى إلى جهة قدر على التوجه إليها. كذا في «البرهان شرح مواهب الرحمن».

قوله: جهة قدرته؛ لأن التكليف بحسب الطاقة، فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ.

قوله: وعدم؛ أي لما لم يجد هناك من يسأله، ولا يجب عليه طلب من يسأله، ذكره العيني، فإن وجد لم يجز له التحري بشرط أن يكون الرجل من أهل ذلك الموضع عارفاً بالقبلة، فإن لم يكن كذلك فهو والمتحري سواء. كذا في «النهاية»، ولو كان في المفازة والسماء مصحية، وله علم بالاستدلال بالنجوم على القبلة لم يجز له التحري. كذا في «البحر».

قوله: تحرى؛ التحري طلب أحرى الأمرين وأولهما؛ أي وجب عليه أن...
And the qibla for one who fears [for his life] is to face the direction within his ability. If he does not know it and has no one to ask, he strives (to determine it). And this is the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, reported by Abd al-Razzaq. And the apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that it is not permissible to gesture while standing; but it is mentioned in Multaqa al-Bihar, al-Burhan, and the commentaries of al-Munyah that he has a choice between praying standing with gestures or with bowing and prostration, and between praying sitting with gestures or with bowing and prostration.

His statement: 'and the qibla' – when he finished detailing what relates to the fourth condition, he began what relates to the fifth condition, indicating that the intended meaning of qibla in the previous statement is not specifically the Kaaba. So whoever fears a human enemy or a beast if he prays toward the Kaaba, or has a sickness that prevents him from facing it, and finds no one to direct him, and whoever is unable to dismount from a moving animal due to fear, sickness, mud, or the like, prays toward a direction that he is able to face. Thus in al-Burhan Sharh Mawahib al-Rahman.

His statement: 'the direction within his ability' – because obligation is according to capacity. 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (Quran 2:115).

His statement: 'and he has no one' – meaning when he finds no one there to ask, and he is not obligated to seek someone to ask, as mentioned by al-Ayni. If he finds someone, it is not permissible for him to strive, provided that the person is from that locality and knowledgeable about the qibla; if not, then he and the one striving are equal. Thus in al-Nihayah. And if he is in the desert and the sky is clear, and he has knowledge of using the stars to determine the qibla, he is not permitted to strive. Thus in al-Bahr.

His statement: 'he strives' – Taharrī is to seek the more appropriate and the better of two things; meaning it is obligatory upon him to...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from the commentary discusses the condition of facing the qibla (direction of prayer) for someone who is unable to do so due to fear, illness, or inability. The ruling is that such a person prays toward whatever direction he is able to face. If he does not know the direction and has no one to ask, he must strive (taharrī) to determine it — that is, exert effort to deduce the most likely direction. This is based on the fatwa of Ibn Abbas, reported by Abd al-Razzaq. The text notes a point of disagreement: according to al-Hidayah, it is not permissible to pray standing with gestures (i.e., without proper bowing and prostration) for the one who cannot face the qibla? Actually the phrasing is a bit ambiguous. The passage then cites other sources saying he has a choice between standing with gestures or with bowing and prostration, and between sitting with gestures or with bowing and prostration. This indicates flexibility.

The commentary explains that the fifth condition of prayer (after the fourth being something else) is about qibla, and it clarifies that the qibla referenced is not necessarily the exact Kaaba for all situations; there is a concession for those who cannot face it. The proof is the Quranic verse: 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115).

Additionally, conditions for taharrī are given: One must not have access to someone knowledgeable about the qibla. If he can ask a reliable person, he must do so before resorting to personal reasoning. If he is in the desert and can use the stars to determine the direction, he must do that rather than taharrī (since that is more accurate). The passage ends with a definition of taharrī as seeking the more appropriate and better of two things, implying that it is obligatory to strive to find the correct direction.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taḥarrī): The effort to determine the correct direction of the qibla through reasoning and signs when certain knowledge is unavailable.
جهة قدرته (jihata qudratihi): The direction that a person is able to face, given his circumstances (fear, illness, inability to move). This is the required direction for his prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is in a desert and the sky is clear, and he knows how to determine the qibla using stars, but he also has a general idea of the direction by personal reasoning (taharrī), which should he follow?
A) He should use taharrī because it is easier.
B) He must use his knowledge of stars to determine the qibla; taharrī is not allowed.
C) He can choose either method.
D) He should combine both to be safe.

Key Takeaway
When unable to face the qibla, the obligation reduces to facing the direction within one's ability; if the direction is unknown and no reliable method exists, taharrī becomes obligatory.

Salah — Prayer

Prayer When Unable to Face the Qiblah: Direction of Ability
Explains the ruling for one who cannot face qiblah due to fear or incapacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for one who cannot face the qiblah, including the conditions for ijtihad, the option of gestures, and the consequences of error.

Core Idea
When facing the Ka'bah is impossible, the qiblah becomes the direction you can manage — and your prayer is valid without repetition.

Facing the qiblah is a key condition for prayer, but what if you are in danger, ill, or lost? The Hanafi school provides a detailed concession based on the principle of obligation according to ability. In this lesson, we examine the ruling from Umdat al-Ri'ayah that the qiblah shifts to 'the direction of one's ability' and the practical options available, including an intra-school difference on gestures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse
Determine which scenarios trigger the concession: fear of enemy/beast, illness preventing orientation, inability to dismount from a moving mount, or ignorance of the qiblah.
The text lists these as valid reasons to pray without facing the Ka'bah.
2
State the ruling
The person must pray to whatever direction he is able to face (jihat qudratihi). If ignorant, he must perform ijtihad (taharrī) to determine the most likely direction.
The ruling is based on Quran 2:115: 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.'
3
Understand the conditions for ijtihad
Ijtihad is only allowed when one cannot determine the qiblah through certainty. If a knowledgeable person is available, one must ask. If stars are visible and one can deduce, ijtihad is not permitted.
The text emphasizes that knowledge overrides ijtihad.
4
Examine the manner of prayer
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Hidayah suggests standing with gestures is not allowed, while other sources (Multaqa al-Bihar, al-Burhan) give a choice of four options: standing with gestures, standing with bowing/prostration, sitting with gestures, or sitting with bowing/prostration.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that the person is free to choose among these.
5
Consequences of error
If after prayer one realizes he faced the wrong direction, no repetition is required. If during prayer he learns the correct direction, he must turn to it and continue. The same applies if his ijtihad changes during prayer.
The basis is the hadith of the Companions who were not ordered to repeat, and the story of the change of qiblah.

Source Text

عمدة الرعاية على شرح الوقاية

ولم يعد إن أخطأ، وإن عَلِمَ به مصلياً، أو تحول رأيه إلى جهة أخرى استدار ولم يعد إن أخطأ، وإن علم به مصلّياً ، أو تحول رأيه إلى جهة أخرى استدار) يتحرى بقلبه، فيصلي إلى جهة مالَ إليها ظنه ؛ لقوله : ﴿ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَتَمَ وَجْهُ الله ، نزلت في مثل هذه الصورة، كما أخرجه الترمذي)، والكلام في هذا المقام طويل، مبسوط في «السعاية»(۳).

(۱) قوله : ولم يعد إن أخطأ؛ يعني إذا صلّى إلى جهة تحرِّيهِ وعَلِمَ بعد ذلك أنّ القبلة كانت غيرها لا تجب عليه الإعادة ؛ لأنَّ الواجب حين الجهل هو التوجه إلى جهة التحري ، وقد فعل، وقد ثبت أنّ بعض الصحابة الله اشتبهت عليهم القبلة فصلى كل منهم إلى جهة تحريه ، فلما أصبحوا علموا أنهم صلّوا إلى غير القبلة، فذكروا ذلك للنبي ، فلم يأمرهم بالإعادة ) ، أخرجه الترمذي والحاكم وأبو نعيم وغيرهم، وأسانيدهم لهذه القصة وإن كانت ضعيفة لكنه تأيد ذلك بإجماع الأمة. [٢]قوله : وإن علم ؛ أي إن علم بخطئه في الصلاة، بأن زالت الظلمة واستنارت الكواكب فعرف جهة الكعبة، أو أخبره مخبر عالم بهما في الصلاة يجب عليه أن يستدير في الصلاة ويصلي ما بقي إلى جهة الكعبة، ولا يجب عليه أن يستأنف ؛ لأنَّ المفروض عند العجز والجهل هو جهة التحري ، وقد فعل، وحين عرف جهتها تبدل فرضها، فيلزم عليه التوجه إليها. والأصل فيه وفي مسألة تحوّل الرأي قصَّةُ استدارة الصحابة له حين نسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس، فإنّه روي أنه حين نزلَ القرآنُ بافتراض التوجه إلى الكعبة ونسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس وصل خبره إلى جمع من الصحابة وهم في الصلاة،

(۲) فعن عامر بن ربيعة له قال : «كنا مع النبي الله في سفر في ليلة مظلمة فلم ندر أين القبلة فصلى كل رجل منا على حياله فلما أصبحنا ذكرنا ذلك للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فنزل وَاللَّهِ الْمُشْرِقُ وَالْمَغْرِبُ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَثَمَّ وَجْهُ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللهَ وَاسِعُ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ (البقرة : ١١٥» في «سنن الترمذي»(٢ : ١٧٦).

The book of prayer/conditions of prayer. And the qiblah of one who fears (is in danger) is the direction of his ability. If he is ignorant of it and there is no one to ask, he performs ijtihad (taharrī). And with this Ibn Abbas gave a fatwa, as recorded by Abd al-Razzaq. And the apparent meaning in al-Hidayah is that nodding while standing is not permissible. And it is mentioned in Multaqa al-Bihar, al-Burhan, and the commentaries of al-Munyah that he is given a choice between praying standing and nodding, or bowing and prostrating, and between praying sitting and nodding or with bowing and prostrating. [Commentary:] His saying: 'and the qiblah'; when he finished detailing what pertains to the fourth condition, he began what pertains to the fifth condition, indicating that what is meant by qiblah in the previous statement is not specifically the Ka'bah. So whoever fears a human enemy or a beast if he prays towards the Ka'bah, or is ill such that he cannot face it, and does not find someone to guide him, and whoever is unable to dismount from a moving mount due to fear, illness, mud, or the like, prays towards whatever direction he is able to face. Thus in al-Burhan Sharh Mawahib al-Rahman. (2) His saying: 'direction of his ability'; because obligation is according to ability, 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115). [3] His saying: 'and he does not have'; i.e. when he does not find anyone to ask, and it is not obligatory for him to seek someone to ask, as mentioned by al-Ayni. If he does find someone, ijtihad is not permissible for him, provided that the person is from that locality and knows the qiblah. If he is not such, then he and the one performing ijtihad are equal. Thus in al-Nihayah. And if he is in the desert and the sky is clear, and he has knowledge of deducing the qiblah by the stars, then ijtihad is not permissible for him. Thus in al-Bahr. (4) His saying: 'performs ijtihad'; taharrī is seeking the more appropriate or preferable of two matters; i.e. it is obligatory upon him to... [Footnote references and hadith narrations follow.] ... And he does not repeat if he erred. And if he becomes aware while praying, or his opinion changes to another direction, he turns around. [Commentary:] His saying: 'and he does not repeat if he erred'; meaning if he prayed towards the direction of his ijtihad and afterwards knew that the qiblah was other than it, repetition is not obligatory, because the obligation at the time of ignorance was to face the direction of ijtihad, and he has done that. And it is established that some of the Companions were uncertain about the qiblah and each prayed towards his ijtihad, and when morning came they knew they had prayed to other than the qiblah, and they mentioned that to the Prophet, and he did not order them to repeat. Recorded by al-Tirmidhi, al-Hakim, Abu Nu'aym, and others, and although their chains for this story are weak, it is supported by the consensus of the Ummah. [2] His saying: 'and if he knows'; i.e. if he knows his error during the prayer, such as when darkness lifts and the stars become clear so he knows the direction of the Ka'bah, or an informant who knows informs him about it during the prayer, then he must turn around in the prayer and pray the remainder towards the Ka'bah, and he is not required to start over, because the obligatory at the time of incapacity and ignorance was the direction of ijtihad, and he has done that, and when he knew its direction, his obligation changed, so it is incumbent upon him to face it. The basis for this and for the issue of change of opinion is the story of the Companions turning around when the abrogation of facing Bayt al-Maqdis occurred. It is narrated that when the Quran was revealed obligating facing the Ka'bah and abrogating facing Bayt al-Maqdis, the news reached a group of the Companions while they were in prayer.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from Umdat al-Ri'ayah discusses the ruling on prayer for someone unable to face the qiblah due to fear, illness, or lack of means. It is a ruling with proof, expanding on a matn from al-Wiqayah. The core ruling: if one fears an enemy or beast, is ill, or cannot dismount from a moving animal, he prays to whatever direction he can manage, because obligation is according to ability. The verse 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' (2:115) supports this. If one is ignorant of the qiblah and has no one to ask, he must perform ijtihad (taharrī) to determine the direction. If one finds a knowledgeable person, he must ask and cannot perform ijtihad. If he can deduce the qiblah via stars, ijtihad is not allowed because that knowledge is superior. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi difference: in al-Hidayah, it appears that nodding while standing (without bowing/prostrating) is not allowed, but other sources like Multaqa al-Bihar and al-Burhan state that the person has a choice between standing with gestures or with actual bowing and prostrating, and similarly sitting with gestures or with bowing and prostrating. This indicates flexibility in the school for those with valid excuses. Regarding error: if after prayer one realizes he faced the wrong direction, no repetition is required, based on the hadith of the Companions who did this and were not ordered to repeat. This is supported by consensus. However, if during the prayer he becomes aware of the correct direction, he must turn to it and continue, without restarting. Similarly, if his ijtihad changes during prayer, he turns to the new direction. The story of the Companions turning when the qiblah was changed from Jerusalem to the Ka'bah is cited as precedent. The ruling hinges on the fact that the obligation at the time of ignorance is the direction of ijtihad, but once true knowledge arrives, the obligation becomes the actual qiblah. This passage is critical for understanding the Hanafi approach to necessity and ijtihad in ritual prayer.

Key Terms
تحري (taHarrī (taharrī)): The act of exerting oneself to determine the correct direction of the qiblah when ignorant, by forming an opinion based on available signs.
جهة قدرته (jihat qudratihi): The direction one is able to face, as opposed to the actual direction of the Ka'bah, due to necessity or incapacity.
إيماء (imā'): Gesturing with the head or body instead of actual bowing (ruku) and prostration (sujud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling if a person performs ijtihad (taharrī) for the qiblah, prays, and later discovers he faced the wrong direction?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) He does not need to repeat the prayer because his ijtihad was valid.
C) He must repeat only if he was negligent in his ijtihad.
D) He must make up the prayer at a later time.

Key Takeaway
When facing the exact qiblah is impossible, the Hanafi school allows prayer to the direction of ability or ijtihad, with no repetition if mistaken, and provides flexible options for posture.

Salah — Prayer

The Validity of Prayer Performed with Ijtihad for Qibla
Ruling and commentary on ijtihad for qibla with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer performed with ijtihad for qibla, and apply it to cases of discovering error before, during, or after the prayer.

Core Idea
A prayer performed with valid ijtihad is valid even if the qibla was wrong — no repetition, because the obligation was fulfilled by the ijtihad.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi principle regarding the obligation of facing the qibla when its direction is uncertain. Through the guidance of the Prophet ﷺ and the practice of the Companions, we learn that the validity of prayer depends on sincere effort (ijtihad) rather than absolute accuracy. The source passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands upon a base text ruling, clarifying the scenarios of error and the weight of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
When a person performs ijtihad to determine qibla, prays to that direction, and later discovers it was wrong, the prayer is valid and need not be repeated. This applies whether the error is discovered after the prayer or during it (with the obligation to turn).
The key principle: the obligation when ignorant is to face the direction of ijtihad.
2
Understand the basis of the ruling
The evidence is from the hadith of companions who prayed in a dark night to different directions and were not ordered to repeat. Although the chain is weak, the ruling is confirmed by ijma'. The Hanafi position relies on the Prophet's ﷺ omission as a proof of validity.
The story of the qibla change from Jerusalem to Mecca also supports turning mid-prayer without restart.
3
Distinguish between discovering error after prayer vs. during prayer
If error is known after prayer, no qada. If known during prayer (e.g., seeing stars or being told by a reliable person), one must immediately turn to the correct qibla and continue the remaining prayer. This is analogous to the Companions receiving news of qibla change mid-prayer.
Turning does not invalidate the prayer; it is a necessary adjustment.
4
Specify that 'opinion' means predominant opinion
The commentary clarifies that the 'opinion' in the matn refers to ghalabat al-zann (preponderant thought), not any weak or hesitant opinion. Only when one has a dominant belief about the qibla direction is the ruling applicable.
Hesitation or weak opinion does not constitute valid ijtihad for this purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يعد إن أخطأ، وإن عَلِمَ به مصلياً، أو تحول رأيه إلى جهة أخرى استدار ولم يعد إن أخطأ، وإن علم به مصلّياً ، أو تحول رأيه إلى جهة أخرى استدار) يتحرى بقلبه، فيصلي إلى جهة مالَ إليها ظنه ؛ لقوله : ﴿ فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَتَمَ وَجْهُ الله ، نزلت في مثل هذه الصورة، كما أخرجه الترمذي)، والكلام في هذا المقام طويل، مبسوط في «السعاية»(۳). (1) (۱) قوله : ولم يعد إن أخطأ؛ يعني إذا صلّى إلى جهة تحرِّيهِ وعَلِمَ بعد ذلك أنّ القبلة كانت غيرها لا تجب عليه الإعادة ؛ لأنَّ الواجب حين الجهل هو التوجه إلى جهة التحري ، وقد فعل، وقد ثبت أنّ بعض الصحابة الله اشتبهت عليهم القبلة فصلى كل منهم إلى جهة تحريه ، فلما أصبحوا علموا أنهم صلّوا إلى غير القبلة، فذكروا ذلك للنبي ، فلم يأمرهم بالإعادة ) ، أخرجه الترمذي والحاكم وأبو نعيم وغيرهم، وأسانيدهم لهذه القصة وإن كانت ضعيفة لكنه تأيد ذلك بإجماع الأمة. [٢]قوله : وإن علم ؛ أي إن علم بخطئه في الصلاة، بأن زالت الظلمة واستنارت الكواكب فعرف جهة الكعبة، أو أخبره مخبر عالم بهما في الصلاة يجب عليه أن يستدير في الصلاة ويصلي ما بقي إلى جهة الكعبة، ولا يجب عليه أن يستأنف ؛ لأنَّ المفروض عند العجز والجهل هو جهة التحري ، وقد فعل، وحين عرف جهتها تبدل فرضها، فيلزم عليه التوجه إليها. والأصل فيه وفي مسألة تحوّل الرأي قصَّةُ استدارة الصحابة له حين نسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس، فإنّه روي أنه حين نزلَ القرآنُ بافتراض التوجه إلى الكعبة ونسخ التوجه إلى بيت المقدس وصل خبره إلى جمع من الصحابة وهم في الصلاة، فاستداروا فيها من جهة الشام إلى جهة مكة، وأتموا ما بقي)، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم وأصحاب السنن على ما بسطناه في «السعاية»، فإن تحول الرأي والعلم بعد الجهل مشابه لوصول خبر النسخ. (۱) قوله : أو تحول غلبه ظنّه ؛ أشار به إلى أنّ المراد بالرأي في المتن الرأي الغالب لا مطلق الرأي ، إذ لا اعتبار للرأي الضعيف ولا للمتردد في باب التوجه. (۲) قوله : وهو في الصلاة ؛ قيد به ؛ لأنه لو تحول رأيه بعد الصلاة لم يعد ما مضى، كما في صورة ظهور الخطأ.
And he does not repeat if he erred, and if he knows during prayer, or his opinion changes to another direction, he turns around and does not repeat if he erred, and if he knows during prayer, or his opinion changes to another direction, he turns around. He performs ijtihad with his heart, and prays towards the direction his thought inclines to; due to His saying: 'So wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah.' It was revealed in such a situation, as narrated by al-Tirmidhi. The discussion on this topic is lengthy, detailed in al-Si'aya. (1) His saying: 'And he does not repeat if he erred' means if he prayed towards the direction of his ijtihad and later knows that the qibla was other than it, repeating is not obligatory; because the obligatory when ignorant is to face the direction of ijtihad, and he has done so. And it is established that some Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) were confused about the qibla, so each prayed towards his own direction of ijtihad. When morning came, they knew they had prayed to other than the qibla, and they mentioned that to the Prophet, and he did not order them to repeat. Reported by al-Tirmidhi, al-Hakim, Abu Nu'aym and others. Their chains for this story are weak, but it is supported by the consensus of the Ummah. [2] His saying: 'And if he knows' means if he knows his error during prayer, such as when darkness clears and stars shine so he knows the direction of the Ka'bah, or a knowledgeable informant tells him about it during prayer, he must turn in the prayer and pray what remains towards the Ka'bah, and he must not restart; because the prescribed when incapable and ignorant is the direction of ijtihad, and he has done it. When he knows its direction, his duty changes, so he must face it. The basis for this and for the issue of change of opinion is the story of the Companions turning when the direction was abrogated from Jerusalem, for it is narrated that when the Quran was revealed obligating facing the Ka'bah and abrogating facing Jerusalem, the news reached a group of Companions while they were in prayer, so they turned from the direction of Syria to the direction of Mecca and completed what remained. Reported by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and the authors of the Sunan as we have detailed in al-Si'aya. So change of opinion and knowledge after ignorance resembles the arrival of abrogation news. (1) His saying: 'or if his predominant opinion changes' indicates that what is meant by 'opinion' in the text is the dominant opinion, not absolute opinion, because weak opinion or hesitation is not considered in matters of direction. (2) His saying: 'while he is in prayer' is a restriction; because if his opinion changes after the prayer, he does not repeat what has passed, as in the case of discovering error.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding ijtihad for qibla when one is uncertain. It opens by stating the key ruling: if a person performs ijtihad and prays, but later discovers they were facing the wrong direction, their prayer is valid and need not be repeated. This is because when one is unable to determine the correct qibla, the obligation is to face whichever direction one's ijtihad leads to, and that obligation has been fulfilled. The proof is a well-known hadith from the Companions who were confused about qibla in a dark night, prayed according to their ijtihad, and later were not ordered to repeat by the Prophet ﷺ. Although the chain of this particular hadith is weak, the ruling is confirmed by Ijma' (consensus). The commentary then addresses a second scenario: if during the prayer, the person realizes their error (e.g., by seeing the stars clearly or being informed by a reliable person), they must immediately turn towards the correct qibla and continue the remaining portion of the prayer; they do not need to start over. This is derived from the story of the Companions when the qibla was changed from Jerusalem to Mecca during prayer; they turned mid-prayer without restarting. The shift in knowledge or opinion during prayer is analogous to receiving news of abrogation. Finally, the commentary clarifies that the 'opinion' in the text refers to the dominant or preponderant opinion (غلبة الظن), not any fleeting thought or hesitation, as weak opinions have no weight in determining the qibla.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): The act of exerting effort to determine the qibla direction when it is unknown, using signs or ijtihad.
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-ẓann): Preponderant opinion or dominant thought after ijtihad, which is the basis for determining qibla direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person performs ijtihad for qibla and prays. During the prayer, he discovers the correct direction and turns to face it. He completes the prayer. Later, he finds his original ijtihad was also somewhat off. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He must repeat the entire prayer because he did not face the correct qibla from the start.
B) The prayer is valid because he turned when he knew the correct direction and continued.
C) He must repeat only the part before turning because it was invalid.
D) The prayer is invalid because his ijtihad was wrong.

Key Takeaway
Sincere ijtihad for qibla fulfills the obligation, making the prayer valid regardless of absolute accuracy, in line with the Hanafi principle of ease.

Ruling on Prayer Without Ijtihad and Congregational Following in Qibla Doubt
Ruling on ijtihad omission and congregational following in qibla doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer without ijtihad is invalid even if the qibla is hit, and explain the congregational conditions when followers have different ijtihad directions.

Core Idea
Prayer without ijtihad is invalid because ijtihad itself is the required condition.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya expands on two important scenarios: the invalidity of starting prayer without ijtihad, and the permissibility of a congregation where each follower has performed ijtihad individually. Understanding these rulings requires grasping the Hanafi principle that the obligated direction is the one arrived at through ijtihad, not the actual qibla.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating the ruling on starting prayer without ijtihad (taharrī): it is not permissible (لَمْ يَجُزْ), even if the person coincidentally faces the correct qibla. This establishes that ijtihad is a necessary condition.
2
Analyze the reasoning (dalil)
The text provides the reasoning: 'because his qibla is the direction of his ijtihad, and it did not exist.' The obligation is to perform ijtihad, not merely to face a physical direction. The hadith of the Companions turning during prayer (from Syria to Mecca) is cited as a precedent.
The hadith is reported by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Apply to the congregational scenario
If followers each perform ijtihad for every direction without knowing the imam's direction, their prayer is valid. However, if a follower knows the imam's direction is wrong or precedes the imam, it is not permissible.
The condition is that the follower must be unaware of the imam's error.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi affirmation
Later authorities like Ibn Humam and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha affirm the absolute invalidity of prayer without ijtihad, even if the correct qibla is hit. They stress that ijtihad itself is wajib.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Some scholars might consider the prayer valid if the qibla is hit without ijtihad. The Hanafi position requires repetition.
The practical difference is whether the prayer must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شرع بلا تحر لم يجز، وإن أصاب) ؛ لأن قبلته جهة تحريه ، ولم يوجد، فإن تحروا كل جهة بلا علم حال إمامهم، وهم خلفَه جازَ، لا لمن عَلِمَ حاله ، أو تقدمه ) فاستداروا فيها من جهة الشام إلى جهة مكة، وأتموا ما بقي)، أخرجه البخاري ومسلم وأصحاب السنن على ما بسطناه في «السعاية»، فإن تحول الرأي والعلم بعد الجهل مشابه لوصول خبر النسخ. (۳) قوله : لأن قبلته ... الخ ؛ ظاهر هذا التعليل يقتضي عدم الجواز مطلقاً، سواء علم بالإصابة في الصلاة أو بعدها ، وكذا ظاهر كلام المصنف ، وإن أصاب، وظاهر قول الشارح في «النقاية» لم يعد مخطئ تحرّى ، بل مصيب لم يتحر، وإليه مالَ ابنُ الهمام في بعض تحريراته. وقال تلميذه قاسم ابنُ قُطلُوبُغا في رسالتِهِ «الفوائدِ الجلة في اشتباه القبلة» بعد نقل هذه العبارات، وعبارة «مختارات النوازل» لصاحب الهداية» : « «لو صلّى بلا تحر لترك ما هو الواجب عليه، وهو التحرّي، وإن أصاب». انتهى. المفهوم من هذه العباراتِ ما
And if he starts prayer without ijtihad, it is not permissible even if he hits [the qibla]; because his qibla is the direction of his ijtihad, and it did not exist. If they perform ijtihad for every direction without knowing the situation of their imam while they are behind him, it is permissible, but not for one who knows his situation or precedes him. They turned from the direction of Syria to the direction of Mecca and completed what remained. Reported by al-Bukhari and Muslim and the authors of the Sunan as we have detailed in al-Si'aya. So change of opinion and knowledge after ignorance resembles the arrival of abrogation news. (3) His saying: 'because his qibla...' the apparent meaning of this reasoning necessitates absolute impermissibility, whether he knows the correct direction during prayer or after it, and similarly the apparent speech of the author, 'even if he hits,' and the apparent statement of the commentator in al-Niqaya: 'One who erred with ijtihad does not repeat, but one who hit correctly without ijtihad repeats' and Ibn Humam inclined to this in some of his writings. His student Qasim ibn Qutlubugha said in his treatise 'al-Fawa'id al-Jillah fi Ishtibah al-Qiblah' after quoting these statements and the statement of 'Mukhtarat al-Nawazil' by the author of al-Hidayah: 'If he prays without ijtihad, he has abandoned what is obligatory upon him, which is ijtihad, even if he hits the qibla.' End. What is understood from these statements is...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on qibla ijtihad, presenting two additional rulings. First, if a person begins his prayer without performing ijtihad (taharrī), the prayer is invalid even if he coincidentally faces the correct direction. The reasoning is that the obligated direction is not the actual qibla but the direction arrived at through ijtihad; since no ijtihad was performed, the prayer is not valid. This is a fundamental Hanafi principle: the obligation when direction is unknown is to perform ijtihad, and fulfilling the actual qibla without ijtihad does not suffice. Second, the passage addresses a congregational scenario: if the followers each perform ijtihad individually and face different directions, but they follow an imam whose direction they do not know, their prayer is valid. However, if a follower knows that the imam is facing the wrong direction, he cannot follow him; similarly, if the follower is ahead of the imam (in terms of knowledge or precedence), it is not allowed. The proof for the general principle of turning during prayer is again drawn from the Companions' turning from Jerusalem to Mecca upon receiving the abrogation news. The commentary then notes a subtle point: there is an apparent contradiction in some statements about whether one who prays without ijtihad but hits the qibla is excused. Some later scholars like Ibn Humam and Qasim ibn Qutlubugha clarify that the prayer is invalid because the obligatory act of ijtihad was omitted. The practical takeaway is that ijtihad is a wajib step that cannot be skipped, and the congregation's prayer is valid only if the followers are unaware of the imam's error.

Key Terms
شرع بلا تحر (shara'a bi-la tahrīr): Beginning the prayer without having performed ijtihad to determine the qibla.
جهة تحريه (jihhat tahrīhī): The direction one arrives at through ijtihad, which legally becomes one's qibla for that prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is unsure of the qibla but does not perform ijtihad; he prays facing a direction and later finds out that it was indeed the correct qibla. What is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is valid because he faced the correct qibla.
B) The prayer is invalid because he omitted the obligatory ijtihad.
C) The prayer is valid but he should repeat it as a precaution.
D) The prayer is makruh but still valid.

Key Takeaway
Starting prayer without ijtihad invalidates the prayer even if the correct qibla is accidentally faced, because ijtihad itself is a required condition (wajib).

Prayer Without Taharri and the Principle of Building
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building prayer after discovering correct qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer without taharri, explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the principle that building the strong upon the weak is impermissible.

Core Idea
Prayer without taharri is invalid even if one hits the qibla; certainty cannot be built upon uncertainty.

This lesson examines a key intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of prayer performed without the effort to determine the qibla direction (taharri). When a person later discovers he was facing the correct direction, the imams disagree on whether he may continue building on the part already prayed or must restart. The underlying legal principle is the prohibition of building a strong evidentiary state (certainty) upon a weak one (uncertainty). We will explore the arguments and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and General Ruling
The passage begins by establishing that beginning prayer without taharri is invalid (la yajuz), even if one happens to face the correct qibla. Recognize that this is the default Hanafi position based on the obligation of taharri.
Taharri is wajib when the qibla is ambiguous; it is a condition for prayer.
2
Locate the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
When a person prays without taharri and learns during the prayer that he was facing the correct qibla, the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say he must start over; Abu Yusuf says he may build upon the part already prayed. Identify the exact point of disagreement.
The dispute hinges on the permissibility of bina' al-qawi 'ala al-da'if.
3
Trace Each Argument's Proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad use qiyas: cases like praying in a najis garment or without wudu where the belief of invalidity prevents building. They argue that uncertainty (shakk) is also a weak basis. Abu Yusuf argues that the obligation (facing the Kaaba) is fulfilled in reality, so building is allowed.
The hadith about companions turning from Jerusalem to Mecca during prayer involved those who had already performed taharri.
4
Apply the Principle of Bina' al-Qawi 'ala al-Da'if
Understand that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the state of knowledge (certainty) is stronger than the prior uncertainty. Since the earlier part of the prayer was performed in a state of uncertainty, it cannot be a valid foundation for the subsequent certain part.
This usuli principle is core to the Hanafi school in many areas of fiqh.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and the Mufta Bihi
The practical consequence: according to the relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the person must restart the prayer from the beginning. According to Abu Yusuf, he may continue. The commentary indicates that the position of the two is preferred.
If he realizes after finishing, all agree no repetition is required.

And if he begins [prayer] without taharri, it is not valid, even if he hit [the qibla]. However, if they all performed taharri [facing] each direction without knowledge of the state of their imam, and they are behind him, it is valid — not for one who knows his state or that he preceded [them]. That is, if he knows the error during prayer or his predominant opinion shifts to another direction while he is in prayer, he turns around. (And if he begins without taharri, it is not valid, even if he hit) because his qibla is the direction of his taharri, and it was not found. Then if they all perform taharri [in] each direction without knowledge of the state of their imam, and they are behind him, it is valid — not for one who knows his state or that he preceded [them]. So they turned around in it from the direction of Syria to the direction of Mecca, and completed what remained. This is reported by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and the authors of the Sunan as we have detailed in 'al-Si'ayah'. Indeed, the change of opinion and knowledge after ignorance resembles the arrival of the news of abrogation. And in 'Ghuniyat al-Mustamli': 'If he begins the prayer without taharri, it is not valid, even if he actually hit [the qibla], because the qibla at that time was the direction of taharri, and it was not found, so his prayer is invalid. This is if he did not know whether he hit or missed. If he knows that he hit, then if he knows during the prayer that he hit, he should start over according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), because the state of knowledge is stronger than what preceded it, and building the strong upon the weak is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, he may build, because the obligation is facing the Kaaba, and it has been fulfilled, so what he has prayed is valid. If he knows the hitting after finishing, there is no repetition by agreement. And the distinction for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) between this issue and the case where he performed taharri and then violated the direction of his taharri is that what is prescribed for something else requires its occurrence absolutely, not its occurrence intentionally, like hastening to Friday prayer, but with the absence of belief in invalidity and absence of evidence for it, and that exists in the case of lack of taharri, unlike that case (where he violated his taharri), because violating his direction of taharri necessitated the invalidity of his prayer in his belief, so it became like one who prays in a garment he considers najis, then it becomes clear it is pure, or one who prays thinking he is hadath, then it becomes clear he had wudu, or one who prays the obligatory prayer thinking the time had not entered, then it becomes clear it had entered — in all this it is not valid. As for the case of lack of taharri, he did not believe in invalidity there, rather he was hesitating between validity and non-validity. So when it appears that he hit after completing the prayer, one of the two possibilities is removed and the other is established, so his prayer is valid.'
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a person who begins prayer without performing taharri (i.e., exerting effort to determine the qibla direction) when the qibla is ambiguous. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) on one side, and Abu Yusuf on the other. The passage first states the general ruling: if one prays without taharri, the prayer is invalid even if he happens to face the correct direction. This is because the qibla for him is the direction he would have arrived at through taharri, and since he did not perform taharri, that direction is absent. The text then cites a hadith about the companions turning from Jerusalem to Mecca during prayer upon learning of the change in qibla. It distinguishes that case: they had already performed taharri (they were facing Jerusalem based on the previous command). The text then details the scenario where one prays without taharri and later realizes during the prayer that he was actually facing the correct qibla. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), he must restart the prayer because the state of certainty is stronger than the previous uncertain state; one cannot build the strong on the weak. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that the obligation is facing the Kaaba, which has been achieved, so he may build upon the part already prayed; his prayer is valid. If he realizes after completing the prayer, all agree there is no repetition. The passage also explains the rationale for the difference between this case and a case where one performed taharri but then turned away from that direction: in the latter, the person believes his prayer is invalid due to violating his own taharri, analogous to praying in a garment he thinks is impure, etc. In the no-taharri case, the person was merely uncertain; when it becomes clear he was correct, the uncertainty is resolved and the prayer is valid.

Key Terms
تحري (taḥarrī): Exerting effort to determine the direction of the qibla when it is ambiguous, based on signs and personal reasoning.
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, which must be faced during prayer.
بناء القوي على الضعيف (binā' al-qawī 'alā al-ḍa'īf): Building a stronger evidentiary state (e.g., certainty) upon a weaker one (e.g., uncertainty) — a principle that is impermissible in the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Continue building on the part already prayed.
B) Restart the prayer from the beginning.
C) Complete the prayer and repeat it later.
D) He does not need to do anything; the prayer is valid.

Key Takeaway
Prayer without taharri when the qibla is ambiguous is invalid even if one faces the correct direction; if one discovers the correct direction during prayer, the relied-upon view is that he must restart, as certainty cannot be built upon uncertainty.

Prayer Without Taharri: Invalid Even If Qibla Correct After Completion
Establishes relied-upon ruling on prayer without taharri after completion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for one who prays without taharri and later discovers the correct qibla after completion, and explain the reasoning and its reliance.

Core Idea
Prayer without taharri is invalid even if qibla was correct — taharri is the required determinant.

This passage establishes the relied-upon (mu'tamad) Hanafi position: if you pray without performing taharri when the qibla is ambiguous, and only realize after completing the prayer that you were facing the correct direction, your prayer is invalid and must be repeated. The text also clarifies a misinterpretation that would limit this ruling to cases where knowledge occurs during the prayer. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly applying qibla-related obligations in daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the moment of knowledge
Consider the scenario: a person for whom the qibla is unclear prays without taharri. He only learns after completing the prayer that he was facing the correct direction. What is the ruling?
Taharri is wajib when qibla is unknown and no one to ask.
2
State the relied-upon ruling
The text declares that his prayer is not valid ('lam tajuz salatuhu') and that this is the relied-upon position ('wa 'alayhi al-i'timad'). Thus, the prayer must be repeated.
This applies even though he happened to hit the correct qibla.
3
Understand the basis of the ruling
The underlying principle: without taharri, the direction of the Ka'bah as an absolute direction is not the required qibla for his prayer. Rather, the qibla for his prayer must be determined by taharri. Hence, the prayer is fundamentally defective.
If he had performed taharri and erred, he would not repeat; but here the condition of taharri is absent.
4
Recognize the rejected misinterpretation
Some attempted to limit the ruling to cases where knowledge occurred during prayer, citing al-Wiqayah. The commentator firmly rejects this, showing that al-Wiqayah's wording does not support that interpretation, and such a reading would lead to unnecessary repetition.
This highlights the importance of precise textual understanding in Hanafi scholarship.
5
Confirm the authoritative status
The phrase 'wa 'alayhi al-i'timad' marks this as the mufta bihi (operative ruling) for fatwa. Later sources like al-Haskafi and Ibn Abidin uphold this position.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin (later Hanafi jurists).

It is the apparent one, and it is that whoever the qibla is ambiguous to him and he prayed without taharri, then after completion he knew that he had hit [the correct direction], his prayer is not valid, and upon it is the reliance. And it was said: These expressions are only for when he began without taharri, then knew during his prayer that he hit; because the author of al-Wiqayah said before that: 'If he is ignorant of it and does not find anyone to ask, he performs taharri and does not repeat if he errs, and if he knows while praying or his opinion changes to another, he turns [around].' I said: In the phrase of al-Wiqayah there is no evidence for this intended meaning by any indication whatsoever, and if the supposition of the issue were about one who knows of hitting during the prayer, then repetition would be necessary, and that is far from the proof of the Shari'ah. Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer performed without taharri when one later discovers that he was facing the correct qibla. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that if the discovery occurs after completion, the prayer is invalid. The text first presents this ruling and then discusses a possible interpretation of al-Wiqayah that would limit the ruling to cases where knowledge occurs during prayer, but the author dismisses this. Then from Ghuniyat al-Mustamli, the detailed positions are given: without taharri, the prayer is invalid even if correct, because the qibla for the prayer is the direction determined by taharri. If one knows during the prayer, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he must restart; Abu Yusuf alone allows building upon the prayer already performed. After completion, all agree no repetition. The Sahibayn provide a distinction: when one violates his own taharri, he believes his prayer is invalid, so later knowledge doesn't help—similar to cases of najis garment or missed time. In the case of no taharri, he was doubtful, so when correctness is confirmed, the prayer is valid. This reasoning also rebuts an objection by Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms
تحر (taharri): Determination of qibla direction through personal ijtihad when the qibla is unknown.
إصابة (isabah): Hitting or being correct in the direction of the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The prayer is valid but he should repeat to be safe.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: prayer without taharri is invalid even if the qibla direction was correct, and this ruling applies after completion.

Building Prayer When Qibla Knowledge Occurs During Prayer: Sahibayn vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on building prayer when qibla knowledge occurs during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether one may build upon prayer performed without taharri when knowledge of correct qibla occurs during prayer, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
During prayer, Sahibayn require restart; Abu Yusuf allows building — knowledge cannot be built upon ignorance.

The previous lesson established that prayer without taharri is invalid after completion. But what if the person realizes during the prayer that he is facing the correct qibla? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute between the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf alone. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the distinction (farq) that reconciles with related cases, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person begins prayer without taharri. During the prayer, he becomes certain that he is facing the correct qibla (e.g., sees the Ka'bah). How should he proceed?
This scenario is distinct from knowledge after completion, where all agree no repetition.
2
State the two positions
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: he must restart the prayer (istqbal). Abu Yusuf alone says: he may continue building on what he has prayed (bina').
Both are within the Hanafi school; Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the school.
3
Understand each dalil
Sahibayn argue that the state of knowledge (after realization) is stronger than the previous state of ignorance. Building a strong part upon a weak part is not permissible. Abu Yusuf argues that the obligation (fard) is simply facing the Ka'bah, which has been fulfilled; thus the prayed portion is valid and can be built upon.
The key difference is whether the validity of the earlier portion requires intention of facing the Ka'bah or merely the objective reality.
4
Analyze the distinction (farq)
The Sahibayn distinguish between this case and the case where one performs taharri but later violates his own taharri. In the latter, he believes his prayer is invalid, so later discovery does not save it. Here, he was doubtful, not convinced of invalidity, so when correctness is confirmed, the prayer is valid after completion. However, during the prayer, the same principle applies: the weak (ignorant) cannot support the strong (knowledgeable).
This farq shows consistency: the ruling after completion is valid for no-taharri case, but during prayer the majority say restart.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text does not give explicit tarjih for the during-prayer dispute, but the initial relied-upon ruling (invalid after completion) aligns with the Sahibayn's cautionary approach. Later Hanafi authorities generally prefer the view that requires restart (Sahibayn) because building upon a deficient act is not allowed.
For fatwa, the cautious position is to restart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الظاهر منها وهو أن من اشتبهت عليه القبلة فصلى بلا تحر ثم عَلِمَ بعد الفراغ أنه ثمَّ أصاب لم تجز صلاته، وعليه الاعتماد.
وقيل : هذه العبارات إنما هي فيما إذا شرع بلا تحر، ثم علم في صلاته أنه أصاب ؛ لأنّ صاحب «الوقاية» قال قبل ذلك : وإن جهلها وعدم من يسأل تحرّى ولم يعد إن أخطأ، وإن علم به مصلِّياً أو تحول رأيه إلى أخرى استدار».
قلت : ليس في عبارة «الوقاية» دليل على هذا المراد بوجه من وجوه الدلالات، ولو كان فرض المسألة فيمن علم بالإصابة في الصلاة للزم التكرار، وهو بعيد من برهان الشريعة». انتهى ملخصاً.
وفي «غنية المستملي»: «إنّ شرع في الصلاة بغير تحر لم يجز، وإن أصاب في الواقع ؛ لأنّ القبلة حينئذ كانت جهة التحري، ولم توجد ، فبطلت صلاته، هذا إذا لم يعلم أنه أصاب أو أخطأ.
فإن علم أنه أصاب ، فإن عَلِمَ في الصلاةِ أنه أصاب استقبل عندهما ؛ لأنَّ حالة العلم أقوى مما قبله، وبناء القوي على الضعيف لا يجوز، وعند أبي يوسف له يبني ؛ لأنّ الفرض هو التوجه إلى الكعبة، وقد وجد فيجوزُ ما قد صلّى. وإن عَلِمَ بالإصابةِ
بعد الفراغ فلا إعادة عليه بالاتفاق.

فجازت صلاته.
It is the apparent one, and it is that whoever the qibla is ambiguous to him and he prayed without taharri, then after completion he knew that he had hit [the correct direction], his prayer is not valid, and upon it is the reliance. And it was said: These expressions are only for when he began without taharri, then knew during his prayer that he hit; because the author of al-Wiqayah said before that: 'If he is ignorant of it and does not find anyone to ask, he performs taharri and does not repeat if he errs, and if he knows while praying or his opinion changes to another, he turns [around].' I said: In the phrase of al-Wiqayah there is no evidence for this intended meaning by any indication whatsoever, and if the supposition of the issue were about one who knows of hitting during the prayer, then repetition would be necessary, and that is far from the proof of the Shari'ah. End, summarized. And in Ghuniyat al-Mustamli: 'Indeed, if he begins the prayer without taharri, it is not valid, even if he actually hit; because then the qibla was the direction of taharri, and it was not present, so his prayer is invalid. This is if he does not know whether he hit or missed. If he knows that he hit, then if he knows during the prayer that he hit, according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] he must restart, because the state of knowledge is stronger than what preceded it, and building the strong upon the weak is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, he may build, because the obligation is facing the Ka'bah, and it has occurred, so what he has prayed is permissible. And if he knows of hitting after completion, there is no repetition by agreement. And the distinction for the two [Sahibayn] between this issue and the one where he performed taharri and violated the direction of his taharri is that what is prescribed for other than itself requires its occurrence absolutely, not its acquisition intentionally. Like going to Friday prayer, but with the absence of belief in invalidity and absence of evidence for it, and that exists in the case of no taharri, unlike that other case, because his violation of his taharri direction necessitated the invalidity of his prayer in his belief, so it becomes like one who prayed in a najis garment in his view then it becomes clear that it was pure, or one who prayed thinking he was impure then it becomes clear he had wudu, or one who prayed the obligatory prayer thinking the time had not entered then it becomes clear it had entered; none of this is valid for him. As for the case of no taharri, he did not believe in its invalidity, rather he was doubtful about its permissibility, so when it becomes clear after completion that he hit, one of the two possibilities is removed and the other is established, thus here, so his prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of prayer performed without taharri when one later discovers that he was facing the correct qibla. The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) is that if the discovery occurs after completion, the prayer is invalid. The text first presents this ruling and then discusses a possible interpretation of al-Wiqayah that would limit the ruling to cases where knowledge occurs during prayer, but the author dismisses this. Then from Ghuniyat al-Mustamli, the detailed positions are given: without taharri, the prayer is invalid even if correct, because the qibla for the prayer is the direction determined by taharri. If one knows during the prayer, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he must restart; Abu Yusuf alone allows building upon the prayer already performed. After completion, all agree no repetition. The Sahibayn provide a distinction: when one violates his own taharri, he believes his prayer is invalid, so later knowledge doesn't help—similar to cases of najis garment or missed time. In the case of no taharri, he was doubtful, so when correctness is confirmed, the prayer is valid. This reasoning also rebuts an objection by Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Continuing prayer upon previously performed rak'ahs, rather than restarting.
عندهما (indahuma): According to the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if a person starts prayer without taharri and realizes during the prayer that he is facing the correct qibla, what should he do?
A) Continue the prayer and finish normally.
B) Restart the prayer from the beginning.
C) Perform sajda sahw and continue.
D) Stop the prayer and perform taharri before resuming.

Key Takeaway
When knowledge of correct qibla comes during prayer, the majority Hanafi position (Sahibayn) requires restarting; building upon the ignorant portion is not allowed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Validity of Congregational Prayer with Different Qibla Ijtihad
Commentary on the ruling of prayer in congregation when each person performs ijtihad for qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer when each person performs ijtihad for qibla and explain the distinction between knowing correct direction before and after completion.

Core Idea
When each person does ijtihad for qibla, the prayer is valid even if directions differ — only knowing the imam's direction and intentionally differing invalidates.

This passage expands on a matn from al-Wiqayah regarding congregational prayer in a dark night. The commentator explains that if each individual performs ijtihad (independent reasoning) to determine the qibla and faces his own direction, the prayer remains valid provided the follower knows the imam is not behind him. The text also resolves an objection by Ibn al-Humam concerning the consistency of the Hanafi position in two related cases. The lesson examines the ruling, its conditions, and the subtle distinction between knowledge during and after the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and its ruling
What is the exact scenario? A group prays in darkness, each does ijtihad, they don't know imam's direction but know he's not behind them. The ruling is that the prayer is valid.
2
Locate the dalil (reason)
The reason is that each faces his own qibla (direction of ijtihad), fulfilling the condition. Difference in direction does not harm, analogous to inside the Ka'bah. Deliberate opposition invalidates.
3
Understand the exceptions
If a follower knows the imam's direction and intentionally differs, or knows the imam is behind him, the prayer becomes invalid.
Knowing the imam is behind reverses the subject (qalb al-mawḍūʿ).
4
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's objection
Ibn al-Humam argued inconsistency: in the present case, leaving the direction of ijtihad invalidates; but in the case of one who prays without ijtihad and later finds correctness, the prayer is valid. He claimed this was contradictory.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The distinction is that knowledge of correct direction during the prayer forces correction (building strong on weak), but knowledge after completion does not. For the one without ijtihad, attainment (huṣūl) of the qibla suffices, not pursuit (taḥṣīl). Thus, the two cases are consistent.

Source Text
