أي صلى قوم في ليلة مظلمة بالجماعة، وتحرّوا القبلة، وتوجه كل واحد إلى جهة تحريه ، ولم يعلم أحد أن الإمام إلى أي جهة توجه، لكن يعلم كل واحد أنَّ الإمام ليس خلفه جازت صلاتهم. ومن هاهنا ظهر الفرقُ عندهما بين علم الإصابة بعد التمام وبين علمها قبله، فإنّه إذا عَلِمَ بالإصابة في الصلاة يلزم بناء القوي على الضعيف، ولا كذلك بعد التمام، وقد اندفع بهذا التقرير ما أورده ابن الهمام من أنّ هذه المسألة : يعني مسألة عدم الإجزاء بالعدول عن جهة التحرّي مشكلة على قولهما ؛ لأنّ تعليلهما في هذه المسألة، وهي أنَّ القبلَةَ جهة التحري ، وقد تركها يقتضي الفساد مطلقاً في صورة تركِ التحري، وإن علم إصابته ؛ لأنَّ ترك جهة التحري يصدقُ مع ترك التحري. وتعليلهما في تلك يعني في التي شرع بغير تحر، بأن ما شرع لغيره يشترط حصوله لا تحصيله يقتضي الصحة في هذه المسألة، وجه الفرق ظاهر مما ذكرناه من الفرق. انتهى (1) [١] قوله : أي صـلى قـوم... الخ ؛ فيه مسامحة ؛ فإنّ وضع المسألة لا يتوقف على الثلاثة فما فوق، بل لو كان من اقتدى به اثنين أو واحداً يكون الحكم كذلك، والقوم إنَّما يطلق على الثلاثة فما فوقها ؛ ولذا عده أهلُ الأصول من ألفاظ العموم. (٢) قوله : بالجماعة ؛ اعترض عليه بأنّ صلاة الليل بالجماعة جهرية، فكيف يشتبه حال الإمام، وأجيب عنه بأنه يجوز أن يترك الإمام الجهر سهوا ، أو بأنه لا يلزم من سماع صوته معرفة جهته فيمكن أن يعرفوا بصوته أنه ليس خلفهم، ولا يحصل لهم التمييز بأنه إلى أي جهة توجه كذا في «البناية». [٣] قوله : جازت صلاتهم ؛ لأنّ كلّ واحدٍ منهم استقبل قبلته، وهي جهـة تحريه، ولا تضرهم مخالفة جهتهم لجهة الإمام، كما في جوف الكعبة، فإنه لو جعل بعض القومِ ظهره إلى ظهر الإمام صحت صلاته، بخلاف ما إذا عَلِمَ جهة تحريه ، وخالفه، فإنّه لا تصح صلاته ؛ لأنّ مخالفة الإمام مانعة من صحة الاقتداء، وكذا إذا عَلِمَ أنَّ الإمام خلفَه ؛ لأنه حينئذ يلزم قلب الموضوع. (۱) من «غنية المستملي»(ص۲۲۲). أما إن علم أحدهم في الصَّلاة جهةً توجّه الإمام، ومع ذلك خالفه لا تجوز صلاته، وكذا إذا علم أن الإمام خلفه. فقوله : وهم خَلْفَهُ، فيه تساهل ، لأنَّ كلامنا فيما إذا لم يَعْلَمْ أَحدٌ أَنَّ الإمام إلى أي جهةٍ توجه ، فكيف يعلم أنه خلف الإمام، فالمراد أنه يعلم أن الإمام أمامه، وهذا أعم من أن يكون هو خلف الإمام ، أو لا ، لأنه إذا كان الإمامُ قُدَّامَه يحتمل أن يكون وجهه إلى وجه الإمام ، أو إلى جنبه ، أو إلى ظهره، وإنما يكون خَلْفَ الإمام إذا كان وجهه إلى ظهر الإمام، وحينئذ يكون جهة توجه الإمام معلومة، وكلامنا ليس في هذا. وإن صلى الإمامُ متحرِّياً واقتدى به من لم يتحر، فإن أصاب الإمام جازت صلاتهما، وإن أخطأ الإمام فصلاته جائزة لا صلاة المقتدي ، صرح به في «البزازية». [1 ] قوله : إن علم ... الخ ؛ إطلاق العلم يشمل اليقين والظن، وتقييد صاحب «تنوير الأبصار» بالتيقن ليس بصحيح، وفي التقييد بقوله : «في الصلاة»، إشارة إلى أنه لو عَلِمَ بمخالفة جهة الإمام بعد الصلاة لم يضره ذلك ، وجازت صلاته، ولم يذكر هذا القيد في الصورة الثانية إشعاراً بأنّ التقدّم على الإمام يضره مطلقاً، سواء علم به حالة الأداء أو بعده ، نعم لا يضر مجرد التقدم بلا علم، صرح به القُهستاني في «جامع الرموز (۱). والحاصل أن علم تقدّمه وكون الإمام خلفه يضرّ مطلقاً، سواء كان بعد الصلاة أو قبلها ، لا التقدّم مطلقاً ومخالفة الجهة، إنما يضر علمها في الصلاة لا غير. [۲] قوله : فيه تساهل ؛ وذلك لأن قوله : «وهم خلفه» إن حمل على كونهم ليس خلف الإمام في نفس الأمر علموا ذلك، أو لم يعلموا يفهم منه اشتراط ذلك ، كذلك، فإنّهم لو اقتدوه على اعتقاد أنهم خلفه جازت صلاته، وإن تقدموا في نفس الأمر، وإن حمل على علمهم بكونهم خلفه، وردّ عليه أنَّ كلامنا فيما إذا لم يعلم جهته فكيف يعلم كونه خلفه. [٣] قوله : وإنما يكون... الخ ؛ فيه خدشة ظاهرة ، فإنّه يمكن أن يقال : المراد (۱) جامع الرموز» (۱ : ۸۳).
That is: A group of people prayed in a dark night in congregation, and they performed ijtihad for the qibla, and each one faced his direction of ijtihad, and no one knew which direction the imam faced, but each one knew that the imam was not behind him. Their prayer is valid. And from here the difference appears according to them (the two) between knowing the correct direction after completion and before it. For if he knows the correct direction during the prayer, then the strong must be built upon the weak, but not so after completion. And by this exposition is repelled what Ibn al-Humam raised: that this issue—meaning the issue of non-validity by deviating from the direction of ijtihad—is problematic according to their view; because their reasoning in this issue—that the qibla is the direction of ijtihad and he left it—necessitates invalidity absolutely in the case of leaving ijtihad even if he knows his correctness; because leaving the direction of ijtihad is true with leaving ijtihad. And their reasoning in that (the one who began without ijtihad)—that what is legislated for something else requires its attainment not its pursuit—necessitates validity in this issue. And the aspect of the difference is apparent from what we mentioned of the difference. End. (1) His saying: 'a group prayed' etc.: there is leniency; for the setting of the issue does not depend on three or more, rather if two or one follow him, the ruling is the same, but 'qawm' is only used for three or more; hence the scholars of usul count it among words of generality. (2) His saying: 'in congregation': objection: night prayer in congregation is loud, so how is the imam's situation unclear? Answer: it is possible that the imam omitted the loudness forgetfully, or that hearing his voice does not necessitate knowing his direction; they may know by his voice that he is not behind them, but they cannot distinguish which direction he faced, as in al-Binayah. [3] His saying: 'their prayer is valid': because each of them faced his qibla, which is his direction of ijtihad, and their direction differing from the imam's direction does not harm them, as inside the Ka'bah: if some of them make their back to the imam's back, his prayer is valid. Unlike if he knows his (imam's) direction of ijtihad and differs, then his prayer is not valid; because opposing the imam prevents the validity of following. And likewise if he knows that the imam is behind him; because then the subject is reversed. (1) From Ghunyat al-Mustamli (p. 222). As for if one of them knows during the prayer the direction the imam faced and still differs, his prayer is not valid, and likewise if he knows that the imam is behind him. So his saying: 'and they are behind him' contains leniency, because our discussion is when no one knows which direction the imam faced, so how does he know he is behind the imam? The intended meaning is that he knows the imam is in front of him, and this is more general than his being behind the imam or not; because if the imam is in front of him, it is possible his face is towards the imam's face, or towards his side, or towards his back. He is only behind the imam if his face is towards the imam's back, and then the direction of the imam is known, and our discussion is not about this. And if the imam prays with ijtihad and one who did not perform ijtihad follows him: if the imam is correct, both their prayers are valid; if the imam errs, his prayer is valid but not the follower's. This is stated in al-Bazzaziyyah. [1] His saying: 'if he knows...' etc.: the word 'knowledge' includes certainty and presumption; restricting it to certainty by the author of Tanwir al-Absar is not correct. And the restriction by his saying 'in the prayer' indicates that if he knows of the imam's direction being different after the prayer, it does not harm him and his prayer is valid. He did not mention this restriction in the second picture to indicate that advancing ahead of the imam harms absolutely, whether he knows it during performance or after; yes, mere advancement without knowledge does not harm, as stated by al-Quhistani in Jami' al-Rumuz (1). The conclusion: Knowledge of his advancement and that the imam is behind him harms absolutely, whether after the prayer or before. As for differing in direction, only knowledge of it during the prayer harms, not otherwise. [2] His saying: 'there is leniency': because his saying 'and they are behind him' if taken to mean that they are not behind the imam in reality, whether they know it or not, implies that condition; similarly, if they follow him with the belief that they are behind him, his prayer is valid even if they are actually in front. If it is taken to mean their knowledge that they are behind him, it is objected that our discussion is when they do not know his direction, so how do they know they are behind him? [3] His saying: 'he is only...' etc.: there is an apparent flaw; for it can be said: the intended meaning (1) Jami' al-Rumuz (1:83).
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on a matn from al-Wiqayah regarding the validity of congregational prayer when the qibla direction is uncertain due to darkness. The commentator explains that if each person performs ijtihad (independent reasoning) to determine the qibla and faces his own direction, and no one knows the imam's direction (but they know he is not behind them), the prayer is valid. The reasoning is that each person is facing his own qibla (the direction of his ijtihad), and differing from the imam's direction does not invalidate the following, analogous to the situation inside the Ka'bah where followers may face different directions relative to the imam. The text then discusses a dispute raised by Ibn al-Humam: how can the ruling be consistent between two cases? In one case (the present one), the imam and followers each did ijtihad and followed their own directions; in another case, a person prayed without ijtihad and later found out he was correct. The commentator clarifies the distinction: knowing the correct direction during the prayer forces a change (building the strong on the weak), but knowing after completion does not. This resolves the apparent inconsistency. The commentary also addresses objections: the term 'qawm' (group) is not restrictive to three or more; the prayer is typically loud but the imam may forget; hearing the imam's voice does not indicate his direction. The condition that followers know the imam is not behind them is clarified: it means they know he is in front of them, which is a broader condition. If a follower knows the imam's direction and intentionally differs, the prayer is invalid. If the imam performed ijtihad and a follower who did not do ijtihad follows him, then if the imam is correct, both are valid; if the imam errs, only his prayer is valid, not the follower's.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Ijtihad or personal reasoning to determine the qibla direction when it is unclear.
جهة التحري (jihat al-taharrī): The direction that one's ijtihad leads to as the qibla.
قلب الموضوع (qalb al-mawḍūʿ): Reversal of the subject; here meaning the follower would be facing away from the imam, turning the situation upside down.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the dark night scenario, what is the minimum number of followers required for the ruling to apply according to the commentator?
A) Three
B) Two
C) One
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
The prayer is valid when each person performs ijtihad and faces his own direction, provided the follower does not knowingly oppose the imam's direction or know the imam is behind him.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Follower's Knowledge of Imam's Direction: When the Prayer Becomes Invalid
Ruling and commentary on follower's knowledge of imam's direction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a follower's knowledge of the imam's direction invalidates his prayer, distinguish between opposing direction and moving ahead, and explain the temporal scope of knowledge.

Core Idea
Opposing the imam's direction with knowledge during prayer invalidates; moving ahead with knowledge invalidates absolutely, even if known later.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary clarifies the conditions under which a follower's prayer is invalidated due to knowledge of the imam's facing direction or position. The commentator refines key terms like 'behind' and distinguishes between knowledge during prayer and after. Understanding these rulings ensures proper congregation prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios causing invalidity
The passage presents two distinct cases: (1) follower knows the imam's direction and opposes it intentionally, and (2) follower knows that the imam is behind him (i.e., he has moved ahead). In both cases, the prayer is invalid.
The first scenario involves opposing direction, the second involves positional precedence.
2
Distinguish the temporal effect of knowledge
For opposing direction, only knowledge during prayer harms; knowledge after prayer does not affect validity. For moving ahead, knowledge harms absolutely, whether the follower becomes aware during or after prayer.
This asymmetry is crucial for ruling on cases where a follower realizes later.
3
Understand the definition of 'behind' (khalaf)
The commentator reinterprets 'being behind the imam' to mean 'not being closer to the qibla than the imam', regardless of the orientation of one's face. This resolves the apparent leniency in the base text.
This definition shifts focus from spatial alignment to proximity to the qibla.
4
Recognize the scope of 'ilm (knowledge)
The text states that 'ilm includes both certainty (yaqīn) and probable belief (zann). The restriction to certainty by some later scholars is rejected.
Thus, if the follower has a strong suspicion about the imam's direction, it counts as knowledge.
5
Apply the taharrī scenario
If the imam makes a determination (taharrī) of the qibla and a follower who did not make a determination follows him, then if the imam is correct, both prayers are valid; if the imam is wrong, only the imam's prayer is valid.
This shows that reliance on the imam's judgment has consequences when his determination is erroneous.

Source Text

أما إن علم أحدهم في الصَّلاة جهةً توجّه الإمام، ومع ذلك خالفه لا تجوز صلاته، وكذا إذا علم أن الإمام خلفه.
فقوله : وهم خَلْفَهُ، فيه تساهل ، لأنَّ كلامنا فيما إذا لم يَعْلَمْ أَحدٌ أَنَّ الإمام إلى أي جهةٍ توجه ، فكيف يعلم أنه خلف الإمام، فالمراد أنه يعلم أن الإمام أمامه، وهذا أعم من أن يكون هو خلف الإمام ، أو لا ، لأنه إذا كان الإمامُ قُدَّامَه يحتمل أن يكون وجهه إلى وجه الإمام ، أو إلى جنبه ، أو إلى ظهره، وإنما يكون خَلْفَ الإمام إذا كان وجهه إلى ظهر الإمام، وحينئذ يكون جهة توجه الإمام معلومة، وكلامنا ليس في هذا. وإن صلى الإمامُ متحرِّياً واقتدى به من لم يتحر، فإن أصاب الإمام جازت صلاتهما، وإن أخطأ الإمام فصلاته جائزة لا صلاة المقتدي ، صرح به في «البزازية». [1 ] قوله : إن علم ... الخ ؛ إطلاق العلم يشمل اليقين والظن، وتقييد صاحب «تنوير الأبصار» بالتيقن ليس بصحيح، وفي التقييد بقوله : «في الصلاة»، إشارة إلى أنه لو عَلِمَ بمخالفة جهة الإمام بعد الصلاة لم يضره ذلك ، وجازت صلاته، ولم يذكر هذا القيد في الصورة الثانية إشعاراً بأنّ التقدّم على الإمام يضره مطلقاً، سواء علم به حالة الأداء أو بعده ، نعم لا يضر مجرد التقدم بلا علم، صرح به القُهستاني في «جامع الرموز (۱). والحاصل أن علم تقدّمه وكون الإمام خلفه يضرّ مطلقاً، سواء كان بعد الصلاة أو قبلها ، لا التقدّم مطلقاً ومخالفة الجهة، إنما يضر علمها في الصلاة لا غير. [۲] قوله : فيه تساهل ؛ وذلك لأن قوله : «وهم خلفه» إن حمل على كونهم ليس خلف الإمام في نفس الأمر علموا ذلك، أو لم يعلموا يفهم منه اشتراط ذلك ، كذلك، فإنّهم لو اقتدوه على اعتقاد أنهم خلفه جازت صلاته، وإن تقدموا في نفس الأمر، وإن حمل على علمهم بكونهم خلفه، وردّ عليه أنَّ كلامنا فيما إذا لم يعلم جهته فكيف يعلم كونه خلفه. [٣] قوله : وإنما يكون... الخ ؛ فيه خدشة ظاهرة ، فإنّه يمكن أن يقال : المراد بكونه خلف الإمام عدم كونه أقرب منه إلى قبلته، سواءً كان وجهه إلى جنبه أو ظهره ، فلا فرق بين الإمام وبين الخلف في حملها على المعنى العام.
وعبارة «المختصر: ولا يضرُّ جهلُهُ جهةً إمامه إذا عَلِمَ أَنَّه ليس خَلْفَه ، بل تقدمه ، أو عَلِمَ مخالفته (۱) : أي إذا عَلِمَ أنَّ الإمام ليس خلفَه.
[٤] بكونه خلف الإمام عدم كونه أقرب منه إلى قبلته، سواءً كان وجهه إلى جنبه أو ظهره ، فلا فرق بين الإمام وبين الخلف في حملها على المعنى العام.
If one of them knows during prayer the direction of the imam's facing, and yet opposes it, his prayer is not valid. Likewise if he knows that the imam is behind him. His statement: 'and they are behind him' contains leniency, because our discussion is when no one knows the direction the imam faced; how then can he know he is behind the imam? The intended meaning is that he knows the imam is in front of him. This is more general than his being behind the imam or not, because if the imam is in front of him, it is possible that his face is towards the imam's face, or towards his side, or towards his back. He is only behind the imam if his face is towards the imam's back. In that case the direction of the imam's facing is known, and our discussion is not about this. If the imam prays after making a determination (taharrī) and someone who did not make a determination follows him, then if the imam is correct, both their prayers are valid. If the imam is wrong, his prayer is valid but not the follower's prayer. This is explicitly stated in al-Bazzāziyya. [1] His statement: 'if he knows...' etc.; the word 'knowledge' includes certainty and probability. The restriction of the author of Tanwīr al-Absār to certainty is not correct. In the restriction by his saying 'during prayer', there is an indication that if he knew the opposition of the imam's direction after the prayer, it would not harm him and his prayer would be valid. He did not mention this restriction in the second case, implying that moving ahead of the imam harms absolutely, whether he knows it during performance or afterwards. However, mere moving ahead without knowledge does not harm, as explicitly stated by al-Quhistānī in Jāmi' al-Rumūz (1). The conclusion: knowledge of his moving ahead and that the imam is behind him harms absolutely, whether after prayer or before, not moving ahead absolutely and opposition of direction; knowledge of that harms only during prayer, not otherwise. [2] His statement: 'there is leniency in it'; because his saying 'and they are behind him' if interpreted as their not being behind the imam in reality, whether they knew that or not, implies that condition is required likewise. For if they follow him believing that they are behind him, their prayer is valid, even if they are ahead in reality. If interpreted as their knowledge of being behind him, the objection is that our discussion is when they do not know his direction, so how can they know being behind him? [3] His statement: 'and he is only...' etc.; there is an apparent flaw in it, for it can be said: what is meant by being behind the imam is that he is not closer to his qibla than the imam, whether his face is towards his side or his back; thus there is no difference between the imam and being behind in interpreting it in the general sense. The expression of al-Mukhtasar: 'It does not harm his ignorance of the direction of his imam if he knows that he is not behind him, but ahead of him, or he knows his opposition (1): i.e., when he knows that the imam is not behind him.' [4] That he is behind the imam means he is not closer to his qibla than the imam, whether his face is towards his side or his back; thus there is no difference between the imam and being behind in interpreting it in the general sense.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a ruling from the matn regarding the follower's knowledge of the imam's direction during prayer. The author explains that if a follower knows the exact direction the imam is facing (i.e., the qibla direction the imam has chosen) and intentionally faces a different direction, his prayer is invalid. Similarly, if a follower knows that the imam is behind him (i.e., he has moved ahead of the imam), his prayer is also invalid. The commentator then refines the expression 'and they are behind him' from the original text, noting a potential leniency: the discussion is about cases where the followers do not know the imam's direction at all, so how can they know they are behind him? The intended meaning is that they simply know the imam is in front of them—this is broader than being directly behind. The commentator also distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) if the imam makes a diligent determination (taharrī) of the qibla and a follower who did not make such determination follows him, then if the imam's determination is correct, both prayers are valid; if the imam is wrong, only his prayer is valid, not the follower's. (2) Regarding knowledge: the term 'knowledge' in the matn includes both certainty and probable belief (zann). The restriction to certainty by some later scholars is incorrect. The qualification 'during prayer' indicates that if a follower discovers after prayer that he had opposed the imam's direction, his prayer is still valid. This qualification is omitted in the case of moving ahead of the imam, because moving ahead harms absolutely, regardless of when one becomes aware of it. However, mere moving ahead without knowledge (e.g., due to crowding) does not harm. The commentator also clarifies that being 'behind the imam' means the follower is not closer to the qibla than the imam, whether his face is to the imam's side or back. This is a general interpretation that removes the earlier apparent difficulty.

Key Terms
علم (ʿilm): Knowledge that includes certainty (yaqīn) and probable belief (zann); in this context, it means the follower's knowledge of the imam's direction or of being ahead of him.
خلف (khalaf): Being behind the imam; interpreted here as not being closer to the qibla than the imam, regardless of the orientation of one's face.
تقدّم (taqaddum): Moving ahead of the imam (i.e., being closer to the qibla than the imam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does knowledge of opposition to the imam's direction harm the follower's prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only if known with certainty during the prayer
B) If known (including probable belief) during the prayer
C) If known at any time, even after the prayer
D) Only if the imam was correct in his determination

Key Takeaway
The follower's prayer is only invalid if he knows the imam's direction and opposes it during prayer, or if he knows he has moved ahead; ignorance or knowledge after prayer does not affect validity for direction opposition, but moving ahead with knowledge always invalidates.

Intention in Prayer: Timing and Sufficiency of Heart vs. Utterance
Commentary explaining intention's timing and the three scenarios of heart vs. utterance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios regarding intention and utterance in prayer and apply the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention relative to takbirat al-ihram.

Core Idea
Heart intention at takbir is sufficient; verbal expression is better but not required.

The intention (niyyah) is the heart's resolve that distinguishes one act of worship from another. In prayer, its timing is critical: it must coincide with the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) or be immediately before it without any unrelated action. The classical Hanafi texts discuss whether verbalizing the intention is necessary or merely recommended. This lesson unpacks the commentary on a matn that addresses these issues, clarifying the three possible scenarios and their rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Recommended Timing
The commentary states that joining the intention with the takbir is mustahabb (recommended). Locate this in the text and note that it is not obligatory.
The phrase 'bi taḥrīmatihā' indicates the moment of takbir.
2
Understand Permissibility of Preceding Intention
The text allows the intention to be made slightly before the takbir, as long as no unrelated action intervenes. Identify the condition for validity.
Unrelated actions invalidate the connection.
3
Recognize the Invalidity of Delayed Intention
If the intention is made after the takbir, the prayer is invalid according to the most correct opinion (al-aṣaḥḥ). Find this ruling.
This is a clear boundary: intention must coincide with or precede the takbir.
4
Distinguish the Three Scenarios of Heart vs. Utterance
The commentary lists three cases: (1) heart intention alone – valid, sufficient, and the prophetic way; (2) verbal utterance alone without heart intention – invalid; (3) both together – better (afḍal). Understand each and its legal consequence.
The matn says 'al-qaṣdu maʿa lafẓihi afḍal' – intention with utterance is better.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصل قصد قلبه صلاته بتحريمتِها والقصد مع لفظه أفضل، ويكفي للنفل، والتراويح
[١] قوله : بتحريمتها ؛ متعلّق بقوله : يصلّ، وهذا بيانُ الوقت المستحب، فإنَّ قران النية بتحريمة الصلاة مستحبّ ، ويجوز تقديمها عليها عندنا بشرط أن لا يشتغل بينهما بما ليس من جنس الصلاة، وأمَّا النَّيَّةُ المتأخرة عن التحريمة فلا يجوز على الأصح. كذا في «البناية» و«الخلاصة».
[٢]قوله : تفسير النية : اللام للعهد أي النية المعتبرة في الصلاة.
[٣]قوله : لفظه ؛ هو إما مصدر ؛ أي مع تلفظه ، أو بمعنى الملفوظ؛ أي مع تكلّم ما يدل عليه.
[٤]قوله : أفضل ؛ هاهنا ثلاث صور :
أحدها: الاكتفاء بنية القلب، وهو مجزئ اتفاقاً، وهو الطريقة المشروعة المأثورة عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأصحابه ، فلم ينقل عن أحد منهم التكلم بنويت أو أنوي صلاة كذا في وقت كذا، ونحو ذلك، كما حققه ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير») ، وابن القيم في : «زاد المعاد»، وقد فصلتُ ذلك في «السعاية»(۳) ، وفي رسالتي «آكام النفائس في أداء الأذكار بلسان الفارس وثانيها: الاكتفاء بالتلفظ من دون قصد القلب، وهو غير مجزئ.
(٤)
And the intention of his heart connects his prayer to its takbirat al-ihram, and intending with utterance is better. And it suffices for supererogatory (nafl) prayers and tarawih. [1] His statement: 'with its takbirat al-ihram'; it is connected to his statement 'connects', and this is an explanation of the recommended time. Indeed, joining the intention with the takbir of prayer is recommended (mustahabb). It is permissible to precede it (the intention) according to us on condition that one does not engage between them in something not of the same type as prayer. As for the intention delayed after the takbir, it is not valid according to the most correct opinion. This is stated in al-Binaya and al-Khulasa. [2] His statement: 'explanation of intention'; the definite article is for the specific reference, i.e., the intention considered valid in prayer. [3] His statement: 'with his utterance'; it is either a verbal noun, i.e., along with his speaking, or in the sense of what is uttered, i.e., along with speaking what indicates it. [4] His statement: 'better'; there are three cases here: First: sufficing with intention of the heart; it is valid by agreement, and it is the prescribed method transmitted from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions. For nothing has been narrated from any of them of saying 'I intend' or 'I intend such and such prayer at such time' and the like, as verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir and Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad. I have detailed this in al-Si'aya and in my treatise Akam al-Nafa'is fi Ada' al-Adhkar bi Lisan al-Faris. Second: sufficing with verbal utterance without intention of the heart; it is not valid.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from the matn regarding the intention (niyyah) for prayer. The matn states that one connects the intention of his heart to the takbirat al-ihram, and that verbal expression (qasad ma'a lafzihi) is better. The commentator begins by explaining that the phrase 'with its takbirat al-ihram' refers to the recommended time for the intention. According to the Hanafi school, it is mustahabb to form the intention simultaneously with the takbir. It is permissible to form it slightly before the takbir, provided that no unrelated action intervenes. However, if the intention comes after the takbir, the prayer is not valid (on the most correct view). The commentator then clarifies that 'intention' here means the specific intention that is a condition for the validity of prayer. The word 'with his utterance' is explained in two ways: either meaning 'with his speaking' or 'with what is spoken' (i.e., the words). The commentator then discusses three scenarios regarding the combination of heart intention and verbal expression: (1) Heart intention alone is sufficient and is the prophetic way; this is agreed upon. (2) Verbal expression alone without heart intention is not valid. (3) Both together is better (afḍal), as implied by the matn. The commentator cites Ibn al-Humam and Ibn al-Qayyim to support that heart intention alone is the transmitted practice, and that verbalizing intention is not a sunnah.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart that distinguishes one act of worship from another; a condition for the validity of prayer.
تحريمة (taḥrīmah): The takbir that begins the prayer (takbirat al-ihram), which makes the prayer prohibited (haram) to worldly actions.
لفظ (lafẓ): Verbal utterance; here it refers to speaking words of intention, which is recommended but not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on making intention after the takbir (takbirat al-ihram) in the Hanafi school?
A) It is valid but disliked
B) It is not valid according to the most correct opinion
C) It is better than before the takbir
D) It is valid only for nafl prayers

Key Takeaway
The intention (niyyah) for prayer must be present at or just before the opening takbir; heart intention alone is sufficient, and verbal expression is merely recommended.

The Time and Verbalization of Intention in Prayer
Explanation of the preferred time and verbalization of intention in salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of intention (niyyah) in relation to the opening takbir and explain why verbalization is not required.

Core Idea
Intention in the heart suffices; coupling with the takbir is recommended, but verbalization is not from the prophetic practice.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the preferred time for making intention (niyyah) in prayer and the ruling on verbalizing it. The Hanafi school holds that intention is a condition of prayer, and it must be present at the time of the opening takbir (tahrimah) or immediately before without intervening unrelated acts. While some later scholars recommended verbalizing the intention, the authentic practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his Companions was only heart intention. This lesson clarifies the three scenarios regarding intention and the evidence for the sufficiency of heart intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (intention for prayer) and its legal status (condition for validity). Note that the passage specifies the preferred time: coupling intention with the takbir is recommended (mustahabb), but preceding it is permissible if no unrelated act intervenes.
2
Understand the concept of tahrimah
The tahrimah (saying 'Allahu Akbar') is the pillar that initiates prayer. Intention must be connected to it. The passage explains that intention after takbir is invalid according to the soundest opinion.
3
Analyze the three scenarios about intention
The passage presents three scenarios: (1) heart intention alone (valid, the prescribed way), (2) verbalization without heart intention (invalid), (3) combining both (recommended by some scholars but not prophetic). Understand which is sufficient and which is not.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof for the sufficiency of heart intention is the absence of any report that the Prophet ﷺ or his Companions verbalized intention. If it were obligatory, it would have been transmitted.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some Shafi'is consider verbalization obligatory, but the Hanafi position is that it is not required. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): a prayer with only heart intention is valid in the Hanafi school but not in the Shafi'i view that requires verbalization.

And his heart's intention for his prayer is valid with its tahrimah (opening takbir), and intending with his utterance is better, and it suffices for nafl and tarawih. And his heart's intention for his prayer is valid with its tahrimah; this is the explanation of intention. And intending with his utterance is better, and it suffices for nafl and tarawih. [1] His saying: 'with its tahrimah' is connected to his saying 'is valid', and this is an explanation of the preferred time; for indeed, coupling the intention with the tahrimah of prayer is recommended, and it is permissible to precede it in our view on condition that he does not engage between them in something not of the same type as prayer. As for the intention that occurs after the tahrimah, it is not permissible according to the soundest opinion. Thus in al-Binayah and al-Khulasah. [2] His saying: 'explanation of intention': the lam is for the covenant, i.e., the intention considered in prayer. [3] His saying: 'his utterance': it is either a verbal noun, i.e., with his uttering, or it means the uttered thing, i.e., with him speaking what indicates it. [4] His saying: 'it is better'; here are three scenarios: First: contenting oneself with the intention of the heart, and it suffices by agreement, and it is the prescribed way transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) and his companions, for no one among them is reported to have spoken 'I intend' or 'I intend such and such prayer at such and such time' and the like, as verified by Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir, and Ibn al-Qayyim in Zad al-Ma'ad, and I have detailed that in al-Si'ayah and in my treatise Akam al-Nafa'is fi Ada' al-Adhkar bi Lisan al-Fars. Second: contenting oneself with verbalization without intention of the heart, and it is not sufficient. Third: combining both, and it is a sunnah according to Tuhfat al-Muluk, but it is not correct, and it is recommended according to al-Munyah, i.e., in the sense of what the scholars did and recommended, not in the sense of what the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) did or encouraged, for that is not established. They justified its recommendation and goodness by saying it contains harmony between the heart and tongue and a combination of resolve.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time and manner of making intention (niyyah) for prayer. The author explains that the intention must accompany the opening takbir (tahrimah) and that verbalizing the intention is better but not necessary. The passage begins by stating that the intention is valid when made with the takbir, and that intending with the utterance is better. This is followed by a detailed commentary. The key ruling is that coupling the intention with the takbir is recommended, and it is permissible to make the intention before the takbir as long as no unrelated act intervenes. However, if the intention is made after the takbir, it is invalid according to the soundest opinion. The author then discusses the three scenarios regarding intention: (1) intention of the heart alone is sufficient and is the prescribed way from the Prophet and his companions; (2) verbalization without heart intention is insufficient; (3) combining both is considered recommended by some scholars, but this is not established as a prophetic practice. The commentary cites authorities like Ibn al-Humam and Ibn al-Qayyim to support that the prophetic practice was only heart intention. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that intention of the heart suffices, and verbalization is merely a recommended aid for concentration.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship; it is a condition for the validity of prayer.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying 'Allahu Akbar') that initiates the prayer and prohibits worldly actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone makes the intention to pray after saying the opening takbir (tahrimah)?
A) It is valid if the intention follows immediately.
B) It is not valid according to the soundest opinion.
C) It is valid for nafl but not for fard.
D) It is valid if the verbal intention is also made.

Key Takeaway
Intention of the heart alone suffices for prayer; it must be present at or before the takbir, and verbalization is merely recommended, not required.

Intention for Supererogatory Prayers: General vs. Specific
Ruling on the sufficiency of absolute intention for nafl and sunnah prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the sufficiency of a general intention for supererogatory prayers and identify the intra-madhhab disagreement on this issue.

Core Idea
For all sunnah prayers, a general intention to pray suffices; specific intention is only required for the obligatory (fard) prayer.

In this passage, we examine a key issue in Hanafi fiqh: whether a person needs to specifically intend the tarawih prayer or the sunnah of Fajr, or whether a general intention to pray is enough. While there is consensus that nafl prayers require only a general intention, a dispute exists among later Hanafi authorities regarding emphasized sunan and tarawih. This lesson walks through the evidence and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Identify the opening ruling: for all sunnan, a general intention (niyyat mutlaq al-salah) suffices; for fard, specific intention is required.
This is the author's summary position.
2
Identify the Point of Agreement
Note that for nafl prayers, there is consensus (bil-ittifaq) that a general intention is sufficient. The commentary explains that nafl is the most inclusive category.
This includes tahajjud, duha, etc.
3
Locate the Disagreement
The dispute is about tarawih and the emphasized sunnan (sunan mu'akkadah). Some later Hanafi scholars (Qadi Khan, al-Bazzaziyyah, al-Khulasah) require specific intention, while the majority (as in al-Hidayah and al-Muhit) hold that general intention suffices.
Note that the disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view: a general intention of absolute prayer suffices for all supererogatory prayers, including tarawih and sunan mu'akkadah. This is supported by al-Hidayah and al-Muhit.
Adopt this position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسائر السنن نية مطلقِ الصَّلاة، وللفرض شُرِطَ

[ ۱ ] قوله : سائر السنن ؛ دخل في إطلاقِهِ سنَّةُ الفجر، حتى لو صلى ركعتين تهجداً ثم تبين أنهما صلّينا بعد طلوع الفجر أجزأنا عن السنة. كذا في «البحر»(4). [۲] قوله : نيَّةُ مطلق الصلاة؛ هذا في النفل بالاتفاق، فإنّه إذا نوى مطلق الصلاة والعمل بعموم أفرادها ،متعذر لا بد أن يراد أحدها ، وصرفه إلى النفل أولى ؛ لكونه أدنى وأشمل ، فإنّه مشروع في كل الأوقات، فكان بمنزلة الحقيقة.

وأما في التراويح وبقيَّةِ السننِ المؤكّدة فقال بعض المشايخ: إنّها لا تتأدّى بنية مطلق الصلاة ؛ لأنها صلاةٌ مخصوصة، فتجب مراعاة الصفة للخروج عن العهدة، وهو الذي صححه قاضي خان) وصاحب «البزازية» وغيرهما.
وظاهر الرواية الذي صححه في «الهداية»(٦) هو ما ذكره المصنف، ونسبه ابنُ الهمام في «فتح القدير» إلى أكثر المشايخ، وهو أن التراويح وغيرها تتأدى بنية مطلق الصلاة، وبه جزم في «المحيط»، وقال: هذا هو الصحيح، وخالف في «الخُلاصَة» حيث قال بخلافه.
And for the rest of the sunan (supererogatory prayers), the intention of absolute prayer (suffices), and for the obligatory prayer, specific intention is required. [1] His saying: 'the rest of the sunan'; its general application includes the sunnah of Fajr, such that if one prayed two rak'ahs as tahajjud and it later became clear that he prayed them after dawn, they suffice for the sunnah. Thus in al-Bahr. [2] His saying: 'intention of absolute prayer'; this is for nafl by agreement, for when one intends absolute prayer, and acting upon all its individuals is impossible, one of them must be intended, and directing it to nafl is better because it is lower and more inclusive, for it is prescribed in all times, so it is like the primary meaning. As for tarawih and the rest of the emphasized sunan, some mashayikh said: they are not fulfilled by the intention of absolute prayer because they are specific prayers, so consideration of the specification is necessary to discharge the obligation. This is what Qadi Khan and the author of al-Bazzaziyyah and others preferred. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) that is preferred in al-Hidayah is what the author mentioned, and Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir attributed it to the majority of mashayikh: that tarawih and others are fulfilled by the intention of absolute prayer. This is affirmed in al-Muhit, and he said: this is correct. The author of al-Khulasah disagreed, stating the opposite.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the type of intention required for supererogatory (nafl) and emphasized sunnah prayers. The author begins by stating that for all sunnah prayers (including the sunnah of Fajr), a general intention to pray ('absolute prayer') suffices, while for obligatory prayers a specific intention is required. The commentary explains that for nafl prayers, there is consensus that a general intention is sufficient because nafl is the most inclusive category. The dispute arises regarding the tarawih prayer and other emphasized sunnan (sunan mu'akkadah). Some leading Hanafi scholars (such as Qadi Khan and the author of al-Bazzaziyyah) hold that these specific prayers require specific intention because they are distinct acts of worship. However, the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) preferred by the majority of mashayikh, as stated in al-Hidayah, is that a general intention of absolute prayer suffices for them as well. The author of al-Khulasah held the contrary view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the text is that of the majority: a general intention is sufficient for tarawih and other sunan mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
نية مطلق الصلاة (niyyat mutlaq al-salah): A general intention to pray without specifying the particular type of prayer; it is sufficient for nafl and, according to the majority, for all sunan.
سائر السنن (sa'ir al-sunan): All non-obligatory prayers, including the sunan mu'akkadah (emphasized) and ghayr mu'akkadah (non-emphasized), as well as tarawih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the favored view (mufta bihi) in this passage, does a person who prays two rak'ahs with the general intention to pray (without specifying tarawih) get the reward of tarawih if it is the month of Ramadan?
A) Yes, because general intention suffices for all sunan including tarawih.
B) Yes, but only if they also intend the time of tarawih.
C) No, because tarawih requires specific intention of tarawih.
D) No, because tarawih is not considered nafl.

Key Takeaway
For all sunnah prayers, including tarawih, a general intention to pray (niyyat mutlaq al-salah) suffices; only fard prayers require specific intention according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Intention for Sunnah Prayers: Absolute Intention Suffices
Commentary on intention for sunnah prayers with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that absolute intention suffices for sunnah prayers and distinguish the intra-madhhab dispute regarding emphasized sunnahs.

Core Idea
Absolute intention of prayer suffices for all sunnah prayers; the label 'sunnah' is post-hoc, not a condition.

In the Hanafi school, the intention (niyyah) for prayer must be specific for obligatory prayers, but for supererogatory prayers, including sunnah prayers, a more relaxed rule applies. This lesson examines the commentary on the ruling that 'absolute intention of prayer' (niyyat muṭlaq al-ṣalāh) suffices for all sunnah prayers. We will explore the scope of this ruling, the intra-madhhab disagreement regarding emphasized sunnahs like tarawih, and the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The base text states that for 'the rest of the sunnah prayers' (sāʼir al-sunan), absolute intention suffices. First, identify what is included: the commentary clarifies it includes the sunnah of Fajr and all other sunnah prayers.
The term 'sāʼir al-sunan' covers both rawātib and non-emphasized sunnahs.
2
Understand the reasoning for absolute intention
The commentary explains that intending absolute prayer must refer to some specific instance; the most appropriate is the supererogatory category because it is lower and more comprehensive. This reasoning applies to all nafl prayers by agreement.
Absolute intention is like intending 'I pray' without further specification.
3
Locate the intra-madhhab dispute
Some later Hanafi scholars (Qadi Khan, author of al-Bazzaziyya) held that for tarawih and emphasized sunnahs, specific intention is required because they are specific prayers. Identify the opposing position and the scholars involved.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a cross-madhhab one.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The relied-upon position (ẓāhir al-riwāyah) is that absolute intention suffices. The proof cited is the Prophet's practice: he did not intend 'sunnah' but simply 'prayer to Allah'. The description 'sunnah' is our labeling of his consistent act.
The dalil is a Sunnah ahad (the Prophet's action), with zanni thubut and zanni dalala.
5
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The commentary states that the ẓāhir al-riwāyah, corrected in al-Hidayah and by Ibn al-Humam, is that absolute intention suffices. This is the mufta bihi position today.
The tarjih authority is al-Marghinani and Ibn al-Humam.

And for the rest of the sunnah prayers, the intention of absolute prayer [suffices]. [1] His saying: 'the rest of the sunnah prayers' – includes in its scope the sunnah of Fajr, such that if one prays two rak'ahs of tahajjud and then it becomes clear that they were prayed after dawn, it suffices for the sunnah. Thus in al-Bahr. [2] His saying: 'intention of absolute prayer' – this is [the ruling] for supererogatory prayers by agreement, for if he intends absolute prayer, [but] acting upon its general individuals is impossible, so one of them must be intended, and turning it to supererogatory is more appropriate because it is lower and more comprehensive, for it is legislated in all times, so it is like the proper meaning. As for taraweeh and the rest of the emphasized sunnahs, some shaykhs said: they are not performed by the intention of absolute prayer, because they are specific prayers, so observing the description is obligatory to discharge the obligation, and this is what Qadi Khan and the author of al-Bazzaziyya and others corrected. But the apparent narration, which is corrected in al-Hidayah, is what the author mentioned, and Ibn al-Humam attributed it to the verifiers in Fath al-Qadir. Its reasoning is that the meaning of sunnah is that the supererogatory act is regularly performed by the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, before or after the obligatory prayer, so if the worshipper performs the supererogatory act in that place, it is true that he has done the act called sunnah, for the Prophet did not intend 'sunnah' but rather prayer to Allah; thus it is known that the description of sunnah is established after his action upon that manner as our naming of his specific action, and originally it is supererogatory, not that its occurrence depends on intending the sunnah.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the Hanafi ruling regarding intention (niyyah) for sunnah prayers. The base text (matn) states: 'And for the rest of the sunnah prayers, the intention of absolute prayer [suffices].' The commentary begins by explaining the scope of 'sāʼir al-sunan'—it includes the sunnah of Fajr, so if someone prays two rak'ahs of tahajjud after dawn, it counts for the Fajr sunnah. Then it discusses the phrase 'intention of absolute prayer' (niyyat muṭlaq al-ṣalāh). For all supererogatory (nafl) prayers, by agreement, if one intends absolute prayer, it is valid. The reasoning is that absolute intention must refer to some specific prayer, and the most appropriate is the supererogatory because it is the lowest and most comprehensive category. However, there is a dispute regarding tarāwīḥ and other emphasized sunnahs: some scholars hold that absolute intention does not suffice because these are specific prayers requiring specific intention. The commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position (ẓāhir al-riwāyah) is that absolute intention does suffice, as mentioned by the author and supported by Ibn al-Humām. The proof is that the Prophet never intended 'sunnah' but simply 'prayer to Allah'; the description 'sunnah' is applied by us after the fact to his consistent practice. Thus, intending absolute prayer in that time and place automatically makes it the sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
نية مطلق الصلاة (niyyat muṭlaq al-ṣalāh): Intending prayer in an absolute sense without specifying a particular type, such as intending just 'I pray' without naming fard, sunnah, etc.
سائر السنن (sāʼir al-sunan): All sunnah prayers other than the obligatory ones; includes both rawātib and non-emphasized supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the ẓāhir al-riwāyah in the Hanafi school, does absolute intention of prayer suffice for the tarawih prayer?
A) No, because tarawih is a specific prayer requiring specific intention.
B) Yes, because the Prophet never intended 'sunnah' but simply 'prayer'.
C) Yes, but only if one also intends a specific number of rak'ahs.
D) No, because the majority of later scholars said otherwise.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, an absolute intention of prayer in the time of a sunnah prayer suffices; you do not need to mentally pronounce the word 'sunnah'.

Specification (Ta'yīn) in Fard Prayers
Commentary on ta'yīn for fard prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of ta'yīn for fard prayers and distinguish it from intending the number of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Ta'yīn of the fard prayer is required; raka'ah count is automatically determined.

When you intend to pray a fard prayer, you must specify which prayer it is (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr) because the time slot is shared between fard and nafl. However, you do not need to intend the number of rak'ahs separately. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on ta'yīn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage begins by stating that specification (ta'yīn) is a condition (shart) for fard prayer, but intention of rak'ah number is not.
The base text is the matn being commented on.
2
Understand the reasoning (talīl)
The commentary explains that fard is an additional description beyond absolute prayer, and the time is suitable for both fard and nafl. Without ta'yīn, the prayer would remain unspecified.
This is the wisdom behind the condition.
3
Examine the scope of ta'yīn
Ta'yīn means intending the specific fard (e.g., Dhuhr or 'Asr). It suffices to intend 'the obligatory of the time' or 'the obligatory of the day'.
Verbal slip does not harm if the heart's intention is correct.
4
Distinguish from number of rak'ahs
The commentary states that when the prayer is specified, the rak'ahs are necessarily specified; no separate intention is needed.
This is a logical consequence: each fard has a fixed number.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللفرض شرط تعيينه لا نية عدد ركعاته، وللمقتدي نية صلاته واقتدائه
[١] قوله : تعيينه ؛ لأن الفريضة وصف زائد على مطلق الصلاة، ووقتها ظرف صالح للفرض والنفل كليهما ، فما لم يعين المصلّي لم يتعين ، وهو أن ينوي الظهر أو العصر، ولو نوى فرض الوقتِ أو فرض اليوم جاز. كذا في «الظهيرية»، ولو نوى الظهر وتلفظ بالعصر أجزأه ؛ لأنَّ المعتبر هو التعيين بالقلب. كذا في «القُنية». [٢] قوله : لا نية ؛ أي لا تشترط نيَّة عدد ركعات ما يصلي، فإنه إذا عين الصلاة تعينت الركعات بالضرورة، وكذا لا تشترط نية الاستقبال إلى الكعبة على الأصح. [٣]قوله : وللمقتدي ؛ أي يلزم للمقتدي نيَّةُ صلاة إمامه مع نية اقتدائه ؛ لأنه يلزمه الصحة والفساد من جهة إمامه، فلا بد من نيَّةِ متابعته، ولا تشترط نيَّة تعيين الإمام، ولو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام ويظن أنه زيد، فإذا هو عمرو صح. كذا في البحر (۲)
And for the obligatory [prayer], its specification is a condition, not the intention of the number of its rak'ahs; and for the follower, [there is required] intention of his prayer and of his following. [1] His saying: 'its specification' – because the obligatory is an additional description upon absolute prayer, and its time is a container suitable for both obligatory and supererogatory, so unless the worshipper specifies, it is not specified; that is, he intends Dhuhr or 'Asr. If he intends the obligatory of the time or the obligatory of the day, it is permissible. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. If he intended Dhuhr and uttered 'Asr, it suffices him, because consideration is for the specification of the heart. Thus in al-Qunyah. [2] His saying: 'not intention' – i.e., the intention of the number of rak'ahs of what he prays is not a condition, for when he specifies the prayer, the rak'ahs are necessarily specified. Likewise, the intention of facing the qibla is not a condition according to the most correct view. [3] His saying: 'and for the follower' – i.e., for the follower, the intention of his imam's prayer is necessary along with the intention of his following, because his prayer's validity and invalidity depend on his imam, so following must be intended. It is not a condition to specify the imam's identity; if he intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd, but then it is 'Amr, it is valid. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn rulings concerning intention for obligatory prayers and for followers (muqtadūn). The base text states: 'For the obligatory [prayer], its specification is a condition, not the intention of the number of its rak'ahs; and for the follower, [there is required] intention of his prayer and of his following.' The commentary first explains 'specification' (ta'yīn): because the obligatory prayer has an additional description beyond absolute prayer, and its time is shared between obligatory and supererogatory, the worshipper must specify which prayer (e.g., Dhuhr or 'Asr). If one intends 'the obligatory of the time' or 'the obligatory of the day', it suffices. The true specification is in the heart; even if one verbally says a different prayer name but the heart specifies correctly, it is valid. Next, the phrase 'not intention of number of rak'ahs' means that one does not need to intend, e.g., 'four rak'ahs for Dhuhr'; specifying the prayer automatically determines the number. Similarly, intention of facing the qibla is not required as a separate intention. Finally, for the follower (muqtadī), the commentary says the follower must intend both the specific prayer (e.g., Fajr) and the act of following the imam, because the follower's prayer becomes valid or invalid through connection with the imam. However, it is not required to intend the imam's personal identity; if one intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd but it is 'Amr, the prayer is still valid.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specifying which fard prayer one is performing (e.g., Zuhr, 'Asr) in one's intention.
نية عدد الركعات (niyyat 'adad al-rak'āt): Intending the number of rak'ahs for the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on intending the number of rak'ahs for a fard prayer?
A) It is required.
B) It is recommended.
C) It is not a condition; specifying the prayer suffices.
D) It is required only for the imam.

Key Takeaway
Ta'yīn (specifying the fard) is a condition for fard prayer; the number of rak'ahs need not be intended separately.

The Follower's Intention (Iqtidā’)
Commentary on the follower's intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain what a follower must intend (prayer and following) and what is not required (imam's identity, number of rak'ahs).

Core Idea
The follower must intend both the specific prayer and the act of following the imam; the imam's personal identity is irrelevant.

When you pray behind an imam, your intention must include both the prayer itself (e.g., Fajr) and the fact that you are following the imam. But you do not need to specify the imam's name or the number of rak'ahs. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on the muqtadī's intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the requirement
The base text states that for the follower, intention of his prayer and of his following is required.
The word 'and' (واو) indicates both are necessary.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentary explains that the follower's prayer validity depends on the imam, so following must be intended.
This is because the muqtadī's prayer is connected to the imam's.
3
Note what is not required
The text clarifies that intending the imam's identity (e.g., Zayd) is not a condition; even if mistaken, the prayer is valid.
Also, number of rak'ahs is not required as it follows from the prayer type.

وللفرض شرط تعيينه لا نية عدد ركعاته، وللمقتدي نية صلاته واقتدائه
[١] قوله : تعيينه ؛ لأن الفريضة وصف زائد على مطلق الصلاة، ووقتها ظرف صالح للفرض والنفل كليهما ، فما لم يعين المصلّي لم يتعين ، وهو أن ينوي الظهر أو العصر، ولو نوى فرض الوقتِ أو فرض اليوم جاز. كذا في «الظهيرية»، ولو نوى الظهر وتلفظ بالعصر أجزأه ؛ لأنَّ المعتبر هو التعيين بالقلب. كذا في «القُنية». [٢] قوله : لا نية ؛ أي لا تشترط نيَّة عدد ركعات ما يصلي، فإنه إذا عين الصلاة تعينت الركعات بالضرورة، وكذا لا تشترط نية الاستقبال إلى الكعبة على الأصح. [٣]قوله : وللمقتدي ؛ أي يلزم للمقتدي نيَّةُ صلاة إمامه مع نية اقتدائه ؛ لأنه يلزمه الصحة والفساد من جهة إمامه، فلا بد من نيَّةِ متابعته، ولا تشترط نيَّة تعيين الإمام، ولو نوى الاقتداء بالإمام ويظن أنه زيد، فإذا هو عمرو صح. كذا في البحر (۲)
And for the obligatory [prayer], its specification is a condition, not the intention of the number of its rak'ahs; and for the follower, [there is required] intention of his prayer and of his following. [1] His saying: 'its specification' – because the obligatory is an additional description upon absolute prayer, and its time is a container suitable for both obligatory and supererogatory, so unless the worshipper specifies, it is not specified; that is, he intends Dhuhr or 'Asr. If he intends the obligatory of the time or the obligatory of the day, it is permissible. Thus in al-Zahiriyya. If he intended Dhuhr and uttered 'Asr, it suffices him, because consideration is for the specification of the heart. Thus in al-Qunyah. [2] His saying: 'not intention' – i.e., the intention of the number of rak'ahs of what he prays is not a condition, for when he specifies the prayer, the rak'ahs are necessarily specified. Likewise, the intention of facing the qibla is not a condition according to the most correct view. [3] His saying: 'and for the follower' – i.e., for the follower, the intention of his imam's prayer is necessary along with the intention of his following, because his prayer's validity and invalidity depend on his imam, so following must be intended. It is not a condition to specify the imam's identity; if he intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd, but then it is 'Amr, it is valid. Thus in al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn rulings concerning intention for obligatory prayers and for followers (muqtadūn). The base text states: 'For the obligatory [prayer], its specification is a condition, not the intention of the number of its rak'ahs; and for the follower, [there is required] intention of his prayer and of his following.' The commentary first explains 'specification' (ta'yīn): because the obligatory prayer has an additional description beyond absolute prayer, and its time is shared between obligatory and supererogatory, the worshipper must specify which prayer (e.g., Dhuhr or 'Asr). If one intends 'the obligatory of the time' or 'the obligatory of the day', it suffices. The true specification is in the heart; even if one verbally says a different prayer name but the heart specifies correctly, it is valid. Next, the phrase 'not intention of number of rak'ahs' means that one does not need to intend, e.g., 'four rak'ahs for Dhuhr'; specifying the prayer automatically determines the number. Similarly, intention of facing the qibla is not required as a separate intention. Finally, for the follower (muqtadī), the commentary says the follower must intend both the specific prayer (e.g., Fajr) and the act of following the imam, because the follower's prayer becomes valid or invalid through connection with the imam. However, it is not required to intend the imam's personal identity; if one intends to follow the imam thinking he is Zayd but it is 'Amr, the prayer is still valid.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtidāʼ): The follower's act of intending to follow the imam in prayer.
تعيين الإمام (ta'yīn al-imām): Specifying which imam (by name or identity) one is following.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer and the number of rak'ahs.
B) The prayer and the imam's name.
C) The prayer and the act of following.
D) Only the following, not the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower must intend both the specific prayer and the act of following; no need to specify the imam or the number of rak'ahs.

The Three Rulings on Intention (Niyyah) in Prayer
Commentary on intention requirements for the individual and follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings on intention in prayer and apply them to scenarios involving specification, rak'at, and following the imam.

Core Idea
Intention requires specifying the prayer, not its rak'at; follower must intend both prayer and following.

Intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of prayer. The Hanafi school details three specific rulings: the worshipper must specify which prayer they are performing, but need not intend the number of rak'at or the qibla. For a follower, the intention must include following the imam, without needing to name him. This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains these points with references to authoritative Hanafi works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
The passage presents three sub-rulings: (a) ta'yin (specification) of the prayer, (b) no need for intention of rak'at number or qibla, (c) the follower must intend his own prayer and his following of the imam.
These are the main takeaways from the commentary.
2
Understand the reasoning for ta'yin
The obligatory prayer has an additional attribute beyond absolute prayer; the same time permits both obligatory and supererogatory, so specification is necessary to distinguish.
Without specification, the intention is ambiguous and invalid.
3
Learn what is not required
Intention of the number of rak'at is unnecessary because specifying the prayer implicitly determines them. Similarly, intending the qibla is not required according to the most correct view.
This leniency simplifies the intention.
4
Apply the ruling for the follower
The follower must intend both his own prayer and his following of the imam, as validity depends on the imam. He need not specify the imam by name; even if mistaken about the imam's identity, the prayer is valid.
This applies even if the follower does not know the imam's name.
5
Note the heart's criterion
The heart's intention is decisive. If one intends in the heart correctly but errs verbally, the prayer remains valid.
This is a key Hanafi principle.

Book of Prayer: Conditions of Prayer. His specification: not intention of number of its rak'at. And for the follower, intention of his prayer and his following him. (1) His saying: his specification; because the obligatory prayer is an additional attribute on absolute prayer, and its time is a container suitable for both obligatory and supererogatory, so as long as the worshipper does not specify, it is not specified. It is that he intends Zuhr or 'Asr. If he intends 'the obligatory of the time' or 'the obligatory of the day', it is permissible. Likewise in 'al-Zahiriyyah'. If he intends Zuhr but utters 'Asr, it suffices him because the criterion is specification by the heart. Likewise in 'al-Qunyah'. Likewise, intention of facing the Ka'bah is not required according to the most correct. His saying: and for the follower; i.e., the follower must intend his imam's prayer along with intention of following him, because for him correctness and invalidity depend on his imam, so intention of following him is necessary. Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn from Al-Wiqayah regarding the conditions of intention (niyyah) in prayer. The author explains three sub-rulings: First, the requirement of ta'yin (specification) of the prayer—the worshipper must intend the specific prayer (e.g., Zuhr or 'Asr), not merely an absolute prayer. Intending 'the obligatory of the time' or 'the obligatory of the day' suffices. The heart's intention is decisive; verbal expression contrary to it does not affect validity. Second, intention of the number of rak'at is not required; specifying the prayer implicitly determines the rak'at. Similarly, intention of facing the qibla is not required according to the most correct view. Third, for a follower (muqtadi), he must intend both his own prayer and his following of the imam, because his prayer's validity depends on the imam's prayer. He need not specify the imam by name; if he intends a specific person but is mistaken, the prayer is still valid. These rulings are attributed to authoritative Hanafi works such as al-Zahiriyyah, al-Qunyah, and al-Bahr.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specification of which prayer is being performed (e.g., Zuhr or 'Asr).
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform a specific act of worship.
المقتدي (al-muqtadī): The person praying behind an imam.

The Opening Takbir: A Condition, Not a Pillar
Defining the first obligatory act: the opening takbir and its legal nature as a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a condition (shart) and a pillar (rukn) in the Hanafi school and explain why the opening takbir is classified as a condition.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn).

Prayer begins with a boundary – the opening takbir (tahrimah). But what is its legal nature? In this passage, the commentator explains why the Hanafi school deliberately chose the word 'fard' (not 'rukn') for the opening takbir. The key lies in the distinction between a condition, which is external to the act's essence, and a pillar, which is internal. You will learn the proof from the hadith and how this classification impacts the validity of prayer. This lesson clarifies a foundational usul point that affects how we understand obligations in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal classification
Notice that the author of the matn says 'farduha' (its obligatory act) and not 'rukn' (pillar). The commentary justifies this choice by stating that the opening takbir is a condition (shart) in the Hanafi school. Read the text: 'لم يقل: ركنها؛ لتدخل التحريمة، فإنّها شرط عندنا لا ركن.' (He did not say: its pillar, to include the takbirat al-ihram, for it is a condition according to us, not a pillar.)
This is the central claim of the passage.
2
Differentiate between shart and rukn
The commentary provides a definition: the condition (shart) is external to the reality of the thing, while the pillar (rukn) is internal. Understand this distinction: a condition is a prerequisite for the act's validity but not part of its essence, whereas a pillar is an integral component whose omission invalidates the act. The opening takbir is the threshold that makes worldly actions unlawful (tahrim) – it is the entry point, not a component of the prayer itself.
This distinction is a hallmark of Hanafi usul al-fiqh.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'مفتاح الصلاة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم' (The key to prayer is purification; its tahrimah is takbir; its tahlil is taslim) is cited. The word 'tahrimuha' (its tahrimah) directly links the takbir to the act of making things unlawful. This shows that the takbir is the boundary that separates the state of prayer from everyday life, supporting its classification as a condition.
The hadith is transmitted by al-Tirmidhi and others; it is mashhur (well-known).
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The commentary implies that other schools (e.g., Shafi'is) consider the opening takbir a pillar (rukn). Recognize that this difference stems from varying usul principles. For Hanafis, the condition is external; for Shafi'is, any integral action that defines the act is a rukn. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for comparative fiqh.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is mainly theoretical, but it affects rulings on forgetfulness (sahu) and compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صفة الصلاة
(فرضها : التحريمة )
قوله: باب صفة الصلاة؛ هو بكسر الصاد، إما مصدر كما في «صحاح الجوهري»: «وصف الشيء وصفاً وصفةً، فالهاء عوض عن الواو: كالعِظة والوعظ، والوعد والعِدة». انتهى. وإما عبارة عن المعنى القائم بذاتِ الموصوف بخلاف الوصف، فإنّه عبارة عن كلام الواصف، كما في «النهاية». والمراد بها إما الأمور المذكورة في هذا الباب من واجبات الصلاة وفرائضها وسننها وآدابها، وحينئذ فالإضافة إلى الصلاة من قبيل إضافة الجزء إلى الكل، وإمّا الكيفية، وحينئذ فالمضاف محذوف، والمعنى هذا باب في بيان كيفية إجزاء الصلاة، وإما الهيئة الحاصلة بتركيب بعض أجزائها ببعض.
قوله: فرضها؛ لم يقل: ركنها؛ لتدخل التحريمة، فإنّها شرط عندنا لا ركن، والفرق بينهما بعد اشتراكهما في توقف الشيء عليهما أن الشرط يكون خارجاً عن حقيقة الشيء، والركن يكون داخلاً فيها. والمراد بالفرض ما لزم فعله بدليل قطعي أعم من أن يكون ركناً أو شرطاً، فيكفرُ جاحده ويستحق تاركه العقاب.
قوله: التحريمة؛ سمّى التكبير ونحوه ما يفتتح به الصلاة تحريمة؛ لأنه يحرم على المصلّي ما ليس من جنس الصلاة، قال النبي : مفتاح الصلاة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم» () ، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره، والدليل على افتراض التكبير حديث: «مفتاح الصلاة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم».
Chapter: Description of Prayer. (Its obligatory: the takbirat al-ihram). His saying: Chapter of the description of prayer; it is with a kasra on the sad, either a verbal noun as in 'Sihah al-Jawhari': 'He described something, description and quality, the ha' is a substitute for the waw: like al-'idha (exhortation) and al-wa'z (preaching), al-wa'd (promise) and al-'iddah (number).' End. Or it is an expression for the meaning subsisting in the essence of the described, unlike al-wasf, which is an expression of the describer's speech, as in 'al-Nihayah'. What is intended by it is either the matters mentioned in this chapter from the obligatory acts, fara'id, sunan, and etiquettes of prayer; in that case the idafa to prayer is from the category of adding a part to the whole. Or it is the modality, in which case the mudaf is omitted, and the meaning is: this is a chapter explaining the modality of performing prayer. Or it is the state resulting from the composition of some of its parts with others. His saying: its obligatory; he did not say: its pillar, to include the takbirat al-ihram, for it is a condition according to us, not a pillar. The difference between them, despite their commonality in that something depends on them, is that the condition is external to the reality of the thing, while the pillar is internal to it. And by 'fard' is meant what is necessary to do by a definitive proof, whether it is a pillar or a condition. Thus, the denier of it becomes an unbeliever, and the abandoner deserves punishment. His saying: tahrimah; he named the takbir and similar things with which prayer is opened 'tahrimah' because it makes unlawful for the worshipper what is not of the type of prayer. The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The key to prayer is purification; its tahrimah is takbir; its tahlil is taslim.' Narrated by al-Tirmidhi and others. The proof for the obligation of the takbir is the hadith: 'The key to prayer is purification; its tahrimah is takbir; its tahlil is taslim.'
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on the description of prayer (sifat al-salah) in the commentary. The author first explains the meaning of 'sifah' (description) linguistically and terminologically, clarifying that it can refer to the attributes of prayer mentioned in this chapter or the modality of performing it. Then, the commentary focuses on the first obligatory act: the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir). The author justifies why the matn used 'fard' (obligatory) instead of 'rukn' (pillar): to include the takbirat al-ihram, which in the Hanafi school is considered a condition (shart) of prayer, not a pillar. The distinction is that a condition is external to the essence of the act, while a pillar is internal. The term 'fard' here encompasses both pillars and conditions, as it is defined by what is required by a definitive proof. Denying it leads to disbelief, and abandoning it incurs punishment. The linguistic reason for calling it 'tahrimah' is that it makes unlawful (yuharrim) things outside the prayer. The proof for its obligation is the authentic hadith: 'The key to prayer is purification; its tahrimah is takbir; its tahlil is taslim.' This hadith clearly makes takbir a condition for prayer to be valid, as the tahrimah is the opening act that transitions from non-prayer to prayer.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The opening takbir that makes worldly things unlawful for the one in prayer.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An act required by a definitive proof, encompassing both pillars and conditions.
الشرط (al-sharṭ): Something external to the reality of an act upon which its validity depends.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of the act's essence; its omission invalidates the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Pillar (rukn) of prayer
B) Condition (shart) of prayer
C) Sunnah of prayer
D) Recommended act (mustahabb)

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is a condition (shart) for prayer, not a pillar (rukn), based on the hadith 'tahrimuha al-takbir' and the Hanafi usul distinction that conditions are external to the act's essence.

The Opening Takbir: A Condition, Not a Pillar
Explaining why the author used 'fard' not 'rukn' for the tahrimah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the opening takbir is a condition (shart) of prayer and obligatory (fard) by definitive proof, and distinguish it from a pillar (rukn) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is a condition external to prayer's essence; its omission invalidates entry, not the internal structure.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the author of Al-Wiqayah used the term 'fard' (obligation) for the opening takbir instead of 'rukn' (pillar). This choice reflects a key Hanafi principle: the tahrimah is a condition (shart), not an integral part of prayer. Understanding this distinction has real consequences for how we view the act of beginning prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the opening takbir (tahrimah). Its ruling is fard (obligatory) by definitive proof. Note that the author says 'fard' not 'rukn'.
fard here includes both conditions and pillars.
2
Distinguish condition (shart) from pillar (rukn)
A condition is external to the essence of the act; the act cannot begin without it. A pillar is internal; its omission invalidates the act completely. The tahrimah is a condition because it is the entry prohibition, not an ongoing part of prayer.
For example, wudu is a condition for prayer, but not a pillar within it.
3
Locate the proof for obligation
The Quran (74:3) commands magnification, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently began prayer with takbir. The hadith 'its prohibition is the takbir' further shows its obligatory nature.
The dalil is both Quran and sunnah, giving it qat'i thubut.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is consider the opening takbir a pillar (rukn). This affects the ruling: for Shafi'is, if one forgets it, the entire prayer is invalid; for Hanafis, the prayer never began, requiring a fresh start.
Both schools agree it is obligatory, but the classification matters for details.
