(فرضها : التحريمة)
[١] قوله : باب صفة الصلاة ؛ هو بكسر الصاد، إما مصدر كما في «صحاح الجوهري»: «وصف الشيء وصفاً وصفةً ، فالهاء عوض عن الواو : كالعِظة والوعظ ، والوعد والعِدة». انتهى. وإما عبارة عن المعنى القائم بذاتِ الموصوف بخلاف الوصف، فإنّه عبارة عن كلام الواصف، كما في «النهاية». والمراد بها إما الأمور المذكورة في هذا الباب من واجبات الصلاة وفرائضها وسننها وآدابها ، وحينئذ فالإضافة إلى الصلاة من قبيل إضافة الجزء إلى الكل، وإمّا الكيفية، وحينئذ فالمضاف محذوف، والمعنى هذا باب في بيان كيفية إجزاء الصلاة، وإما الهيئة الحاصلة بتركيب بعض أجزائها ببعض.
[٢]قوله : فرضها ؛ لم يقل : ركنها ؛ لتدخل التحريمة، فإنّها شرط عندنا لا ركن، والفرق بينهما بعد اشتراكهما في توقف الشيء عليهما أن الشرط يكون خارجاً عن حقيقة الشيء، والركن يكون داخلاً فيها. والمراد بالفرض ما لزم فعله بدليل قطعي أعم من أن يكون ركناً أو شرطاً، فيكفرُ جاحده ويستحق تاركه العقاب.
[٣] قوله : التحريمة ؛ سمّى التكبير ونحوه ما يفتتح به الصلاة تحريمة ؛ لأنه يحرم على المصلّي ما ليس من جنس الصلاة، قال النبي : مفتاح الصلاة الطهور وتحريمها التكبير وتحليلها التسليم» () ، أخرجه الترمذي وغيره، والدليل على افتراض التحريمة قوله : وَرَبِّكَ فَكَبِّرْ (١) ، ومواظبة النبي على ذلك.
[١] قوله : وهي قوله : الله اكبر ؛ هذا هو المنقول عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قولاً وتعليماً وفعلاً على ما هو مخرج في «معجم الطبراني»، و«صحیح ابن خزيمة»، و«سنن ابن حبّان» وغيرها. ومن ثم صرحوا بأن اختيار خصوص هذا اللفظ سنة مؤكدة، فلو شرع بفارسية أو بالتسبيح أو التحميد أو نحو ذلك كره (4) ، صرَّح به في «الذخيرة» و«الظهيرية» وغيرها. [٢] قوله : وما يقوم مقامه ؛ أي كل ما يدلّ على التعظيم الخالص غير المشوب بالدعاء وغيره ؛ وذلك لأن قوله وال : ﴿ وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى ) ، وقوله : وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ، إنما يدل على وجوب ما يدلّ على التعظيم ، فإنّ التكبير هو التعظيم، ولا دلالة فيه على خصوص لفظ : «أكبر»، حتى يكون فرضاً، غاية ما في الباب أنّ
Chapter: Description of Prayer
(Its obligation: the Tahrimah)
[1] His saying: 'Chapter: Description of Prayer' - it is with kasra on the sad, either a verbal noun as in Sihah al-Jawhari: 'He described a thing, description and quality, so the ha' substitutes for the waw: like 'izza and wa'z, wa'd and 'idda.' End. Or it is an expression for the meaning subsisting in the essence of the described, unlike 'description' (wasf) which is an expression for the speech of the describer, as in al-Nihayah. What is meant by it is either the matters mentioned in this chapter from the obligatory acts (wajibat) of prayer, its obligations (fara'id), its sunan, and its etiquettes; in that case the addition to prayer is of the type of adding a part to the whole. Or it means the modality (kayfiyyah); in that case the added element is omitted, and the meaning is: 'This is a chapter explaining the modality of performing the prayer.' Or it means the form (hay'ah) resulting from the composition of some of its parts with others.
[2] His saying: 'Its obligation' - he did not say: 'its pillar' (rukn) in order to include the Tahrimah, for it is a condition (shart) according to us, not a pillar. The difference between them after their commonality in the dependence of something on them is that the condition is external to the reality of the thing, while the pillar is internal to it. And what is meant by 'obligation' (fard) is that whose performance is necessitated by a definitive proof, whether it is a pillar or a condition; so the denier of it becomes an unbeliever, and the abandoner deserves punishment.
[3] His saying: 'the Tahrimah' - the takbir and similar things with which prayer is opened are called 'Tahrimah' because it prohibits (yuharrim) upon the praying person what is not of the type of prayer. The Prophet said: 'The key to prayer is purification, its prohibition is the takbir, and its release is the taslim' - narrated by al-Tirmidhi and others. The proof for the obligatoriness of the Tahrimah is His saying: 'And magnify your Lord' (74:3), and the Prophet's continuous practice upon that.
[1] His saying: 'And it is his saying: Allahu Akbar' - this is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in words, teaching, and action, as recorded in Mu'jam al-Tabarani, Sahih Ibn Khuzaymah, Sunan Ibn Hibban, and others. For this reason they explicitly stated that choosing this specific wording is an emphasized sunnah. So if one begins with Persian (Farisiyyah) or with tasbih, tahmid, or something like that, it is disliked (makruh) - explicitly stated in al-Dhakhirah, al-Zahiriyyah, and others.
[2] His saying: 'and what stands in its place' - i.e., everything that indicates pure magnification (ta'zim) unmixed with supplication (du'a) and other things. This is because His saying: 'and he remembered the name of his Lord, so he prayed' (87:15) and His saying: 'And magnify your Lord' (74:3) only indicate the obligation of what indicates magnification. Indeed, takbir is magnification, and there is no indication in it for the specific wording 'Akbar' such that it would be obligatory. At most, what is in the matter is that...
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is from a commentary (sharh) on Al-Wiqayah, explaining the beginning of the chapter on the description of prayer. The author first defines the term 'sifah' (description) and explains what is meant by 'Chapter on the Description of Prayer'—whether it refers to the various rulings (obligations, sunan, etc.), the modality of prayer, or the composite form. Then he turns to the phrase 'Its obligation: the Tahrimah.' He notes that the author deliberately used 'fard' (obligation) instead of 'rukn' (pillar) because the Tahrimah is a condition (shart) according to the Hanafi school, not an integral part (rukn). The distinction is that a condition is external to the essence of the act, while a pillar is internal. 'Fard' here means that which is necessitated by a definitive proof (dalil qat'i)—whether it is a condition or a pillar—so that denying it amounts to disbelief. Then he explains why the opening takbir is called 'Tahrimah': it prohibits the worshipper from engaging in anything not part of the prayer. The evidence for its obligation is the Quranic verse 'And magnify your Lord' (74:3) and the Prophet's continuous practice. The commentator then discusses the wording of the takbir. While the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the transmitted form and choosing it is an emphasized sunnah, other wordings in Persian or other forms of magnification (like subhanallah or alhamdulillah) are considered disliked (makruh) but not invalid. The proof from the Quran is general, commanding magnification (takbir), which does not specify a particular wording. Therefore, any expression that conveys pure magnification, without supplication, suffices for the obligation, though the sunnah is to use 'Allahu Akbar'.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir that initiates prayer, called tahrimah because it prohibits (yuharrim) actions not part of prayer.
الفرض (al-fard): That which is obligatory by a definitive proof (dalil qat'i); includes both pillars and conditions in this context.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of an act that lies within its essence; its omission invalidates the act.
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' or any expression of magnification; the act of declaring Allah's greatness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, why did the author of Al-Wiqayah use the word 'fard' instead of 'rukn' for the opening takbir?
A) To indicate that the takbir is a sunnah, not fard.
B) To include the takbir as a condition (shart), which is not a pillar.
C) To emphasize that the takbir is a pillar of prayer.
D) To show that the takbir is optional.

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir is a fard condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn), and its omission prevents the prayer from beginning.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
7 min
The Wording of the Opening Takbir: Obligation of Magnification, Sunnah of 'Allahu Akbar'
Expanding on the ruling for the wording of the opening takbir, including the status of non-Arabic phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that the obligation of the opening takbir is fulfilled by any expression of pure magnification, and that the specific Arabic wording 'Allahu Akbar' is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).

Core Idea
The Quran commands magnification generically; 'Allahu Akbar' is the prophetic sunnah, not the only valid wording.

After establishing the obligation of the opening takbir, the commentator turns to its wording. While 'Allahu Akbar' is the transmitted form and is considered an emphasized sunnah, the Quranic proofs for magnification are general. This opens the door for using other expressions of pure magnification, though doing so when one can speak Arabic is disliked (makruh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation: magnification (takbir), not a specific phrase
The Quran (74:3, 87:15) commands magnification in absolute terms. Therefore, the fard is to perform an act of magnification, not to utter a particular set of words.
This is the key to understanding the dispute.
2
Recognize the transmitted wording as sunnah
The Prophet (peace be upon him) consistently used 'Allahu Akbar' in word and teaching. This makes that wording sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
Choosing it earns reward; omitting it without excuse may be sinful if it becomes a habit.
3
Learn the ruling for other wordings
If one uses Persian (or other languages) or expressions like 'Subhanallah' or 'Alhamdulillah' that convey pure magnification, the obligation is fulfilled, but it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because it abandons the sunnah.
The commentary cites Al-Dhakhirah and Al-Zahiriyyah for this ruling.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab dispute
Some scholars (likely Shafi'is) require the exact Arabic wording. They argue that the hadith and practice specify it. The Hanafi response is that the proofs are general and specification requires a strong proof, which is lacking.
The practical difference: Hanafis allow other languages; opponents do not.

Source Text

The Ruling on the Wording of Takbir al-Ihram
Expands on takbir wording and disputes among imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on the required wording for takbir al-ihram and explain the basis of the dispute with Abu Yusuf, al-Shafi'i, and Malik.

Core Idea
For takbir al-ihram, the fard is any pure glorification; the specific 'Allahu Akbar' is sunnah, not obligatory.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a crucial distinction regarding the opening takbir. While Muslims commonly associate the phrase 'Allahu Akbar' with entering prayer, the Hanafi school holds that the obligatory element is the act of glorification itself, not the specific Arabic wording. By examining the Quranic evidence and the views of other imams, we will understand why the Hanafi position allows flexibility and what the practical limits are.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: any expression of pure glorification (ta'dhim) suffices for takbir al-ihram. The specific wording 'Allahu Akbar' is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada), not fard.
This is the mufta bihi (al-mukhtar) according to the author.
2
Identify the opponents and their views
Abu Yusuf restricts validity to four specific Arabic phrases: 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allahu al-Akbar', 'Allahu Kabir', 'Allahu al-Kabir'. Al-Shafi'i allows only the first two, and Imam Malik allows only 'Allahu Akbar'. Note the progression of restriction.
Each opponent relies on ahad hadith about the Prophet's practice.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponents cite the Prophet's constant practice of saying 'Allahu Akbar' as evidence that this specific wording is obligatory. Their proofs are ahad hadith transmitted in various hadith collections.
These hadith are authentic but not mutawatir.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that the Quranic verses (87:15 and 74:3) command glorification ('takbir') in absolute terms without specifying wording. Ahad hadith cannot restrict the general command of the Quran. Thus, the specific wording is sunnah, not fard.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amm (the general) remains binding unless specified by a qat'i dalil.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the Hanafi mufta bihi, a person may begin prayer with phrases like 'Allahu Ajal' (Allah is more majestic) or even Persian equivalents (though disliked), and the prayer is valid. In the other views, such phrases would invalidate the prayer.
This eases the prayer for non-Arabic speakers or those with speech difficulties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[٢] قوله : وما يقوم مقامه ; أي كل ما يدلّ على التعظيم الخالص غير المشوب بالدعاء وغيره ; وذلك لأن قوله وال : ﴿ وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ فَصَلَّى ) ، وقوله : وَرَبَّكَ فكير، إنما يدل على وجوب ما يدلّ على التعظيم ، فإنّ التكبير هو التعظيم، ولا دلالة فيه على خصوص لفظ : «أكبر»، حتى يكون فرضاً، غاية ما في الباب أنّ خصوص هذا اللفظ يكون سنة (۳) ، فالفرضُ مطلقُ ما يدل على التعظيم، فلو شرع بقوله : الله أجلّ أو أعظم كفى ذلك ، ولو شرع باللهم اغفر لي لم يجز ) ، هذا كله عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ، وهو المختار. وعند أبي يوسف يجوز بأربعة ألفاظ الله أكبر، والله الأكبر، والله كبير، والله الكبير لا بغيرها، وعند الشافعي باللفظين الأولين فقط ، وعند مالك بالأوّل فقط ، ولكل وجهة هو موليها.

بل ظاهر الآية والأحاديث مطلق، لا يفيد إلا اشتراط الذكر المطلق، والأحاديث الواردة في هذا الباب القولية والفعلية لا تدل على اختصاص التكبير بالعربي ، بحيث لا يجزئ غير العربي ، بل غاية ما يثبت منها أن النبي لا لا لا لا اكتفى عليه ، ورغب غيره إليه ، وهو إنما يثبت الوجوب أو السنية، لا أنه لا يجزئ التكبير بالفارسية، وإن كانت الأحاديث دالة على اختصاصه بالعربي اختصاصا بالغا إلى حد الاشتراط، فالآية معراة عن هذا الاشتراط ، ولا تصلح أخبار الآحاد ناسخة لحكم الكتاب، ولا تقيدة لإطلاق ما في الباب». Book of Prayer / Description of Prayer. It is his saying: Allahu Akbar, and what stands in its place. Tahrima: His saying [in Quran]: 'And your Lord magnify' (74:3), and the Prophet's constancy in that. [1] His saying: 'It is his saying: Allahu Akbar'; this is what is transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, in word, teaching, and deed, as is found in the Mu'jam al-Tabarani, Sahih Ibn Khuzayma, Sunan Ibn Hibban, and others. (4) Hence they declared that choosing this specific wording is a confirmed sunnah; so if one begins with Persian (4) or with tasbih or tahmid or the like, it is disliked (karaha), as stated in al-Dhakhira, al-Zahiriya, and others. [2] His saying: 'and what stands in its place'; meaning everything that indicates pure glorification unmixed with supplication and other things. That is because His saying: 'and he mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' (87:15), and His saying: 'and your Lord magnify' (74:3) only indicate the obligation of what indicates glorification. Indeed, takbir is glorification, and there is no indication in them of the specific wording 'Akbar' such that it would be fard. At most, this specific wording is sunnah (3). So the fard is any expression indicating glorification. So if one begins with 'Allahu Ajal' or 'Allahu A'dham', that suffices. And if one begins with 'Allahumma ighfir li', it is not valid. This is all according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and it is the chosen position. According to Abu Yusuf, it is valid with four wordings: Allahu Akbar, Allahu al-Akbar, Allahu Kabir, Allahu al-Kabir, and not with others. According to al-Shafi'i, only the first two wordings. According to Malik, only the first. And each has a direction towards which he turns.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This is an expansion (sharh) on the original matn of al-Wiqaya concerning the wording of takbir al-ihram (the opening takbir of prayer). The author first confirms that the specific phrase 'Allahu Akbar' is the transmitted sunnah from the Prophet, based on multiple hadith sources. However, the author clarifies that the obligatory element (fard) is any expression that conveys pure glorification (ta'dhim) of Allah, unmixed with supplication. This is derived from the Quranic verses 'and he mentioned the name of his Lord and prayed' (al-A'la 87:15) and 'and your Lord magnify' (al-Muddaththir 74:3), which indicate the obligation of glorification without specifying a particular wording. Therefore, the fard is absolute glorification, while the specific wording 'Allahu Akbar' is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkada). The author then presents the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that any expression of pure glorification suffices, such as 'Allahu Ajal' (Allah is more majestic) or 'Allahu A'dham' (Allah is greater), whereas words mixed with supplication like 'Allahumma ighfir li' (O Allah, forgive me) are invalid because they are not pure glorification. Abu Yusuf restricts validity to four specific Arabic phrases: 'Allahu Akbar', 'Allahu al-Akbar', 'Allahu Kabir', and 'Allahu al-Kabir'. The author declares Abu Hanifa's view as the chosen position (al-mukhtar). The passage also records the positions of other schools: al-Shafi'i allows only the first two, and Imam Malik only the first. The long footnote by al-Laknawi reinforces the Hanafi position by arguing that no decisive proof requires Arabic, and the Quranic verse is absolute, so Persian or any language indicating glorification might be valid, though the specific Arabic wording is recommended.

Key Terms
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer, which makes what was previously permissible (e.g., eating, speaking) forbidden. It is synonymous with takbirat al-ihram.
التكبير (al-takbir): Any expression that magnifies Allah; here it specifically refers to the opening takbir of prayer. The author distinguishes between the specific wording 'Allahu Akbar' and the general concept of glorification.
التعظيم (al-ta'dhim): Glorification or magnification of Allah, free from any admixture of supplication. It is the essential element in takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-mukhtar), which of the following expressions is NOT valid for takbir al-ihram?
A) الله أكبر (Allahu Akbar)
B) الله أجل (Allahu Ajal)
C) اللهم اغفر لي (Allahumma ighfir li)
D) الله كبير (Allahu Kabir)

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi relied-upon view, the opening takbir requires any expression of pure glorification; 'Allahu Akbar' is the sunnah but not obligatory.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Takbir al-Ihram: Condition or Pillar? The Hanafi View and Its Practical Consequence
Debate on takbir al-ihram: condition or pillar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers takbir al-ihram a condition (shart) rather than a pillar (rukn), and state the practical consequence of this view for linking prayers.

Core Idea
Takbir al-ihram is a condition, not a pillar: one takbir can validly begin multiple prayers in sequence, though it is makruh.

This lesson examines the debate over the legal nature of takbir al-ihram (tahrimah). The Hanafi school holds that it is a condition (shart) for the prayer, not a pillar (rukn). This classification has a direct practical consequence: it is permissible (though disliked) to begin a nafl prayer immediately after a fard prayer without reciting a new takbir. The proof is drawn from the Quranic verse in Surat al-A'la. Let's unpack the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of takbir al-ihram in the Hanafi school
The text states ‘wa huwa shartun ‘indana’ — it is a condition with us. Understand that condition (shart) is external to the essence of the prayer but necessary for its validity.
Hanafi usul: shart is separate from rukn; a single shart can serve multiple acts.
2
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) — linking prayers
If one prays a fard and then immediately stands for a nafl without salam and without a new takbir, it is valid in the Hanafi school because the same takbir (condition) can serve both prayers.
The text also notes this is valid but disliked (karaha).
3
Examine the Hanafi proof from the Quran
The verse ‘fa salla’ (so he prayed) uses the letter ‘fa’ indicating sequence. This shows that the mention of Allah’s name (takbir) precedes and is separate from the prayer, i.e., a condition.
Proof is from al-A'la 87:14-15.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i considers takbir al-ihram a rukn (pillar). Consequently, each prayer must have its own takbir; linking would be invalid because a pillar cannot be shared.
This difference leads to different rulings in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[١] قوله : وهو شرط عندنا ; ثمرةُ الخلافِ تظهر في بناء الصلاة بعضها على بعض، فمن صلى فرضاً ثم قام إلى النفل من غير السلام عن الأول، ومن غير التحريمة المبتدأة للنفل يجوز ذلك عندنا ; لأنّ التحريمة شرط ، ويمكن أن تتأدى مشروطات بشرط واحد كالطهارة الواحدة يصلّي بها الصلوات الكثيرة. (٤) وعند الشافعي له لا يجوز بناءً على أنّ التحريمة ركن، فلا يمكن أن يتأدى صلاة بركن صلاة أخرى، والجواز عندنا عبارة عن الإجزاء، ولا نجاة عن لزوم الكراهة. كذا في «الدر المختار، وحواشيه [۲] قوله : لقوله تعالى ; هذا دليل لكون التحريمة شرطاً لا ركناً، وحاصله أنَّ الله قد عطف الصلاة على ذكر اسمه بحرف الفاء الدالة على التعقيب حيث قال : قد أَفْلَحَ مَن تَزَكَّى وَذَكَرَ اسْمَ رَبِّهِ، فَصَلَّى (0) (۱) من سورة الأعلى، الآية (١٥).
[1] His saying: 'And it is a condition with us'; the practical consequence of the dispute appears in connecting one prayer to another. So if one prays a fard prayer, then stands to pray a nafl without making the salam from the first and without a new beginning tahrimah for the nafl, that is permissible with us, because the tahrimah is a condition, and it is possible for multiple conditioned things to be fulfilled by one condition, just as with one purification one can perform many prayers. (4) With al-Shafi'i, it is not permissible based on the fact that the tahrimah is a pillar, so it is not possible for a prayer to be performed with the pillar of another prayer. And what we call permissibility is a matter of validity, but there is no escape from the necessity of dislike (karaha). This is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its glosses. [2] His saying: 'Because of His saying [the Quran]'; this is the proof that the tahrimah is a condition not a pillar. Its summary is that Allah has connected prayer to the mention of His name with the letter fa, which indicates sequence, where He said: 'Successful is he who purifies himself and mentions the name of his Lord and prays' (al-A'la 87:14-15).
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the takbir al-ihram (tahrimah) by addressing its legal nature: is it a condition (shart) for the prayer or a pillar (rukn)? The matn states 'it is a condition with us' (i.e., in the Hanafi school). The commentator explains the practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute: if one prays a fard prayer and then immediately stands to pray a nafl without saying the salam from the first prayer and without a new tahrimah for the nafl, it is permissible in the Hanafi school because the tahrimah is a condition, and multiple prayers can be fulfilled by a single condition, just as one purification (wudu) can serve multiple prayers. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, this is not permissible because he considers the tahrimah a pillar; each prayer must have its own pillar. However, the commentator notes that even though it is permissible in the Hanafi school, it is still disliked (makruh). The proof for the Hanafi view is the Quranic verse from Surat al-A'la (87:14-15) where prayer is connected to the mention of Allah's name with the letter 'fa' (then), indicating sequence, which suggests that the mention of the name (i.e., the takbir) is a preparatory condition before the prayer, not an integral part of the prayer itself. Thus, the tahrimah is a condition, not a pillar.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): A condition that is external to the prayer but necessary for its validity; the tahrimah is a shart because it is not part of the prayer's essence but its beginning.
الركن (al-rukn): A pillar or integral part of the prayer; the commentator states that according to Shafi'i, the tahrimah is a rukn, meaning it must be present within each prayer.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; here it refers to the permissibility of linking prayers without a new takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of considering takbir al-ihram a condition rather than a pillar?
A) One cannot pray any prayer without it
B) It is permissible to pray a nafl immediately after a fard without a new takbir, though disliked
C) It is invalid to pray more than one prayer with a single takbir
D) The takbir must be said in Arabic only

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, takbir al-ihram is a condition, not a pillar; one condition can serve multiple prayers in sequence, but doing so is makruh.
